O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, dear children, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine, its fulfillment, and have finished it through its explanations and statements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with this treatise, which is the beginning of the work of hands, namely "surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work of hands is treated differently in our region and is strange to all, the science is lost and cut off, and there is nothing left from its roots except for small descriptions in books by the ancients about what the hands have done.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed, and knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will revive this treatise by organizing it according to the order of exposition and explanation, and also by providing an abridged version; I will bring together the forms of cautery instruments and other tools used in the work, with adjustments to their declaration and preparation as needed.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has languished.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who wishes to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, must know the judgment of the members, their shapes and connections, and the separations of parts; he should have knowledge of bones, nerves, blood vessels, and the number of organs, and understand the functions of moving and resting veins.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And Hippocrates says that the name without deeds is empty, and the deed without knowledge is useless; especially in the art of healing.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that he who is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, risks error and misleads people; as I have often seen with many of those who engage in this science without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a most wondrous sight, where a woman had an abscess on her neck, and the arteries were affected; so much blood issued forth that the woman died in her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I witnessed another marvel where a stone was removed from an old man's bladder; the stone was large; it tore off a piece of the bladder, and the man bled internally for three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him; I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and if it were not removed, he would surely die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another wonder, which was the cure of a duke from our land who had broken his leg, and with the break came a wound; the curious ones, full of ignorance, held the break on the wound as if by strong ropes, leaving no space for the wound to heal, and left it like that until the end; and he commanded that he should not loosen it; and so he waited until the leg was completely swollen and painful and came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	They called me to come to him, and I hurried to loosen the leg; and when I heard it dislocate, there was no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way of corruption was already confirmed in the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I also saw another wonder: the abscess became worse, and then it was inflamed due to the evil nature of its mastery.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the chancre, when it is free of melancholic humor, one should not use iron to treat it unless it is in a part that can be entirely removed, so as to eliminate what is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear child, it is necessary for you to know that the art of healing is divided into two parts: that is to say, the work of hands in various arrangements; and I will show in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, hold fast to these words, so that the wicked do not speak ill of you. When you take up your weapons in battle, begin with your sick and weak patients gently and resolutely, using the best method, so that through God's grace you may be saved and joyful. Cast away all diseases full of sorrow and give health to those who suffer. Leave behind what makes you doubt and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the other, filled with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in none of his warnings: "Do not take ill health too seriously, lest you be called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cautery and ague medicine cautery, and it is ordered from the head down to the feet; and about the shapes of instruments, and the tools for cautery, and everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and poultices and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is ordered and includes the shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar conditions; it ordains the use of hot compresses from the neck down to the feet, and the shapes of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, remembering the work, it is necessary that I mention the quality of the aid and the harm of each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and the harm caused are the most extensive discourse and subtle science, containing secret answers; on these topics, many wise ones have spoken and agreed among themselves; however, their words are sufficient for me, as I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally to every condition where it has matter, whether the conditions: that is to say, the hot condition with matter, and the dry condition without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the hot and dry condition, matter combines, and some devise that cautery is great help, while others say the opposite: that cautery is of no use for illnesses arising from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For natural fire is hot, and should not be treated with heat for hot illnesses by either heat or dryness, and he who says the contrary states that cautery provides great help to hot and dry conditions that affect humans' bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and its moisture with the heat of fire, you perceive that the flesh is fresh.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, no one should attempt it unless they have tested it themselves, and know by long experience the chapter of cautery, and the diversity of human complexes, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the remedies and the passage of time; for other complexes we only have fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all agreed and were convinced about the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, child, that cautery joins fire, which is a secret of healing, and indeed it is much gentler than burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and brings no harm but to the member that is afflicted, and does not affect any other member.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines travel from one member to another by moving away, and they bring diseases of sorrow without healing; and perhaps the fire does not harm the patient because of its high value and the goodness of its substance, unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And because I have found it by experience and through the long service and study that I have put into this art, and it is about the truth of things; and therefore I excuse myself for the length of my speech, for I do not like to deprive you of the secret hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it heals the diseases of the body, as the philosopher says by demonstrating; consider it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know this, my son, that there is agreement among them as to when cauterization should be performed and the appropriate tools chosen.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate in all seasons, because the pain and harm caused by the disease are removed with the help of cauterization; especially when cauterization is for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait until a greater evil comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear child, as they do who are ignorant; for to the illness that is healed by cautery there is no relapse; and thus it must be done; but not as they care for it, because cauterization is only a medicine that alters the complexion, dries up the humors that cause pain, and works more quickly than other medicines because of the worthiness of its effect and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And one of its capabilities is that illness comes according to the complexion and state of the patient and the nature of the disease, and excesses accumulate within it through the acquisition of foods and similar things; except for cauterization applied where there is little excess and moisture, as in cutting away flesh or similar conditions that cause pain, and such pains do not recur; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last of medicine, and that's true; but they do not believe that cautery has any value after medicine, because when we administer remedies for any illness and they are ineffective, then we resort to cautery, and it does have value.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it becomes clear that cautery is indeed the last of medicine, not according to the opinions of ignorant people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold cautery instruments are better than iron ones, and they only considered the quality of the gold and the high value of its substance; they said that the heat of cautery does not burn, but I have tested it and found that it is true for no man; gold cautery is more effective than iron.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet, when you heat the gold instrument, you are not sure if it is heated through by the color of the gold, and as soon as it cools down; and if it is overheated, it goes to the fire; and thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cautery because we have made it suitable for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	You have ordered this chapter from the beginning to the end, so that the path may be lighter to follow.
dou cautere olivaire	Oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Fire cautery is useful for moisture and cold on the head, and it is effective in cases of disease called "soda", and due to many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for numerous dreams, toothaches, throat pains, and especially in all diseases caused by cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar ailments.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient is purged with a solvent medicine, cleansing the head III or IV times, according to what the virtue and age, and the patient's habit can bear; and then the head of the patient is made red again.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit with his back between your hands, and place his hands on some weight; afterwards, put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two fingers; and leave it there until your two middle fingers come, then apply the cautery called "olive" (olivare), which has this shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And mark the place with ink, then gently and slowly lower and pull your hand, disturbing it slightly; afterwards, lift your hand alone, and if you see the bone fully healed, stop the cautery as I told you; then take a little silk and fill it with soft butter and place it on the wound, leaving it for three days until the burning sensation is gone; after that, dress the wound with the remedy called "tetrafarmacon" while it is still clean.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they say that the older a wound is, the more it bleeds; and because of this, one must act quickly.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one must not leave the cautery so long that the bone is burned, and then remove what is burned from the bone, and it will heal.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another says that one must leave the cautery for so long, and pull so hard that the bone is displaced as wide as a woman's fetus, so that the humors can come out; and one should keep the wound open for a long time; then one should cleanse and dress it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in all cases, except for those who have no choice but to suffer; and I think I should leave them; for the joint is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we see in other members; and when the patient's joint is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery seems safer and more mobile to me, and from this I always use it together for the good.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain in the head comes and lasts for a long time, patients should use herbs and pills called 'cochie', and purgatives for the head and eyes and bandages; and if one performs the cautery that we have mentioned above, and it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's joint is of strong nature and not too stiff; then cauterize it deeply as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cauterizing each horn of the shoulder joint as we have said before, and cauterizing the one called "vasselz" (likely referring to a specific muscle or tissue), which is where ventouses (cupping glasses) are applied, gently hold your hand so that you do not see the bone. The patient experiences much greater pain from this cautery than from others, which I will discuss later. It is important that the cauterization of the horn joints be more precise than that of the middle part of the shoulder, and this is its form:
dou cautere dou chief	For fire cautery, instruct the patient 
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the head sudden pain arises, and the disease spreads to the oil (or possibly eye), and the condition is purged with purgative medicines, and other treatments as I have mentioned in the division of diseases, none of these bring relief, then one should perform cauterization according to two methods, that is, using a hot ague medicine or by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with hot ague medicine involves pricking a small hole in the skin and removing the flesh around it (escorce) and the covering layer (recope), then placing the exposed part back under the skin in such a way that you can close the wound. Keep it tied and compressed for 12 hours, then untie it and treat the wound with strong poultices for 2-3 days, after which apply cotton soaked in butter until healing is complete.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the dressing is done, as long as it is healed; and if you see something burning from any of the medicinal fires that I have written about or the treatment of medicinal fires.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the fire cautery with this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because the head is shaped like a seal or cap where there is a small appearance; and it is placed on the painful joint, and you hold your hand and gently twist the fire slightly, until half of the depth of the heart is burned; and then lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is dangerous, and abundant blood flows.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing cotton in the wound, leave it for three days; then moisten it with butter, and continue treating the wound until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare," be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine that is not old.
de emigraine	migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When treating migraine as we have previously described in the divisions of illnesses, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cautery mentioned in the medicine does not suffice, then you must reheat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; then apply it to the painful area along a line half a digit long, lift your hand once, and be careful not to cut the artery or let it bleed down to the bone. Guard against the jaw muting when chewing, and ensure the tongue remains motionless, preventing spasms from affecting the patient. Be cautious regarding the clotting of blood from the artery that has been cut, especially in someone who is unaware or unstudied, as this can be very frightening. Leave the wound half-healed. But I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it is mentioned in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice against the disease, and the patient suffers, cauterize both parts as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healthy; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter about the extraction of the artery, with a cautery having two blades; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.

de la torture de la bouche	Of mouth torture" translates roughly to "Du torture de la bouche" in

This is the shape of the cautery.

de litargie	The word "de litargie" appears to be related

de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine. After the surgeon has prepared the patient, make an incision around the dislocated joint, making it as circular as possible and placing it back in its socket; let the patient rest with their arms crossed and firmly secured from all sides; apply a dressing, using aged butter, and heat it at a manageable fire so that the patient can bear it; then remove the circular bandage from inside the socket and allow it to cool; and repeat this process for the patient once each week with a different, suitable treatment until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or, if you need to cauterize it, make several incisions across the cautery.

And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and shape, according to your constraints; and do not turn away from the right path those who have study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have explained in the sections on diseases, and your treatments are of no benefit, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in a healthy position; then take his arm and rest it between your hands in such a way that he does not move or raise his head; afterward, apply moist cotton soaked in wine or persil juice on top of the wound. Next, heat up the cautery tool until it is hot enough: position it over the head as if it were a quill, ensuring that the cautery itself touches the skin; if you find it more suitable, point it from one side to the other, or make it look like a tent; however, whatever shape it takes, this part should be moved for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, open it and drain the pus and moisture; if it is closed, perform the operation again and draw out the bowel; then place the hot cautery on a firm surface, hold your hand over the affected area above the oil to prevent any mishap, and apply the cautery to the fat of the oil, and the corruption.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you start the cauterization close to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, restart the cauterization again, and do so as many times as necessary, leaving it for three days; then apply moistened butter cotton to cure the drying dressing until it is healed, and if after forty days it remains unhealed, apply a corrosive medicine to the exposed bone; and the remedy should be according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that no one from the past spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand the fistula, fix its position; then apply a subtle heated tool to it, thus forming:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and it makes the quantity of a drop of blood; and hold your hand firmly, and do not let the patient move at all, so that the blood does not escape from its place; and it is necessary to put on the patient soft moist cotton or wool in such a way that the drop remains close to the fistula, and the healthy tissue recovers wonderfully through this.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the ulcer is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, it is necessary to administer heat or cold, and bring the ulcer back into the body according to what is appropriate for its own place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks appear in the lips, known as 'poil', especially on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these wounds as we have discussed in the previous sections, and the treatment does not benefit, then use a small surgical knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And insert the instrument into these wounds until it reaches the bottom; after that, treat the wound with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms in the throat's root or uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it causes putrefaction and swelling, becoming a fistula, and you treat it as we have discussed in previous sections, but it does not benefit; then you should perform cauterization according to the size of the fistula. After extracting or opening the fistula, hold your hand until the heat from the fire reaches the bottom, and leave it there. Do this once or twice, following the treatment we have mentioned for wounds, until it is healed. If treated in this way, it is good; if not, you must expose the affected area and remove the corrupt bone, as you will find described in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	no movement of the joints
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and treatment with medicines is ineffective, then place the patient's aching jaw in a healthy position; afterward, apply the hot cautery where the tooth's shape will be as if you put a cane on the tooth; and insert the hot cautery deeply, holding your hand tightly so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; then release your hand and repeat the cauterization according to your desire; afterward, make the patient rinse his mouth with salt water, and do this for an hour or longer.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner, the teeth that were moving are fixed firmly, and the gums softened and restrained, and the moisture corrupted and dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from cold, or there is chill or fever, and the cures of medicine are ineffective, then it is necessary to use cauterization according to these two methods: butter cauterization and fire cauterization.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cauterization is such that you press butter into a cold spoon made of iron or silver, then wrap cotton around the pointed end and moisten it with melted butter. Apply it to the aching tooth firmly and hold until it cools; do this several times so that its virtue reaches the root of the tooth. If the moistened wool and cotton in butter seems too soft, apply it again to the aching tooth and place a hot iron on top until the heat rises up to the edge of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	He performs the fire cautery by making a flame so intense that it sears a piece of iron or steel, rendering it hot enough to not be endured by the patient; then he warms the cautery, which will shape itself as follows, and places it on the tooth, holding his hand until the cautery cools down; do this repeatedly, for the pain will subside in that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in anticipation of this cautery, and then suck on a hot brick; and this is the shape of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And perform the cautery on the upper lip where you wish, according to what you can do; and this is the shape of the instrument.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is from cold moisture and is not obedient to digestion with medicine, then apply hot cautery afterward so that the form appears, and it has openings for the fumes of the cautery to escape from the other side; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, as it is necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply cautery according to its quantity, and leave it thus for three days; and then cover it with moist cotton or butter until the burn is healed; afterward cure the shoulder with oil and bandages until it is sane.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture conquers the channels of the body, especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be freed first by soluble medicines; after, make them perform cautery at the root of the throat, and beware not to go down to the throat, and only dare with a little heat.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, perform another cautery at the joint of the collarbone with the spine, and these cauteries that are called "clavicle" as we have shown before; cure the limb as we have said above until it is healed.
de la toust	from the heat
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and any illness of the shoulder is caused by cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or rigidity, and it is an old illness, then make two cauterizations on the strong parts of his veins; and another cauterization between the two joints of the limbs; and this cauterization which is called "clavicle" is according to the form mentioned above.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make a cauterization by pricking the entire cauterization called "point" from which the shape is as mentioned above in the illness of the ears; and the points can be up to 30, or even more.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the treatment, reset the limb according to what is mentioned above, and make the cauterization in three stages according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because cautery is lighter, because you do it three times.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the joint
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, remember to support the patient on their back and side; afterwards, gently press the area inside the wound with your left hand. If the joint is disaligned internally, apply heat to the cautery with two thin pieces of cloth until it forms a shape.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and burn the heart as long as it feels hot, and let the image of the burn be three burns together; for this reason, cauterization is done with a cautery having three prongs, so that the shape of the cauterization is six prongs; and the nerve according to the fineness of a thread, and this is the form of the cautery with three prongs.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never adjust this nerve, for which there are eight burns.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After placing the burn, put on bandages with silk; then rest the patient and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated from above, this happens rarely, then apply cautery to the thick part with a hot iron, or use many cauterizations by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	Because the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach, causing it to lose its color, and catarrh multiplies within it, and usual treatments do not help, then the patient should be careful on his back, extending his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	From this and afterwards, perform three cauterizations by removing the flesh with a knife as thin as a finger, across all the cautery; and two cauterizations on each side until the shape of the cautery is at three angles, and there is enough space between them that they are not joined together when they rot; and make the cautery so complete that it affects both parts of the heart, and the shape of the cautery remains without adjustment.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you are cauterized with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form, and he who is afraid of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and marking on the stomach at the point as much as you see fit; then cauterize across the entire cautery called "point.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment we have previously discussed, as long as he is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver experiences pain from cold and moisture and excessive flatulence, as long as it is disrupted from its natural state due to excesses; and the patient is treated as we have said in divisions, but it does not help, then it is necessary that the patient be careful with his head; and a sign of this is three cauterizations according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, removing the humors, starting from the right or left side of the navel; and there should be enough space between each cauterization, approximately the thickness of two fingers; and the cauterization should be long throughout the body, without pressing too hard with the hand over the entire cauterized area; and it is burned only slightly on both sides of the heart, and the patient should rest his legs and ease his breath; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish to cauterize these cauteries with a knife, if you are clever and skilled in the art, be careful not to burn the entire heart, for it would cause great harm; and let it not come to boiling, for the blood vessels there are very delicate, and the wise ones know this.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you need to know if it is within the liver tissue or in the peritoneum: if it is within the liver tissue, the patient feels moderate pain; but if it is in the peritoneum, they feel intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure requires rest, it is necessary that the patient be careful with their head; then mark the place where the abscess is, and then apply the hot cautery which resembles a reed, in such a way:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the cautery until the veins are burned, and come just to the pus, as long as the infection is entirely gone; after the cure, according to the treatment of wounds, as long as it is healed; and it is not appropriate for this cautery to be used by anyone other than someone who has studied medicine extensively and whose hands these diseases have never corrupted.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can move it boldly, but I still think it is better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	The "discation" or "dislocation" treatment of tears (pleursin
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for pleursin (tears), one should perform cautery with an aristologe root, in this manner: take a long aristologe root, as large as you can find, and dry it, making sure it is also as thick and as long as your arm; moisten it in oil, hold it over the fire, and cauterize (make a burn) at the upper part of the eye between the eyelashes and the eyebrow, and small burns down in the area beneath the beard; also cauterize between the fifth and sixth ribs while slightly bending back, and another one across the hip, and yet another on the stomach, and between the shoulders; do not press your hand hard, but hold it open as if smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they say that no old man should use fire cautery resembling a razor, and burn it, and place it between the ribs, until it reaches this abscess; and there will be great pain, as we have said about the hot kidney.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work, there is great fear, or the sick die now, or a fistula appears that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mouse according to the divisions of treatment we have mentioned, and it does not benefit, then they (the healers) resort to three ways of cauterization that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Dislocate the joint in such a way that you make three cauterizations, or four, following the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the cautery of the fire that we have mentioned above; and do not rush your hand to all the cauterization, and let the patient be careful on his back; and another way of cauterizing is to heat the cautery with two irons, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and ease the pressure that is on the mouse, or the pain from which the patient suffers from the left side, and elevate it according to the pressure, according to the length of the body, and let the cauterization be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After you have heated the two irons until the pressure is felt on both sides, then quickly remove the cautery, and thus you will have four. And if you see that the cauterization is complete at three irons, be careful to cauterize the whole cautery with three irons.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has festered for a long time, this is more difficult to treat than other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	The term "ydropisie" appears to be a medieval
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not effective for edema, except in the manner known as "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	If your treatment according to the methods we have mentioned in divisions is not effective, then you should perform four cauterizations around the waist, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spine, and two behind the back on the kidneys, and make sure these cauterizations are close to the affected area.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the cautery open for a long time to allow pus to drain, do not abandon the patient's care after the cautery; healing would be hastened, and the two wounds would heal together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the stomach should be like the claw that we have shown above; and for the back, it should be oval, as is shown above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the stones
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the stones are swollen in a hydroptic patient and are filled with clear urine, you should cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and gently apply your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, so as to close the citrus wound, and be the cautery according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make two incisions around the affected area; and if there is no pain in the wrist, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains reach up to the fingers or shoulders, cauterize each part, and apply good care to the patient and take medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you apply good care and purge the fluides, it will be healed by God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the wound
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture occurs in the abdomen, and the bowels descend into the coils, it is new, so it is necessary that when you see it cure, do not disturb it that day; and use things that leave the stomach, so that the intestines descent from his stomach; after make him lie on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the bowels are repaired, and arrange them in your hands, and sign from below the rupture on the bone of the wrist, and at a whole sign that is like half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with which this form is.
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and exudes tendrils.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their proper places; and have the minister place his hand so that they do not return backward; and carefully open the patient's thighs, and put cushions and supports beneath them on both sides, and another one upon his rear which holds his hands; then apply the cautery to the sign on your entire hand, holding it straight and keeping it there until you reach the bone, and if you do not touch it the first time, repeat it again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the joint does not jump when applying the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that through this the patient does not die or suffer any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauterizer of children be subtle according to their measure, and also for adults according to their measure; after three days cure the joint with butter until the burn is healed; afterwards treat other wounds until they are clean, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well closed; and it is necessary that his movements be limited for a long time, so that the boils do not appear when he goes to bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to stand up, apply a well-made bandage and use it for another forty days; and have good rest, work little and guard against too much drinking and eating, and excessive laughter; and following this instruction, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will now describe the treatment for cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are known not to heal, you should perform cautery according to its extent, burning the third of the heart; after which, follow the cure as we have said; and no one among the ancients has stated that it should be cauterized at three angles in this manner.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the site of the hernia with a sign, and make a line across the width above the rupture; then another from below, and hold your hand firm over all the cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cautery is lighter and easier.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain arises in any limb, whether from falling or injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and the medicinal cure is ineffective, then it should be cauterized with the cautery known as "the point," and the cauterization must be done according to the length of the limb and its smallness and fragility, and its twist, and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the first cautery is successful, it's good; but if not, start again with another cautery on the same limb, because such is its custom to move towards the nearest limb, so you must perform the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	From illness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The wounds are aided in no way by cautery, especially the illness that arises from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	If you can see the wound, take care if the illness is in its beginning, and if it can be cured as we have said in the previous division, and does not stay nor linger, and you doubt that the corruption might spread to all the patient, then make a cautery on the head: first on the new growth, and the other at the end of the hair on the forehead; also on both horns, and behind on the nape; and let your hand be so steady that the cautery reaches the bone, and until the scabs come out far enough for the vapors of the thick humors to escape; and cauterize the mouse according to what is suitable.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the pain is spread throughout, it becomes evident that you must cauterize these cauteries we have mentioned above, starting with the soles of the feet, and cauterize on the spine at the nape of the neck, and cauterize on the spine at the back, and one on the hip joint, and another on each shoulder; and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the wrist, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the pits of the hands; and beware of the nails that are on the bottom of the feet, so as not to burn them. Never make a cautery on the bone of the elbow, or another on the stomach bone, or one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you perform cauterization, the greater the aid it provides and the more beneficial it is; and know that the patient feels no pain from cauterization as the healthy do, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be great and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the ways of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, apply wheat flour with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling appears in any member and is cured by medicines, oils, and bandages, but there is no improvement, then make a cautery on the member according to its size and shape; and the cautery should go slightly into the flesh towards the heart; then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never should a cautery be performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the end of the nerve that controls the member, and thus if the swelling is removed; nevertheless, no one should attempt this unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the passages of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of albars (or albaras, a medical term
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is ignited, and the medical art has no effect, then cauterize with a hot iron, according to the amount of thick pus, until the white (pus) is drained, and it changes color; then apply a cure made of flour, lentils, rose oil, plantain leaves, collical moss, and alder bark, each part separately; mix them all together, wrap it in cloth, and keep it at the site until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of a cancer (chancre) by cauterization.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a wound appears at the beginning, and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that seems to form a circle, around the entire wound.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	However, wise people say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the wound; nevertheless, I do not find this good, as I fear it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never wanted it to happen. A better practice is to cauterize around the wound, with a cautery called "circle," as we have said regarding many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	from the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has a disease called "adubelati," and it does not want to die or because of the excess it produces or because of the old age of the patient when he is weak (that is, too much) and has little blood, or because of time; then you see that it hastens to die: at this point, cauterize around with many small cauteries while piercing; after, leave it so.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	Because it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through all the cautery, make the cautery so hot that this is its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this illness called "adubelati" until the cauterization has reached the heart, and it is done in such a way that the patient feels relief in this manner so that the flow of putrefaction is stopped.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment, until it is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	Heal the fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another type of illness is called "corrodens," which is nothing other than a corruption of the member, as it attacks the members just as fire does the dry wood.
