Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a limb that can be treated with fire cautery, then heat the cautery instrument very small and very large, according to what is suitable for the limb or the disease; after cauterizing all parts until you eliminate all corruption, leave nothing from it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and apply oil to the cauterized limb suffering from broiling due to fire until all burns from the fire are eliminated, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of wounds that cause pain.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days the wound does not heal, it is good; and if not, repeat the cautery on the part that has remained dislocated from the corrupt joint.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this mixture has never been cured with a strong medicine instead of fire cautery; however, fire cautery is more helpful, and I have already described the treatment with a weak medicine in the previous section: take it as needed.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the vessels that come as pieces
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that a pain arises from a defect which we call "close" according to our intention, and it is a great fault which wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is when you heat the cautery cheveit (a type of instrument) like a pen with a bow, and make it from good iron to the proper size that can pierce the nail from all sides, and have subtle margins; then place it hot on the nail and turn your hand around the nail until it goes to the bottom of the nail; leave it thus for three days until it begins to fester; then apply a poultice of wild mallows, finely ground with wool, and leave it on all night. The nail will come off and be extracted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the shoulder with a warm compress until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	If they are affected by heat and the skin is blistered and irritated, it is necessary to apply hot water cautery; this is done as follows: take a cane of iron or steel, or a pen-like instrument with a sharp point, and place the claw and the irritant (i.e., the blister) on top, specifically targeting warts. Place the cane around them so it envelops everything, then pour some hot water over it, holding your hand firm and twisting the cane so that its edge comes into contact with the root of the nail. Ensure the hot water reaches all the way to the base. Let the patient endure the stinging sensation of the hot water for an hour; then leave it be, and the affected area will eventually come loose from its roots completely.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	First, do one after another, until you have eased all those that are in the body, then treat the injuries which cause pain.
li cure dou trembler	It cures the trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	If anyone trembles from cold or quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you make them four cauterizations or five on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one cauterization on the fish, and one on the stomach with an olive cauterization; if this stops the trembling and hastens their recovery from cold disease.
des pustules puans	from pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never is it apparent through external defects or pus-filled blisters that come from highly corruptive matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	if it is necessary in the first place when they appear that one performs a cauterization on each head of the pustule: a subtle cauterization with a stick of myrtle, of which the point is seized by fire, or with a long root of aristologue, or with a lenticular cauterization.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never should one cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow worse in advance, but the excesses from which they come are broken off and healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there occur great complications from the blood of an artery that is cut in a wound that leads to gangrene, or to the incision of an abscess, or to cauterization of a limb, and similar things; it is a very grievous thing to become infected.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	However, if it happens to anyone, hurry to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it tightly until the pain is completely relieved from your finger, and no more blood flows; then take several small and large olive oils and heat them in the fire until they are all red hot. Then, according to the size of the wound and the position of the artery, place the cautery on the vein where you hold your finger, and keep it there until the pain is completely stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a sudden burning occurs while you are lying with your arm above the vein and the cauterization is complete, quickly take another cautery from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And continue to apply one after the other until the pain is completely gone; be careful not to burn the nerve that is close by, and let no further harm come to the patient; and know that when the flow from the artery ceases, it cannot be well restored, especially when the artery is large, except by one of the four methods we have mentioned: either by cauterization, or extraction when it has not been treated, or tightly wrapping it with strong thread, or applying medicines that have the power to stop blood flow; and bind and fasten it securely.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers relief tightly binding them with cloth or placing hot things on them, or similar, will not benefit unless he does it properly.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they have no suitable medicine at hand, he should apply his two fingers to the wound of the vein as we have said, pressing firmly until it ceases to hurt from the pressure on the wound and the vein; and he should not move his finger, but moisten it with cold water often, as much as it becomes very cold, so that the pain subsides and the swelling and bruising cease. And make inquiries about what they need for cauterization and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	We begin the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every illness in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and about the herbs, causes, tools, and shapes of cauterization; I placed that chapter dealing with the head and neck up to this point, and now I will proceed to this chapter using the same method so that those who wish to learn may find it easier.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, before we begin, it is important for you to know that this chapter involves greater risk and fear than the first one on cauterization, and therefore requires more caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	Because many ways of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from such who are so certain of their illness that they die slightly because of the severity of their condition and the magnitude of their suffering; and for these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who give you their consent, saying: "Wait, I am tired"; and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not give consent to those who come to you with such a manner, but put more great care in your honor than in your greed, and do not act rashly but wisely regarding those whom you are certain of, and from whom you can obtain and let go; and use prophecy and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health may be restored; and this will help you to gain a good reputation, glory, and lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear child, our lords give you good understanding and rectitude, and if you desire the holy inspiration from his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter for you, in considering by chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery that I have devised from the head down to the foot, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	dou chief plein d'aigue" translates to "a head filled with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	You know that this illness comes very often in children at birth, and when the child's head is too tightly restrained, it causes no end of trouble as there is no known cure.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness except in children, and to all those that I have seen, death comes quickly; and for this reason, I think it is best to leave the work in parts for treatment.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose joints were filled with water, and the head swelled each day until it could not be supported; and due to the moisture, he died, and this moisture is gathered under the bone near the joint, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such that the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, so you must make a wide cut across the head until the moisture runs out; and it will be as long as necessary, until the moisture has drained. And see the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the openings of the sinuses in each part widely open, and there is a sharp, strong discharge when you press it with your hand from inside, and it does not return, then you should make three cuts in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After loosening the cracks of wounds and applying poultices and oil, he puts it on for up to five days; then he unbinds it and treats the wound with bandages and compresses, and stretches the head evenly, and gives the patient dry meat from a bag of moisture until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you observe or measure the size of the abscess and the arrangement of the water; for it never appears in front, nor behind, neither on the right nor on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Measure therefore the abscess and the water it contains, and cut along its edge; be careful not to touch the artery; then comes a flow of blood, so that the patient dies from a gentle decay caused by blood and moisture evacuation.
de reume	Of the root
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens to anyone a disease called "cataract" as some call it or worse, and the illness is ancient, and the cure of medicine does not help, then the last remedy is the cautery with which one severs both arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, as soon as you see the patient turn their head back, rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries open, then gently pull the patient's collar all the way up using a sharp scalpel from both sides, close to the ears where the arteries are located, and make sure they are closed. Then mark the spots with signs, sever one of them with the scalpel, making a cut as wide as the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, remove the spatule from beneath the artery and cut above it, also cutting as it should go through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it bleeds continuously unless something holds it shut from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open by itself, it is necessary to measure the quantity of space equal to three fingers, then seal it with a thread and make it go up to the bone; and this amount of blood to be let out is six parts, or perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can withstand and the filling of the artery. Then look at the wound: if there is no discharge from pus on the bone where the cut ends, remove the bandage and bind it, and apply treatment as long as it remains clean.
de emigrainne	from migraine headache
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old migraine headaches come with catarrh due to moisture in the eyes and sockets, and cold perspiration, and other similar symptoms, and all medical treatments are ineffective, then we should drain the arteries of the eyes and apply cautery, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient pulls out the hairs from his temples, and locates the artery which opens in the temple, as it opens well with its beating, and is very deep that no man who is too quick can reach it; and if it is covered, then the patient strains it with some cloth, and rubs the place with a rough cloth, and applies hot water until the artery becomes clearly visible; then take the instrument in the shape of this:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin gently until you reach the artery, then treat it with pincers, and separate it well from the threads that hold it in each part; and if the artery is thin, turn it to the tip of the hook, then cut off that portion according to the quantity of two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it does not heal without great pain throughout.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat the abscess with six pieces of garlic, until three are consumed; and if the artery is large, it is necessary to tie it with two threads of strong silk, so that putrefaction does not come before the healing of the wound and causes complications; then cut off the excess between the two threads at the same time, and if you see fit, cauterize the patient with a cutting instrument until the joints are cut; and this is the most effective treatment, if the patient does not have fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery is aid to finish off moisture: therefore it is of greater help with moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the wound with cotton wool and cover it with tightly-bound bandages; and when they are untied, be careful to apply dry medicines that produce heat, and fresh bandages until healing is complete; and as soon as you see the artery exposed, hasten to close it by cauterization, or use vitriol and press with your hand so that the wound is sterilized; and if you do not have this at hand, place ice on the wound until the bleeding stops, and then draw out the cotton wool as required; and what moves more easily and is lighter in the extraction of the artery is to cauterize the vein from this cautery, cutting it from both sides, but the cuts should be well spaced to preserve heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	Because when the instruments are too tight, they hold back their heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have space between the two blades large enough, and then when you have cut through both bones, you place the hot iron onto it until it reaches the bone, and open the vein in two places; and make sure there is distance between the two joints because this cautery is not firmly joined throughout. And this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes descend into the veins that are on the head and face, and medicine applied there does not help, you see the face of the patient contort and feel a sensation as if of cold; and the skin is dry and moist so that the hairs on the eyelids fall out, and the eyelids are scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called this the ancient "contused cure", and what you do for the patient suffering from this condition is to cut the hairs on their forehead, then make three cuts on the forehead evenly according to its length; one of the cuts should be as deep as two, extending downward towards the nose, and the other two cuts are made in the middle of each side of the forehead, above the eyelids. Avoid incising the arteries that are on either side of the forehead. Keep your hand away from the continuation of the mandibles, and make sure each wound is about three finger-widths across. Have a piece of sponge and cloth ready to wipe away the blood, then mold the spatula with its sharp edge as follows:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made on the temple, all the way to the second incision; and scrape all the tissue that lies between the two incisions, down to the surface of the bone, then make another cut from the middle of this one to the other second, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you insert the instrument called "cultellaire" (a type of scalpel) into the first incision, it should be very sharp on one side and soft on the other; its shape is as follows:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	and place the sharp side of the instrument towards the opposite edge at the center, and the soft side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the top to the bottom until the incision is continuous all the way to the heart, and then make another slit in the middle, reaching the other side; and then extract the blood evenly, and press out the wound for the blood taken; then place a piece of old cotton in each slit, and cover it with moistened cloths in wine and oil and lard, and ensure that no abscesses form; and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and administer a strong flow of cold water, then apply basilicon dressing with rose oil, and other treatments to cure wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	your joints.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any catarrh comes habitually, and you see the eyes swollen and small, weakening vision, and the membranes burning, and the hair falling out, and the head aching painfully, and the patient sneezing; then know from these symptoms that this matter and catarrh do not come from a single cause, but rather from many veins, and the moving cure that exists is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to press their forehead, then make a deep cut across the forehead, and another one very wide.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the cut in the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the muscles of the temples that move when you blink. When the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood out with a sponge, then separate the two edges of the cut and place old cotton on it, and cover it with linen strips. Then wrap moistened cloths dipped in wine and oil over it and be careful not to get any pus; once the bone is healed, rub the bone gently until the pain goes away, then use drying agents that prevent infection.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of rye flower and three parts of colchicum, and make a paste; apply it to these wounds to draw out the poison throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear infections
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that causes an infection in the ears is one of four things: grains, animals, mineral stones, or similar objects; seeds, such as beans, peas, or other pulses; or fluids, like water or mucus and similar substances.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	If anything, such as a stone or any other object that does not fit properly in the ear, causes pain or does not grow inside the ear, place the affected ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, and it distills any little drop of purple oil or oil of myrrh, then it is ready for extraction; and the deed is to make him sneeze from the condition, and stop his nostrils when sneezing occurs, and place within the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and stretch the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times this treatment causes fever; and if it does not come out, extraction is done with delicate pincers, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pincers, that's good; if not, extraction is done with a thin, double-sided instrument; and if it still does not come out, a chain of iron is made and the head of the chain or an opening in the ear is blocked tightly with soft wax so that the air current cannot enter with the chain. Then the treatment is carried out thoroughly, as we have said many times; and if it still does not come out in this way, a lot of pressure is applied to the stone with cotton between them, and a suitable instrument is used to force it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not do all these things that we have said, hurry to split the ear so that the abscess hardens and the spasms cease; and the method of splitting is such that you first make the patient from the cephalics, extract the blood according to its virtue, then place the patient between your hands and bring the ear back up, making a small cut at the base of the ear where the fat or tissue depends; and let the split be as thin as a moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it vigorously in your mouth; and treat until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if there are grains present and they swell, then perform extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, then apply a delicate spatula according to this form.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and perform an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not attempt this if you think the grain is moist due to earwax, having made many attempts with it; then extract it with subtle forceps and suck gently, as we have said, so that the extraction is light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case where something breaks off in the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use sneezing to expel the foreign object, and to open the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lay something on that same ear, whether there is a foreign body or water.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps through fire, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If the fire is not hot enough, take many small twigs, according to the length of your thumb, and heat them slightly over the fire; then put the patient in a gap or hole in his ear and try from another side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and keep doing this stone-on-stone until all the liquid has completely left, and so it will jump out completely. And if you see any remaining, take a thin twig and insert one of the ends into the ear, and burn the other end with fire as much as the thicker twig is burned; then do the same thing with other twigs until all the liquid has completely left, as we have said for the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	During the removal of an animal, if it is a small bone, like a pin or similar object, treat it as we have said in the previous section. But if it is a large bone that one can feel, use pincers for its extraction; and it is the lighter matter to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When treating earworms as we have described in the previous section and dealing with discharge, if the treatment is not effective, you should examine the ear in sunlight. If no worms are visible, use fine pincers to remove them; if they still cannot be seen, take note of their shape.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be tightened from below and widened from above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And then gently turn the bottle more subtly into the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient, then suction until all the air is extracted; do this often until all the bubbles disappear.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, then stop the air from escaping around the cotton as I mentioned before; and if they do not protrude as we said, then administer distillations that the ancients have tried in treating worms, and you will find them or learn about distillations; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear using all these instruments, forming them as you see fit.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And take a thin piece of silver or gold, and put it over the small opening to distill; and above the vessel to collect the distillation; and with a well-made brass instrument press down within the distillation, then take a razor and wrap a piece of soft cloth around the tip carefully; then pour in your oil or juice, and whatever you choose from your medicines into the ear, and the candle should be in the ear. Then put the razor completely into the cotton and press your hand firmly until the oil is distilled or slightly drawn out of the ear; and let the patient feel it within, and the distillation will be warm as if it were distilled in the ear; but be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not then be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From ear discomfort
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born with any perforation in their ears; and the same occurs with adults due to a wound or an object lodged inside the ear, and this blockage comes completely obstructing the ear, unless one can see it; and sometimes the perforation becomes slightly wider, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When the blockage completely obstructs the ear, if one cannot see it, it requires careful treatment in multiple ways, and in this case, it is necessary to place the affected ear towards the sun; and look inside. If you see the swelling clearly visible, with all these small particles forming a shape, then that indicates:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And make cuts and incisions all around and behind the ear, so it does not damage; if the inflammation is from a foreign body or the cartilage of the ear, hold it with delicate pincers and remove it gently until that part is completely cleaned.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	If the inflammation is deep in the ear, take a fine, sharp razor, warm it slightly over the fire, and insert it into the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the inflammation where the patient feels great pain in the ear, make a slight hole, and be careful not to hurt the edge of the ear; then place in the ear a plug according to the size of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Make sure no dirt remains in the wound until it is healed, or take a cloth and dampen it with rosewater, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on it; and if you see an ear swollen, it is necessary to remove the tent and replace it with another moistened tent made of rosin oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the occurrence of blood comes, soak a sponge and drape it with cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that remove the flow of blood, which are treated through distillation.
de la char des papieres	Of the work of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Always consider that papers (or materials) coming from moisture become stiff and brittle; it is necessary to extend them with clamps and pincers, taking care to remove the root of a spatula, then place them in hot vinegar.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if, after peeling them, you cauterize with a subtle lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after incision is moved; and often they repair themselves, as if nothing had remained of their roots; and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not come back.
de la gresle	from the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come to us papers of certain things that seem gravel in form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail," and it is a gathering of great moisture on the paper both inside and out; the work involves: take care if the hail becomes silent from one side to the other, and this is a slight thing to notice; then make a cut with a wide blade, gently scrape each part, then take hold of them with pincers and chip away.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot chip away without piercing the paper slightly, it causes no harm to the patient; and if the gathering is great, and has a seam, treat it as long as it remains healthy; but if it is small, do not use much force, for the adhesions will soon restore it and cause trouble.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the pain is descending inside the ear towards the top part, turn the paper around, and the pain will be in pinches, pressing from both sides; and if the paper is moved by incision, it causes no harm; and when the pain is cut away, drain the water with salt, and cure the place that caused the pain until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinch is a fat that is trapped under the skin of the eyes, and it occurs more often in children than in adults, causing great pain to their eyes. It leads to cataracts in the morning, preventing them from gazing at the light of the sun because tears constantly flow from their eyes. Due to this, they rest their faces on their hands, sleeping with their eyes closed, and the skin beneath their eyebrows becomes moist, revealing the presence of exinch that has opened up in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the limb with your hands and feel the extreme pain between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of performing this procedure is that the patient places their head on a healthy surface; then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in a circular manner according to the quantity of blood from each part, place it on top; press with your hands on both sides so that the blood collects within the circle; make a small cut in the middle with a sharp spatula, no larger than the wound made on a vein, and ensure the skin is completely sealed; continue until all the blood has drained; and in different positions, more blood will drain from the cutout, forming a shape like a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract then, with one whole piece of cloth between your fingers over the fire, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread; and be careful not to press into the gap, do not reach all the way to the oil, do not touch it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the gap does not open at first, gently widen it a little until it opens; then extract as we have said, and moisten cloth with water and blood, and place on the wound, and strain by bending.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if with such people who grind and apply something to corrupt the moisture that is stuck.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it as long as it is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the hot abscess, treat it with external soothing as long as it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow in papers (abnormal hair growth), other than their natural state, and they become inflamed, causing harm as if they were custom-made tears, soften the papers, and produce albugine (a type of scurf), all due to the destruction of the hairs; then the cure is to be done in four ways: either with a cauterizing fire, or with ague medicine according to what is mentioned in the chapter on cautery, or through incision and stitching, or by plucking, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your healthy hand, then turn the paper from the oil on your left hand; if it turns, that is good; if not, insert an needle along all the thread above; and this should be done at the edge of the paper where the hairs grow, along all the thread above the entire paper, and turn it against the razor. Then cut the paper away from the hairs, from the base to the tip, from the large tear to the small one; then extract the thread, and place under the paper a small piece of cotton and cloth, and sign on the paper with a figure of an anchor, like the shape of myrrh, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you raise the paper which is measured in all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if you take a skilled person who cuts a great quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make a cut across all two lines that you have marked, and begin with a large tear from one end to the other; and let it be one of the splits near the natural hairs, in the thickness of a root, then turn the edge in one of the two angles towards the heart, then scrape off all of it; then bring the two edges together with a stitch of a needle with all the thin threads of wool, and wipe away the blood, and let go of the excess threads on both sides without any sticky things, if you can do this. And if not, leave the stitch and the threads for three or four days, then treat the wound without stitches using drying and constricting things, because the paper revives with the healing of the wound and the gathering of it, but the stitch moves (as the ancients say), and that is a work without sorrow; or in another way: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure like the leaf of a myrtle, as we have told it, at three points according to the shape that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take hold of what overcomes the small muscles equally according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the tweezers, and the matter is not equal, take a needle with thread and wrap it around the figure; and wrap another thread through the large wound, and the second thread through the small one, and assemble them equally between your fingers; then gently let go of your hand equally, and gently all the skin marked by you; as we have said, then sew together the two edges of the wound, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, calm it with wax and similar soothing applications; and sometimes happens that the paper-like matter sticks: it is necessary for you to use what we have said about the incision; but sewing in one way or another is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for the back is as follows: take paper and make it inside according to what I have said, then create two strips by art, also thin, as long as the paper and wide enough; tie both parts where you hold the threads; assemble them carefully on top of the paper from oil, and pull the two strips from the formed parts; leave it like this for several days, and the skin that was strained will die, contract, and fall off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays and the strain is strong, then treat it while it is still healthy; when the wound is healed and if the paper can be lifted, and the hairs do not grow back; this is the shape of the two strips that you will make according to this figure and this quantity in length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work requires such skill that you must press an extremely fine needle into the skin, and wrap it with soft and fine silk thread; then join the parts together and tie them gently, so that the length of the threads is a palm's length; then arrange in the wound another fine thread of silk quickly, and tie the ends loosely with thread; then place the patient's head on your healthy body; and let the sun be so positioned that the work is revealed, for this is a delicate and precise work, then push the needle through the entire wound at its root, where the hair is properly adjusted, and pierce it gently into the paper until you treat it above the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the wound in the paper with the natural hair. Then withdraw your hand as the hairs come completely out of the wound in the paper along with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair does not grow with the treatment and pulling, pull the hair out from the root along the entire length that you have ordered; until the hair comes out completely through the opening above, and you see it with your eye; then pull the hair and the thread, and close the wound and let it be closed for two or three days, until the new hair grows in its place; and if the hairs are small, accompany them with a longer natural hair from the horse, and raise it along with that one, as long as it is elongated and then released.
de la porriture de l’oil	regarding the inflammation of the wound
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness called "aleacrati" or putrefaction comes about in the body, it has two manners: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs suddenly from a wound, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of working on it is that you split open this adhesion, and separate the lips from it, and place linen strips inside, and bind them as long as they are healthy; and it is not appropriate to use things that dry out and constrict in the treatment of it.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than before; but there are remedies that soften, such as fennel; and rosewater of water or linen seeds cooked, and garlic oil melted in any of the eyes, and it envelops a bandage, and the cure for these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the true power of your cure lies in ensuring it does not adhere to the shape it once was; and these remedies that we have mentioned are only proper means to deal with this illness, so that it does not return to its former state.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the matter that comes into the eye

And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that is good; if not, take a razor and insert it into the fissure, turn the paper, and make two cuts on either side inside the paper; let the edges of the two cuts form two angles of the incision you have made, so that when they are brought together, the shape is like the figure of a letter "G"; then remove the char, according to the extent it has grown out from both sides, from the area next to the paper; then adjust the two parts properly and sew them with a thread of wool; then apply the treatments we have mentioned for mollifying medicines and bandages, until it is healed.

And if the illness comes from cutting, stitching, or cauterizing, it is necessary to make a clean cut beneath the skin and hair, following what has been said; then separate the two sides of a wound as I have mentioned, and one must perform the work according to the nature of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and skilled surgeons devise various means by which they can restore the natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what is appropriate for treatment and with different instruments, are placed in various positions.

de la bowe de l’oil	of the oil's fat
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the appearance of water in the division, and what is necessary to pierce; doing it according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should place the patient between your crossed hands away from direct sunlight and tie the healthy oil tightly; then place the paper of the oil in your left hand if the hairs are on the left side, or in your right hand if they're on the right; then take in your right hand, if the hairs are on the left, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand, if they're on the right; then place the tip of the instrument along the edge of the oil's crown by the thickness of a hair at the innermost part of the blade, and twist the instrument called "almagda" vigorously, and turn your hand until it pierces the crown of the oil, and feel that the almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda's way be equal to the full measure of the distance from the prunelet to the end of the shadow; and this is the crown of the oil; you will see the bone in the paper due to the clarity of the corneal fabric, and then place the instrument up to the water or where the liquid is, and express it through one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he feels a sharp descent now, if he sees the patient before him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a brief rest, and feel the second descent, insert the instrument with force, and when it is deeply embedded and does not come out, slowly extract it by turning your hand back and forth; then re-insert gently, pulling it a little from side to side, and remove the oil inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply hot oil or any other moist oil, rosin, and an abundance of wax, and wrap with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, put a fine cloth over with much heat.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the mixture cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are many people with too hard eyes, it is necessary that you press the instrument called "alberit", which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctiva gently, without causing too much damage, but make it subtle, and let the mixture enter, as we have said; and after the work is complete, prepare the patient for sleep, placing him on his back in a dark place; and be sure of all movements, give light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his condition for three days. Then release him in the same dark room, test his vision, and show him no things, and then put the bandage back on for seven more days; and it is not appropriate that you perform this at the time of treatment or after incision now, but rather you should lighten it, because acute pain rises sharply.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess appears, you should loosen the skin in front of the seventh day and follow the advice of him who soothes the abscess; when it is soothing, then loosen the wound and place a cloth on its face to cover for some time, and thus remain in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then, leave the house little by little and return to your usual life; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the East who told us of a plant that grows in distant lands and whose sap is said to heal all ills, which we suck in order to be cured, but I have never seen it in our land, nor do I remember having read about it in the books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of alchemy, for whoever does not know them will see them as strange; they should be of pure gold.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the center of this same subtlety be in one place, and the rear in three corners acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the charm on the new-born
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No child should be born with charms adjusted in various ways, for there are none that seem like scorpions filled with poison; and if there are such with a charm of fine gold color, or a charm smooth and of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In this case where the wound is sore and not yet healed, you must place the patient's face between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, pour the medicine into those wounds, and treat them fiercely; and hold what you can sustain with a delicate spatula from one side, until you know that the wound is entirely healed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there is anything left that cannot be covered, open it with all delicate and light instruments until nothing remains; and without delay, perform the incision as necessary; and for malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize while the wound is still fresh, so that it heals completely. Then apply a cool compress or wine.
