Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If he opens his mouth and moisture comes out until the gums are healthy, then you know it is safe; and if the moisture does not come out as it should, know that there is something stuck in the bone above, preventing the instruments from cutting: then you must insert a piece of linen thread somewhat thick, and use your hands skillfully, with some space between each one, and place the patient's toes wrapped in the thread into his power, and pull gently until the thread comes out through the gums; and this is often done by children at school, and it is a light task for whoever wants to do it. Then hold the cheek that comes through the gum with one hand, and the other cheek that comes through the mouth with the other hand, knowing one after the other as we who are in thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	As long as you know that the new flesh has been corrupted, then treat the child, wipe off the blood, and moisten the wound with Egyptian ointment, and put it back to its place as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments have corroded everything that is remaining in the wound; and then place a bandage around the head for no more than a day, as long as it is healed, and if there is a need for dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, with which one distills oils and medicines into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	Whether it is made of silver or gold, resembling an open lamp, like a pipe, lead it as such; and if you see fit, make a closed pipe, and let the instruments be full to purge the head; have several pipes attached to the head to hold it in place while heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the pain near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times, near the nose, there appears a sickness called "telul," which swells and grows greatly, making it a thing of great concern to look at; and for this reason, it is necessary that you grasp it at the beginning, and remove it entirely, then apply the cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay in treating it until it becomes large, be careful not to miss its soft, pale color, its poor sensation: do not touch it with iron, because it is a deep abscess. For when one treats an abscess at all, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of gentle touch, not pale in color, and you see that it can be completely treated, then empty the patient and treat it without fear, using drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and wounded
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when the flow of continuity comes to one of these powerful cartilages, it benefits little, indeed, for no man.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore appropriate to do the following when this happens to no one, if you consider that the wound is fresh with blood; and then close the two lips with a single stitch, and treat it as long as it heals; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, it is necessary that you scrape all parts of their heart while they heal, then close the two lips with a single stitch, and tighten them, and sprinkle dragon's blood powder on top of the wound, and add incense ground; and place a piece of plaster strong or other adhesive plaster over it, and leave it until it falls out by itself, then treat it with care as long as it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is such that you bring the wound together: either with needles, as we have said in stitching the belly; or with thread, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, abscesses on the lips can be hard, appearing like small grains, both smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, and split each one open, taking them as pincers and scraping each part; then apply the ointment after the vitriol is ground, until the wound is stained; then use a dry leaf, and cure the wound with things that are dry until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	from the treatment of gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a gum treatment becomes inflamed, which the ancients call "albulus"; it is necessary that you hold it with tweezers, cut off the root, and let the bowel or abscess drain; then apply soot or other powder to draw and dry it; and if the gum returns after the incision, it happens often, especially if cutting it again, and cauterize it: if it does not return after cauterization; these are the shapes of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	from obstructions
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	No teeth are ever aligned at the top of the gums, inside the mouth between the teeth and their tough edges; nor do they become black or yellow or rotten until decay reaches the gums, and then the teeth stink. It is necessary that you hold the patient's jaw in your hands, and his teeth should be in your safe keeping, and pull out any visible teeth or rough edges until nothing remains; and so do with black, green, yellow, and other types as long as they are rotten; and if you remove what is at the initial cause of this condition, it is good; but if not, repeat on the second and third day until everything is pulled. And know that teeth require different tools to pull them out, according to what the work demands, because the tool used for pulling between teeth has a different shape from that which removes individual teeth. Keep these shapes and others with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	You should take care when treating a toothache and do not delay drawing the pain out as much as you can, for no one should let it go; for it is a very precious substance, hence there is no excuse for ignoring it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is constrained from drawing out the pain, it is necessary that you be certain about the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the patient pleads with you, thinking it is a healthy tooth and asking to pull it out, but the pain does not cease because of this, as we have already seen with these patients; and when you are well certain about the aching tooth, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth with all your strength to protect the gums from all sides; then move the pliers with your fingers at the first little pull, as long as they are well gripped, then tighten the pliers; and hold the patient's jaw in your hand between your knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth properly without breaking it, if it does not come out, take none of these instruments and push it gently from each side, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the tooth is broken and chipped, it is necessary to fill the gap with cloth or use a plug where the tooth is missing; if it is tightly stuck with pincers, be careful not to break it while removing; it is very important to work carefully around the gums to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Be very careful not to break it, and if a part breaks off, return the fragment to the patient; due to the evil of the root, he will experience greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be wary that you do not act like the ignorant healers who, through their haste and boldness, break the vessels at every turn and do not take heed of what we have said; but they bring about great illness through their chatter about the roots or the vessels they break, as we often see. And when the vessel is torn, wash it with wine or honey and silk; and the bleeding that ensues, which often occurs, can be prevented by applying vitriole powder; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which to mute the vessel first, should be long and thick-handled, so as not to bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let the tools be of good quality, so that they do not bend when pulling, and made of iron well-forged, and toothed for secure grip.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains stuck when pulling, it is necessary to place over it moist cotton or butter for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the eyes are softened, then apply pliers called 'algefri', which make the dislocated part look like it's being cared for; they should be made like a file and have this shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out of these claws, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put the instrument called "althali", which is a plier, whose form is as follows:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is very thick and hard so that it does not break, and the root jumps out by itself, that is good. If not, use all the instruments, whose forms are as follows:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument with two prongs, its form is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are used in the treatment of teeth, and this instrument that resembles large pincers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument should be sturdy so it doesn't break, and you should know that many tools for teeth exist; and also other instruments, not mentioned. The most skilled surgeons create their own instruments according to the specific needs revealed by their work and the condition of the patient, as there are various diseases where no instrument was taught by the ancients. If a fragment breaks off or becomes useless, and he seeks the appropriate instruments I've told you about, he should use gestures, and its shape is as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and well-held to hold the bone firmly so that it does not escape but can be held and extracted; and then return to the patient with suitable medicine, and if there is any decay in the bone, even if small, use all these instruments.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth does not appear according to the body's natural shape, and its form is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the original one, and is not in its proper place, and cannot be filed or polished. Then extract it; and if it is impacted with the neighboring tooth, take this instrument whose shape is like a small beak, made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And take a small knife and hold it in your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it from one side as the shape allows.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like filing the metal for making needles; file the tooth little by little in your hands until it does not move anymore, when it has reached its desired shape. Then, at the end, it should be completely smooth without any roughness, and if the tooth is too sharp, it can hurt the tongue, so you must file away the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not hurt or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth hurts
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth hurts deeply, either from impact or decay, and the patient cannot bear pressure on it, they only suffer more when treated with restrictive medications, which is ineffective. They should then be restrained with an appropriate length of gold thread, for silver wire turns green and decays, but gold never does. The thread must neither be too thin nor too thick, according to the space between the teeth. If you successfully align the teeth, take the thread and wrap it twice around the two healthy teeth next to each other, then place the gum fragments (if there are any) between the misaligned teeth, as close as possible to the healthy tooth on the opposite side. Continue covering until you reach the part you started with, pulling your hand gently but firmly until the tooth no longer moves; it should be held tightly at the root by the thread.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the pieces of bone with pliers, assemble them, and insert them between the healthy teeth, and place it such that the tongue does not bleed; then leave it as tight as it can stay, and if it comes loose, the thread will come out, and it should be re-sewn with another thread; it should last for all its time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is reset in its place, fresh by fresh, as we have said; nor should anyone other than a skilled and patient person intervene, and they do not make the shape of a bone tooth from a living animal, but place it where there is a deficit, and tighten it as we have said, and let it stay for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Cut the skin around the tongue's surface.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No matter what kind of these bonds that come from beneath the tongue, whether naturally or by a deep wound; and the work involves opening the mouth of the patient with care, keeping their head in a safe position, and gently lifting the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament widely, as much as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or any other obstacle, and it is due to an instant wound, drive a hook and cut widely that bond; be careful not to cut too deep into the fissure, so as not to harm the artery beneath; and once done, lift the tongue with warm or cold water, then apply a thin cloth of linen underneath the tongue; and repeat this for each night, so that the bonds do not harden.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the blood flow occurs, place a hot stone on it; and if the pain persists, apply slow-burning caustic to it, which is good for that; then continue treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is red or black or hard, so the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it turns pale and there is moisture, pour vinegar on it and scrape it with a fine spatula from both sides; and if the pain persists in your work, place hot stones on it until it is cleansed, then return to your work until all is treated; then lift the limb gently and slowly, and continue treatment until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	From the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes, there appear in the throat openings called "godath", which are properly known as the two amandres, and when you treat them, as we have said in the previous division, if they are not fully healed, be careful: these abscesses are hard, of small size, and of a pale color, so do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is thick, do not touch them with iron, also to avoid the spread of blood; but leave it until it dies, and then you will remove it, or it will break on its own. And if they are of a white color, and the root is thin, have an instrument ready to cover it, but first ensure that the abscesses are calm and at ease.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient stand before the sun, and stretch his legs to their limit, opening his mouth wide, and gripping his teeth with his hands, pressing his tongue down onto the instrument, which forms its shape; it should be made of silver or fine gold, as sharp as a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You cannot press the tongue onto all of this instrument and observe the abscess, so take the file and insert it into the wound, pulling it out upwards as much as possible; do not touch any part of the threads with it, then cut with the instrument, forming a shape that resembles teeth; however, the head is curved inwards, one side facing the other, they are very sharp, and made of hard iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, if it is like pliers, then this is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	It should be cut on one side and named; and when you have extracted one of the mandibles, extract the other in the same manner, and after the incision, rinse the patient's wound with hot and cold water, and if bleeding occurs, rinse it with water containing extracts of pomegranate peels or myrrh, and similar substances, until the blood is stopped; then treat it while it is still fresh; and no other abscesses are formed in the throat besides the two mandibles, so cut them out as you would the two mandibles.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was in her throat, namely a small abscess; and the whole throat was tightly closed so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, nor eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained thus for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed two ribs through the two openings in the throat.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then hastened and inserted one needle into one of the openings, then drew it out, and extracted a significant portion of pus; then I did the same in the other opening, opening the mouth and pressing the tongue; after inserting the needle into these abscesses, I squeezed some pus out, only a little coming out, and thus the passageway in the throat was opened for the woman to begin drinking water and then wine, and I continued cutting into the abscess for a long time. The abscess would recur, filling up the space that I had emptied, becoming quite large; then I bandaged it and cauterized it inside the throat. Thus, it stopped growing, and I parted from these tasks, leaving God to complete the healing after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the retina detaches from the eye, and it is swollen and distant, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thin, round, and flat, it is called "retina.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have described in the previous section, but the treatment does not help, and you notice that the abscess is healing, and it has become smaller, it is then necessary to make a cut; and that which was round and swollen is now closer and not distant; and it is bloody or of a dark color, then be cautious when making an incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the ill patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see this, according to the manner I have said, take a clean and long cloth, and make the patient face the sun, pressing the tongue with the instrument we spoke of earlier; then insert the pin in the wound and pull it out, cutting it with one of the two instruments I mentioned for incising the mandrils.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is important that you do not remove more than the excess beyond the natural limit; for if you do, it grieves the voice and speech, and after the incision, use what we have said regarding incising the mandrils, and treat it as long as it remains clean.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient feels great pain, it is necessary that you use a tool for cauterizing the sensitive parts.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of cauterization is very hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place their head on a healthy surface and then press the tongue against the instrument described in the chapter on cauterization with hot, sharp forceps, neither too thick nor too thin; and by using this instrument, it takes the form of:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the physician hold a hair, as if it were a spoon's handle, and place the instrument with all the medicine on top of the eye; and have the patient lying on their side, so that the saliva and mucus from their mouth can drain the medicine without going down into the throat or causing pain. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it stop flowing and the pain from the medicine is eased; and if you notice, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, soak the cotton in the medicine, and twist the instrument through the cotton onto the surface of the eye, until the cotton sticks to the eye. Do this often, until the cauterization of the medicine is complete, then leave it to dry, and after three or four days, or even five, if you need to repeat the cauterization of the medicine, do so again, and after the cauterization, wipe around the eye with cotton soaked in fresh, cold water, and use gargles until the eye is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than cauterization, especially for incisions; if it is carried out through fumigation in this manner, take plenty of calament, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, and similar herbs, and mix them all together in a pot or any one of them separately, and place it there; make the pot well sealed with strong clay, and among the pot have a cheveit (tool) according to this manner.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	It should be of silver or gold, and one of the joints should be squeezed in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye becomes dry; after that, it often recurs as long as the eye is dry; be careful not to perform this at the beginning of a hot abscess, as many complications can arise; and do not perform this unless it is in the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, take a cane and insert a piece of cold iron into the mouth of the patient so that it is not too hot; for the cold iron does not allow the vapor to burn the mouth, and it is a good cure, together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a burning sensation occurs in the throat from bone or fishbone or some other thing; therefore, you must treat what you can see and press the tongue against the sun with all your tools until you see the thing move. And if it does not open and is stuck in the throat, you should make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the burning sensation will leave through vomiting. Or the patient may swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a piece of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread, and tie a thread to the sponge and then pass it; and when it reaches its place, if it gets stuck, pull strongly and extract it. And if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it can enter the throat more easily, and raise the head; beware not to touch the epiglottis, allowing it to fall back down; guide the patient in placing the instrument, for he must move it gently, as if something were open inside; when he swallows, let him swallow everything fully, until it is completely out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the mucus in the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No treatment should be given to the mucus, as I mentioned in the previous division, except with medicinal remedies; and if that does not help, then observe the throat of the patient at sunset, press the tongue with the instrument I have told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, pull it with all the small hooks or subtle pincers that are suitable for it.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if these are not suitable, take a horsehair and insert it into the throat of the patient, then pull or gently tug on the hair; do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has fever all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in headfirst, moving it with your hand often; and as soon as the wound feels the water, it will close.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not break as we have said, and the patient is filled with bad smell from the smoke of the herb mentioned in the fumigation of the eye, do this many times, for it will eventually break without warning.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The method of fumigation is as follows: you fill a pot with hot coals, cover it with a perforated lid, and place the instrument for fumigation in the perforations. Then pour your fumigation, and have the patient put the tip of the cane in their mouth and close their mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but goes directly to their lungs. The sputum should come up now, and if it doesn't, repeat the fumigation many times. Have the patient endure thirst and eat salty and bitter things, and do not let them drink water. Then it will be necessary for the sputum to come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the wound, if you can see it, resembles a curved claw that enters the throat; and it looks like a bird's beak, and has the roughness of lime, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; and here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many appearances of abscesses are, according to what is remembered from this book, and they differ in terms of perforation and size; and there are two ways: one that has the same appearance, and those that hold moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the upper part is different from that of the lower, and the abscess of the fleshy part of the limb is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if at the abscess one should not pierce while the bowel is still alive according to its completion; and if of such that it is necessary to pierce when they are thoroughly hardened, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are in the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	Because when an abscess comes from damaged joints, and it is left as long as it is rotten around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or if the abscess is in the principal member, and you delay piercing it while it is still alive, it will harm the principal member; or if it is in the foundation, pierce it likewise when it is still alive; and it is not advisable to pierce a firm abscess without completing digestion, except for that which is in the foundation, so that it does not rot completely, and becomes fistulous, and cannot heal thoroughly.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of perforation of the abscess which is deadly according to its completion, and this is when the pain is soothed, and the fever departs, and the pain and redness lessen, and the swelling and sharpness of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you must make the perforation depend on the location of the abscess, and where it opens; and it should be a long cut through the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in the joints and nerves and arteries, and everywhere equally, without any swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And for abscesses that are in soft flesh, it is better to leave the incision until it is completely healed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it too soon after this, the body will be filled with veins of blood, and it will be full of filth, and by chance, the lips may harden and become attached to it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if at any abscess that is pierced according to the thickness of the flesh, as needed by the member.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should treat small abscesses with small incisions; and for large ones, with large incisions and many cuts according to the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to press and cover, and when they have become as hard as a cloth, and are numb, then you should do as is done for blisters: and if there are such that are cut in three angles, and if there are such that are covered like the fleece of mirth, like the abscesses of enemies; and if there are such where a round size, and other sizes, and similar cuts are made.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	As for those who do not have a head, if the abscess is soft and superficial, you should puncture it thoroughly; and if the abscess is large, and has a strong bow, and you puncture it, do not drain all the pus at once, but only part of it; then bandage the abscess until the next day, and thereafter extract nothing from it again; repeat this process many times little by little until all the pus has drained. Especially in cases where the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old decrepits.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For sometimes the spirit jumps at the outcome of the bow, which might cause the patient to die, and you should not be alarmed by this.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Beware therefore of this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, if the wound is clean, and if it is a small abscess, apply a thin layer of linen or cotton; and if it is a large abscess with many openings, it is necessary to insert a bandage in each so that they touch one another; and if you have found in the abscess a part of hard skin, and you have closed it around, then fill it with old cotton or shreds of dry linen without moisture, and bind it for three days; then open it and apply treatment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the infection spreads to your work, then apply cold water and ice, moisten the bandage, and lay it on the affected area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the infection persists, apply a governance and cure, as well as the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter or the affected area is very sensitive, you should place moistened blankets and drapes on top of it; and if it is in a state where the flesh is firm, lay moistened drapes with cold wine and oil, or hot wine and oil, for up to three days, as we have said; then remove the abscess, wipe it, and cure it as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: for I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and now see this chapter.
des soros	from blood
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or there are many small abscesses that come from the heat of the head, and they are like threads, as well as the sinew of a chicken, and they have many similar appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are thick and such that have moisture as well as pulsation; and if there are any of these that are hard and resistant to cutting, then there is no doubt that the artery does not do anything contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the thigh is such that you should test all instruments called "intrusive" with which the following form is obtained, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they make a hole from above down long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, it withdraws without leaving any skin that contains the moisture, for it returns immediately if left alone; then immerse a cotton in Egyptian ointment if available; otherwise, use water and string, and apply to the wound, leaving it until the next day; and this will heal those who are delayed by night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the bandage again, as before, on the second day and third, until you know for certain that it does not stay during the night; then treat the wound with suitable medicine until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	If the abscess persists for a long time, following this form, drain it completely; then cut around it from all sides and apply every effort to draw out the pus from the wound where it lies; and if the artery reacts badly, do as I have told you.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Also, treat an abscess that is painful, and cut it and cure it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut the abscess first and moisten it if necessary; for it is filled with little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there is no moisture in any of these abscesses or swelling, and these are the abscesses I removed from an old woman's shoulder, I found the abscess as hard, sharp, and white as a stone, and it could not be crushed; and if anyone were to try to do so, they would cause just as much damage as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses occurring on the head or shoulder, those which come as a result of children's teething and at the roots of the ears, the opening should be kept completely open towards their closest position to allow the bowel to pass, and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess appears in the neck, and it discharges pus, and causes pain, and never comes elsewhere on the body, and it is full, and twisted together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly inside its ribcage, as we have said of the nodule and abscess on the head; and there are many appearances of these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others of a malicious nature that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that which you see of good disposition for touch, and it resembles the color of sound flesh, and is firm from every side and not hollow; then you must cut it from above, and scrape each part, and the two lips of the heart as we have said in the chapters on the head; and take it little by little, and be sure not to cut the nerve or vein, and do not make them too deep, so that the hand does not slip, and do not look too far ahead, lest you cut something you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work, apply vitriol or any powders that stop blood flow, and close the wound; leave it until the pain is relieved, and the wound becomes softer, and then begin to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is stained with blood, it returns to your work as long as you complete it; then pay attention to your expert judgment if no small scabs remain, if you clean and dress them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scab, it is not enough that you clean only that scab at its root, but tie it with a thick double thread and leave it hanging without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment and treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you clean the entire scab, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them now, so that there is no delay due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you need to understand how to deal with the root of it, and pull it out, and cut it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those scrofulas that have an excess, pierce them where they appear to be dying; and the piercing is done in the same way as mentioned before, then apply these remedies with bandages and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what remains from the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, continue the treatment with healing ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	squinance (n.) - squint or astigmat
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	They old ones spoke and discussed about the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and it is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with squint (cross-eye), it is important to avoid cutting the throat's fold, known as the "epiglottis"; one should not attempt this, because all the veins and the source of the patient's pain are located in those who have an abscess hot in their mouth, or in their throat, or in their windpipe.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the urethra's channel, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss caused by strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it in three circles or four small incisions across, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the incision, not touching the cartilage; and these cuts are very suitable for cutting through the epiglottis so that there is no obstruction, and the vessels are long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the masters are timid, it is necessary that they stretch the throat skin to the entire wound, then cut through the heart until it reaches the chain; and avoid blood vessels, if you see anything, and then remove the obstruction, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by cutting the river of the chain that goes out from the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and there is doubt about the strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound towards the heart, and cut through all the way to the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote healing, as long as it remains healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says: One should not proceed with this until the throat is completely closed, and the patient is considered dead, lacking all breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then, they should cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, thus preventing death; and for this reason, the ancients ordered that the wound be left open as long as the evil of the illness persists, which takes three or four days. And then they commanded to close the wound and dress it, as long as it was healing; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a damsel took a knife, and stabbed it in her throat, and cut part of the channel of her womb; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was coming from it, and realized that it had no power or passage to the outside other than through the throat, and the veins were emerging from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I acted quickly, sewed up the wound, and cured her until she was healthy; and she could not speak for fear, but later recovered her voice and returned to normal; that is why I say that one should have no fear of working near the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	from the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cystic abscesses are called "throat hernias," and they are large abscesses in the color of a thorn, and they affect women mostly; and they occur in two manners: natural and accidental, or naturally without any cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental condition occurs in two manners: one is similar to fat, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that arises from an artery; it causes fear, and it is not advisable to make incisions except on a small area, testing and exploring every opening: if you find it just like fat and it cannot be moved, cutting it off as we cut our fingers, and treating it with all care until it heals perfectly.
des nous	From us.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways in which we differ, and I will describe all their similarities; now it is necessary that I explain the entire distinction between us and our origins.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that origins are hot and feverish as long as the ebullition persists, and once the putrefaction is complete, then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains satisfaction, which is its own sac and according to the condition of the body, and begins like a seed, and becomes large; and they are according to two similarities, either fatty or moist, and very much in color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You should, when you approach the treatment of a new patient, that you test and inquire first about all the instrument called "entangling" (entromissoire), according to its form as it appears in this chapter or the following one.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	The method of inquiring about abscesses is that you press more or less moistily on the abscess, and turn your fingers in and out, as long as you know that the instrument has pierced the center, then do it according to the size of the abscess; then extract the entangler (entromissoire), and be careful not to slip.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture runs in the cut, and it changes its color as I have described for other abscesses, and after introducing moisture, it does not come out, knowing that it is filled with pus, then make a cross-cut, and take it as pincers, scraping it gently from each side, and protect the wound where it lies so you draw it healthy with new (bandages); and if you cannot draw it healthy, cut it into pieces so nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing remains, it returns to the body many times; and if a little remains, without causing great pain, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, tighten the wound, place hot poultices on the abscess, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed; and if it is large, cut both edges of the wound, and treat it from those who cause harm.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the pain persists against you or other things, use quickly and thoroughly the vitriol ground, and leave it for two or three days until the wound heals, and the blood flow stops; then return to cover what had been dislocated from new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Behold the shapes of the instruments that enter, and they are of three types: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret", and one called "breb", and these are also in three sizes: large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistulas; and they are similar to the needles with which spells are cast, and are made of brass, iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more effective for enclosing the corbs of fistulas; and these are also in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the opening.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the joints are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and also joints with two curves in three ways; and joints with three curves, equally in three ways; and joints with two curves, or just one curve, in three ways; and all these are necessary for their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The tool used for this purpose should be sharp, and there are some that do not cut well from one side only, causing the skin to be torn, preventing the cutting of veins or nerves; these are called scissors, which, when properly used, do not let the patient feel the opening of the abscesses; they come in three sizes: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they should only be used on fleshy parts like legs, arms, mammary glands, wounds, and similar areas; never use a smaller tool resembling a finger splint according to this form to stop the flow of blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it never rests in its place which is beneficial for veins, arteries, and always returns according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never swell the breasts of any man when they begin to be corrupted, as long as they look like women's breasts; they remain ugly and swollen, and anyone who wants to cure them should do so according to this form from this line b until g.
