puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and apply medicinal poultices with charcoal, then bring together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it as long as it is healthy; if the breast inclines downward, and becomes softened because of its size, just as in women, making two cuts above and below, through which one edge holds onto the other at the end of each, so that the longest line contains the smallest according to this form from this line b until g. Then scrape off the skin between the two edges, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for treatment, as long as it heals; and if it does not heal, or the incision has not been completely made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood stagnation, then you should fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive dressing; leave it until it absorbs the grease and fat, then treat it as long as it heals.
des apostemes des asselles	from the abscesses of armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are hard scrofula or have nodules, and if they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line B to line G.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, apply old cotton to the wound and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with suitable dressing until it heals.

And if the abscess resembles scrofula, then do as we have said for cutting out scrofula, and if the wound sinks in, apply cautery as we have mentioned before.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When an artery bursts and the flesh above it heals over, many abscesses often form, and this also happens in a swollen vein with an abscess; and if you recognize it for an arterial rupture, the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it at your fingers, it feels strange; and in the case of a vein, it appears red and bulging; and it is foolish to attempt to treat this abscess, especially when it is deeply embedded among tissues, and with thorns and snakes, or in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should seek iron cautery, and for one who is at the head, likewise, and on whoever has an artery opening from above the skin along; then make an incision as often as necessary, and carefully extract the artery with a double thread in two parts, just as I taught you about the extraction of the two arteries in the temples; then mark the space between the two threads with an instrument until there is no remaining pus, and release the abscess; then apply the treatment that seems best while the wound is fresh; then treat any subsequent care as appropriate, until it heals; and if the abscess is located alongside a vein, hold your hand over it, and carefully pierce it with a needle, making a double thread, so you can pull from the other side; then bind the abscess, as I told you, to one of its parts with the thread; and if you doubt that the thread has come loose, push another needle through all the remaining part below the first incision, and tie the threads in three places; then cut away the surplus portion until only what is left is bound; then cover it with a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, and apply treatments and dressings as needed until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	Of the abscesses of nails
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, so too do they appear in nails when they are damaged or subjected to excessive strain, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this occurs more often in joints and all limbs where there are joints, which is a source of great abscesses, and their appearance seems to be the color of the flesh, and they take on various shapes with pain; and when they are pressed, the patient feels great pain, and it is not fully healed within the body, but remains close to the heart; and it moves from all sides, neither advancing nor retreating, neither below nor above, and the one in the joints should not be covered with iron: perhaps it would cause contraction; and the one at the head or forehead makes the skin contract.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, and it has a point, then with tweezers, remove it at its base; and if it is large, suspend it on a hook, and then scrape off the skin, then cut out the flesh and sew up the wound, and apply the cure until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	Des grosses boces pendans" translates directly to "pendant large mouths
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	It never appears in the belly alone, but is a disease called "fungus" due to its appearance, it has subtle roots, and large droppings; it also includes small and large worms. I have seen people with two or more funguses in their bellies that were more similar to each other than to anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, had fine roots, were deeply split, and constantly exuded moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. quant li boude ist fuer	When the bowel is blocked.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the bowel comes from cauterization of a wound or fissure in the colon, and is located in the stomach and not in any of the bowels, as it happens with other ruptures, or bleeding from veins or arteries according to what is above, or flatulence; and if it is due to rupture through the wall of the colon and through the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and it is a slight thing without pain, and opens up in various ways.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to an intestinal issue, then it is more diverse, and when pressed by the fingers at its opening, it returns, and sometimes becomes constricted, greatly expanding at the bath entrance or through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light issue, and it opens easily when pressed by the hand, not constrained; and if it is due to blood, it appears through these signs: a large and hard abscess, fixed according to its quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it feels soft upon touching, and the severity is such that you must observe its appearance, whether it is the blood of an artery, a vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary, you must leave the cure.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter about abscesses, both for the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if there is an appearance of the intestine or bowels, it is necessary that you command the patient to retain their excrement, and be completely stretched out straight, then tie around everything close to the wound; then command them to lie still between your hands, then stretch half of the abscess above all the large hook; then bind it with a strong thread or firm silk string, making sure the wound is entirely closed; then open half of the abscess that is stretched over the string and insert your index finger, exploring the intestine; if you find it bound by the string, untie it and bring out the intestine from outside the abdomen; and if you find the bowels, take them at the hook and remove the excess; and if the artery or vein causes obstruction, gently go around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two strong threads, threading the needles as you made holes; then pull the abscess in four parts over the needles, and if you see any remains, remove the needles and leave the wound to heal, cutting off any dead flesh itself; or you can remove it when it becomes soft and rotten, then treat the wound as necessary, and finish the abscess as we have said; and drain the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound accordingly, and sew up the wound.
dou chancre	The first sentence translated from Old French to English is
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the appearances of cancer and how it should be treated with medicines, and how to avoid the cure of iron; and we say that cancer spreads in the body, requiring great caution in its treatment, and the ancients advised that when cancer is in a part that can be cut out, like the breast or thigh, or in similar places, it must all be removed as soon as it appears; but for large and old cancers, one should not even approach them, because I have never seen anyone heal from them; no one has ever healed from them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for the work, when it is in place or can be removed, as we have said, it is that you remove the black blood from the patient at any time; then make it healthy if there is a clear sign of filling, and cut out the malady in a good place to perform the work; then apply your ointments or ulcers, and wash all parts, and draw out all bones without leaving anything; let the blood flow out completely, and feel the place with your hand or any object, and if the occurrence of blood makes the incision of the artery or vein contrary, cauterize it until the wound is cleansed; then treat it with another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	The term "dydropisie" appears to be a
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed the symptoms of hydrops and how the collection of fluid is formed, as well as the signs of each condition, and the treatment using medicine or iron; in these two cases, it is only through medication. One should not use iron on these two conditions: namely, tympanitis and yposarche, as they are deadly. Therefore, when treating this hydrops condition, which is called "eclites" with medicine, and the cure does not work, consider if the patient is weak or has another illness besides hydrops, such as stomach upset or similar; in these cases, do not use iron, for there is doubt. And if you see the patient is of strong constitution and has only hydrops without other illnesses, and is neither too young nor too old, then proceed thus: lay the patient gently on your hands, and ask a helper to press the abdomen towards the lowest part with water, then take the sharp spatula according to this form.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And make incisions from both parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Insert the point, but do not push it too deep so that it reaches the intestines when inserted, and do not break through; then observe if there is any droplet formation towards the intestines. You should make your incision three fingers' depth directly under the breastbone on the left side if there is a buildup due to liver disease; and if it is due to a bloating of the bowels, make the incision on the right side, but do not let the patient lie on the incision to prevent any excess fluid from flowing towards the weak part. Then pierce through all the skin with your instrument, and the flesh, and gently press your hand on all the pus between the skin and the muscle as if you were peeling it; when the pus reaches a depth of eight parts (as deep as a fingernail or so), pierce the muscle, which is the water-sign, then pull out the instrument, and this is the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a thin silver chain, and is of fine steel or iron, and has in each side a small opening; on one side three openings, and two on the other, and one on the third; and the end is cut like a feather, which is the shape of the incision that scribes make when they cut feathers.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of it is the opening, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it sinks immediately onto the instrument; then empty half or a third of it, for if you empty more than is necessary at that moment, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit into the weapon, or he may lose his palm, or approach death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue in the patient indicate, and his pulses; then take the instrument and hold back the water, and it is now held back by the stop that blocks the opening I mentioned, which you pierce in this way; then repeat the instrument on the other side, if you see the patient suffering, and draw out a small amount of water; do this for one day, and be careful not to allow any more water to remain but just a little.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave much water, whether through the cure of a grave or hot sand, or through sweating or a bath or in the sun, and he becomes thirsty; and treat with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after draining the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	from the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born who does not have an opening in the penis, or if the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary for him not to pierce through all the very subtle spatium according to this form,
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then open the subtle channel of the bladder, and hold it closed for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the closure, let him urinate, and then replace it; however, in some cases, this is not necessary, because the force of the urine will not allow it to remain closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening is small, it is a sign of a weak bladder closure, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the fracture in their place are crippled, for no one is born with a fracture at the top of the bone, so they cannot urinate until they raise their bone up; and they cannot procreate because the matter cannot come down to the marrow, and it is a great illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies on their back, then the top of the bone and its head are also as thin as a quill, so that the fracture can be set correctly; and beware of the discharge of blood which comes many times, and if it happens, stop the bleeding with what stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	from the pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often, this ulcer appears on the penis, and it has an unappealing appearance; there are both benign and malignant ones. You must press them gently with a subtle incision, drain them, and clean and dress them with moist cotton in Egyptian ointment. Then continue to treat the wound with diaphoretic ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, with putrid color and odor, it requires cautery treatment.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have achieved it, and if the splint is in a tight knot, with part of it inside the skin and part of it outside, then it is necessary to remove the splint that is inside first; and once it is loose, then treat the part that is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, unless you are certain of the position of the splint, it can become damaged and lead to discoloration and rot in the wood, so it is necessary to remove all that is black and rotten, then cover it with an ointment made from honey and flour, prepared from red apple bark and leaves, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a feverish event occurs, then administer the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery is of great help in two dispositions: that is to say, in the case of fever and corruption; and if the part of the penis is corrupt and withdrawn, then it is necessary that you insert or apply a plug to the penis and make the patient urinate; and when the hair on the head of the penis is dry for those who have not been circumcised, or there is an ulcer or abscess, in this case, therefore, it is necessary that you scrape it with a sharp instrument until the ties are loosened and the parts around the penis are relieved; and if it is a difficult thing to decide, then scrape it gently from the top of the penis and the scrotum with any tool, and then carefully separate them, and place a thin, moist linen cloth soaked in cold water over the area directly.
de la circoncision	On circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a dislocation of the continuation like other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our will, especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best and most gentle operation for their healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they do not practice it in their laws, and we have acquired knowledge of it only through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have observed most of the masters and elders who perform circumcision in the presence of force, and at all times with a fresh cut; if it were according to custom, as there are two layers, and perhaps one removes this one and delays that one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or she returns with the wound still open, and the pain is doubled, and the point of the limb is not certain; and in the cleaning of a nail, by chance, the iron escapes, and it corrupts the work, and often they heal in such a way that no further cleaning is needed and I wish it so.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the cleaning that is done with force on every link of thread, I have found the benefit of experience, because the forces cut exactly as well from above as from below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, if you cut evenly in all directions; but the thread should be well twisted around the skin; and it is important that at the first attempt you make the child think that you are only gently tying the thread around the stick, and then let him struggle in every way that you can. Then twist it between your hands straight, and press the forces between your fingers or toes so that the infant does not see them, nor any of the tools. Then press your hand against the stick and blow in its heart, and pull it up until the end of the stick is free; then clean it well of all the dirt that is stuck to it, tie the joint with a double thread, and bind it to another thread; and hold it in place on both sides with the second binding at the pocket and the index finger. Cut between the two threads, then lift the heart gently from above, pull the stick's head; let the blood flow little by little, for that is how it heals. Then apply powder and cover it with a gluey cloth made of half-boiled egg mixed with rose water, preserved with good rosin oil and fresh herbs, and leave it until the next day, and treat it differently each day until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of purification is as follows: both shoulders should be held still and cut, and the shoulder blades should also be large and equally sized.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in purification occurs when the veins inside are not cut properly; then you must extend your finger to reach them, so they do not form an abscess; and do the same for the other one, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, use tweezers, and then continue.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they exceed three days, and the skin under the arrow is swollen, leave it until the abscess has healed, gently peeling off the crust; continue to press on it as you can, and protect the part of the arrow, for it will not harm anything.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the wound suddenly from gunpowder, which we have spoken of in treating of powders, and if one applies too much heart, it will go above, and cause no harm; treat it then, as we have said, while it is still whole.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to a stone, or frozen blood, or bowels, or a deformed kidney, or similar conditions, as we have discussed in the previous section; and if the urine cannot be released, and you observe that the retention is caused by a stone in the bladder or at the neck of the bladder, it is necessary for the patient to be bent over his knees; pressure should then be applied to his lower back, and he should stretch his belly upwards from the region above his back, and constrict the patient as much as possible. This will force the neck of the bladder against the stone positioned above, allowing the urine to flow. If this does not happen, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it is then necessary to administer extraction to all instruments called "syringes", which are shaped like a bird's feather, with a length of about 12 inches.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method for urination is as follows: Take a double thread and tie one end with wool or cotton around the head of the syringe; pull the thread inside the syringe and cut off the excess wool, leaving it up to the top of the syringe. Then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk and place the patient on a seat with a moistened urethra pipe made of oil and olive oil and tepid water. Gently insert the syringe into the urethra until it reaches the root of the pipe, then double the pipe over the tip. Remove the syringe before the bladder is completely emptied, and feel the patient urinate until all the contents are out; do not be concerned if the thread follows the direction in which it was inserted, as pulling on it will help empty the bladder. Continue to use the syringe until the bladder is completely empty, easing the patient's discomfort.
des maladies de la vessie	From the diseases of the bladder.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or inflammation come to the bladder, due to an accumulation of putrefaction, you should draw out water and medicines using a device called a "clepsydra", and it is shaped as follows:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and the cheeks with which the medicine must be applied are shaped to effectively burn the urethra without additional damage, if possible, so that the moisture can be drawn out and expelled as needed. When you pour your medicines into the bladder, place the head of the container in the moisture and draw it out gently; then, forcefully push back the tube that is attached. The moisture will enter the vessel now, directly reaching the bladder, which the patient will feel. This is the form of a subtle enema by which one purges the bladder. It looks like this:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or gold, and the joint is higher; then dislocate it from the breast where the ligament breaks; take a sheep bladder and fill it with the moisture you wish to use for enema; tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat the moisture over the fire; insert the tip of the enema into the anus, then press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture reaches the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle, pierce it around, then insert a strong thread through these holes, assemble the circle as one would a dal, and place inside oil, moisture, and water, tie it with the instrument, and press your hand as you did with the bladder until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed the methods for dealing with stones and their extraction, along with various medicinal approaches; I outlined the distinction between calculi that are in the kidneys, and all the signs, and what kind of stone requires surgical intervention; and also regarding the bladder and urethra. I will now explain these matters clearly and concisely.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is in the bladder occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign of acute urinary tract infection, similar to water in its subtlety; it opens the way for the patient's pain, greatly irritating their urethra, and often causing them to urinate frequently, creating sediment; and these infections lay the foundations. The cure is lighter for children under four years old, but more difficult for those between youth and old age; the treatment is milder for those with large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient through a cleanse, in order to draw out all impurities from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often obstructs the effort to cut into stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and straighten them up and move them to the bottom, so that the stone descends to the full extent of the bladder, without moving upwards; then place the patient between your hands with their feet down, so that the bladder is completely inclined downwards; then tie them up and touch them inside; if you feel the stone in the space, now hasten to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out at the touch, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, and if the patient is older, use your middle finger; press firmly into its base, grasp the stone, and when you feel it on your side, near the bladder's neck; then press down with your finger, and push the stone out through the opening where you see the chafing.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the helper to press the bladder with their hand, and command them to stretch their right hand above, and with their left hand, remove the skin covering the stones in the area where the incision is made; then use the spoon-shaped tool to complete the procedure.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make an incision between the scrotum and the base, not in the middle but on the side of the left navel; let it be straight on the stone, and your two legs should be either on the base or above it, and cut across so that it is wide enough to allow for expansion, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure from the stone at the base will cause it to come out without effort; know that there are stones with angles and margins, so be careful when they try to emerge; and if they are on top, resembling a glans or pearl, and round, then their emission is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If there are angles and margins, make the incision larger; if it does not come out, you need to use pliers that are also like a lime at the top to extract the stone so that it does not escape; or you can insert a small, curved instrument at the top; and if you cannot do it this way, then enlarge the opening slightly, and if it is without a sac, extract it with vitriole; and if there are more than one stones, first remove the largest one from the neck of the bladder, then cut, and pull out the others afterwards.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, they want to pull it out, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things can happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine returns immediately through the wound that the limbs cannot heal; but nevertheless, strive hard to extract it, either with pincers or by removing debris, as long as you treat it in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply incense, aloe, and dragon's blood to the wound, tighten it, and place a moist cloth made of oil and wine, or oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then bind the patient tightly on his chest, and do not untie the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, if a lot of warm oil and water comes out, then apply healing ointment and basilic treatment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corrosions occur in the wound, and congelations of blood in the bladder, and it retains urine, which is known to happen without hesitation with the urine: then press your finger into the wound and extract the blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder and cause putrefaction; then clean the wound with water and herbs, and aid it in every way that you know, until it heals; and it is necessary that during all treatments, you bind both thighs together and apply medicines to the joint.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small and can be passed with a stick, and driven in deeply, so that urine cannot pass; then the treatment of what I say is such that you cut it many times, and this excision is an excuse for the cutting.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have tested this myself.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take the iron at the front according to this form, and fix it at three angles in one stick.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the stick next to the stone so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then gently push the iron into the stone until it reaches it; and pull the iron out of the stone little by little, as much as you can pierce the stone from another side; soon urine will come out, and press your hand on what is remaining of the stone inside the stick.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is often broken and jumps with urine, and hurts the patient; and if you cannot do this for any reason that defies you, then take a needle and thread, and sew the stone from below and above, then pull it out forcefully, and loosen the bond, and cleanse the frozen blood in the wound; and treat until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the women's stone" (referring to kidney stones)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is rare for women to have stones, and when they do, the cure is difficult, and it is hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; the second is that it is not easy to find a woman with sufficient knowledge who can uncover the wound, especially if she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. And the third way is that, by chance, one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art of midwifery; and the fourth way is that the womb of a woman is more sensitive than that of a man, so it needs to be cut deeper, and there is great fear involved. If necessity arises, you should enlist the help of a wise midwife, scarcely ever a laywoman, and if you cannot find one, then don't hesitate to use a clever device; present her with a toy well-crafted in the ways of women's lives, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you instruct her regarding the examination of the womb. And take great care that she is a virgin woman: then she must insert her finger into the vagina deep enough to grasp the womb, and should constrict it down onto the sick person's hand, and recommend that she inserts her left hand on top of the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she feels it, she must move it little by little from the entrance of the bladder down to the thigh, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then chop into the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle towards the inside, where it is moved and inserted, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her leg above or below the stone, and make the incision first small. Then twist the right in the thigh, if you feel the stone so deep in the wound that the stone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and with points.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	knowing these similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the wound does not heal, put crushed vitriol on it and keep it there for an hour until the wound is cleansed; then return to your work while the stone is still hard, and have the tools I told you for removing stones from humans to assist you in your task; and if the wound does not heal, and it's an artery that's cut, sprinkle powder on the area and press with tenes and bends, and do not repeat this, leaving the stone and not pulling it, unless by chance the patient were to die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the eyes open, return to your work while the stone is still hard.
de hernie carnouse	from herniated cartilage
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse (hernia) is nothing other than the gathering of moisture or white substance, which is detached from the heart of the organs, containing the egg white, and it is called "syfac", never properly part of the egg white itself; and this is the thin skin of the organ between the white substance that we have mentioned; and this does not occur naturally.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is due to weakness in the organs, and this material expands.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never does it come from percussion on the joints, and this moisture takes many forms: it can be yellowish, or without redness, or black, or white water, and so on; and these are signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is white as we have said, then the abscesses are bright, quite long like the shape of an egg, and do not open the joints, because they are filled with moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, then the abscesses are bright with part of an egg, and one might think it's another abscess; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white, then it smells well; so when you want to know the color of the moisture, examine all the affected area as we have described.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what follows then, after the introduction, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to their ability and the completion of their body; then place them on their back, on something slightly raised, and put many sheets under them; then have them sit on their left side, and command the assistant to sit on their right, and extend the staff towards one of the two ribs near the heart; then take the scalpel, and cut through the skin of the ribcage from top to bottom down to the elbow, and make the incision entirely straight by examining the skin of the ribcage until it turns white, and carefully remove the skin according to the patient's ability; then make a large perforation in the scarred tissue with water at an angle, and extract all the water, and then apply bandages, and pull the scarred tissue upwards; and do not touch the heart of the ribs, but only the scarred tissue; cut around it carefully, as finely as possible, that if you do not cut it cleanly, the water will return; and if the effusion has ceased to your satisfaction, then put it back in its place when you have completed the work with the scarred tissue; then join the two ribs of the heart with a stitch, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the heart corrupted by another illness, it is necessary that you hold the vessels that are suspended, fearing the flow of blood; then cut off the clot from the entire suspension, and treat the heart as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the blood is collected in two parts, knowing that these are the branches, cut off the other part just as you did with the first, then dry the wound, and apply a clean bandage moistened with rose oil; and place another clean bandage moistened with wine and oil, and wrap the two knots, and cover them with double-lined cloth, and tie it securely to all the ties according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two strips of cloth, made from shredded wool according to this likeness, and join them together with stitching in the gusset of the breeches; one strip should be sewn to the base, reaching up to the back, and the other to the bend of the finger; and the third on top of both, gathering the restriction at the loop of the breeches. And the doctor, in every way you can, should make sure everything is stretched out; and be careful that the fire does not touch the wound; and know that this work is safer; and move gently with the cutting of veins, and pull without causing complications from abscesses or other issues; and if anything goes against you, whether it's an abscess or any other complication, treat what is going against you as mentioned above.

de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the hairs
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	You know that in this chapter there are various adverse conditions, which is why I think it is better to leave it alone; and I will tell you about the work and appearances of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I therefore say that many abscesses occur in the body, and especially in the hairs; and this is the case in most instances.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is known from the excessive acrid and bitter fluid that flows from the hairs, or through percussion; and the color of the abscess matches the color of the skin; it does not cause pain, and is a deep abscess; and sometimes there are multiple abscesses that are hard, painful, and dark in color, or of a bright red hue, and they do not originate from any new artery or vein inflammation.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches. de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the cowls
