de la routure dou syfac	from the rupture of the sinew
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The treatment of this condition involves incising the tissue where the rupture has occurred, or extending it on the abdomen in the region of the angles, so that the intestines descend from this rupture to one of the openings; and this rupture is either due to section (incision) or extension, and these two methods have very similar causes: percussion, a jump, shouting, lifting a heavy weight, and similar actions; and the signs when it is due to extension include gradual occurrence over a long period, without sudden onset, and the abscess is evenly distributed up to the very edge because the rupture pushes the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the incision that it brings a sudden pain to the start, and various abscesses appear beneath the skin close by, and this is due to the exit of the intestine and the flesh from the force of the incision.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never remove the bandages with the intestines still inside, as they are trapped and cause great pain to the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, which are dangerous, it is important to be cautious.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of the procedure is that you command the patient to straighten the intestine in their hand within the wound if it can be done; then remember it on their collarbone between your hands and ease the hips; then stretch the heart above, and cut all the flesh from the bones along; then insert the fingers into the spaces of the groin according to what you need to open the wound, and make sure they can go through; then remove the skin that is under the hard white flesh until all the white flesh is fully exposed from all sides; then with your index finger, take hold of what follows the flesh, between the white flesh which is under the skin of the groin, and the second flesh, and separate what is behind the groin, and between the second flesh; afterward, with your right hand, take hold within the heart of the flesh, and place the white flesh above in your left hand, and ease the bone towards the tail; and command the assistant to stretch the bone upward, and loosen what is behind the ligament; and if there is no sign of intestine or hard white flesh, put it into the belly under the skin; then take a needle with a thick thread made from X threads, and insert it in the rear part of the flesh, after the skin of the groin; then cut off the parts that appear with the threads, as long as there are IIII threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the form of a cross, and tie the flesh, which we have said is under the skin of the groin, with a strong thread from both sides; then wrap the parts with threads, and tie them so that no vessels that nourish them can enter inside, nor come out; then put the thread according to the first long thread on both sides, and after these two threads, leave the flesh which is under the heart of the groin, a palm's length from it; and afterward, do the same as with the other parts, according to the shape that the bone takes. Then cut off the part that is under the skin of the groin, until it is smooth, and bow it, as we have said before; then apply moist wool to the wounds, and put on the thread that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never should the white part be cauterized after incision, out of fear of bloodletting.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, leaving the wound open until it heals on its own; and if it takes time to close, apply hot water as we have said, until it heals completely; then treat the wound with other remedies, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	herniated cartilage
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this condition, never have I seen anyone dare to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients say that it is made like a root that is gathered together in a knot, in such a way that you bind the vessels after cutting them slightly beneath the skin; then cut through its middle and treat the abscess of him who opens it, as long as the vessels are intact; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No rupture should occur from the attack of enemies, as we have said, and open the vessels; and no part of the intestines should protrude through the openings, and if it does, it is dangerous, and you must repair them every hour; but if it persists for too long at this point, it may become a wound or abscess, until the intestines protrude; and this happens due to the extension of the syphac that is present in the enemy, as it becomes stretched then softened and swelled, opening the vessels; and its cure is through cautery, as we have previously said; and never should it be treated with iron in this manner. And so, the patient should lie on his back with his hands beneath him, then cut the vessel of the rupture deeply according to the quantity of three fingers; next, extract the syphac that is below the skin, take a sharp instrument, and place it over the visible part of the syphac; press firmly into the abdomen, then cut the two visible parts of the syphac at the base of the instrument, and sew them shut; then remove the instrument, and do not allow the syphac or any other thing to protrude or extend, as I have told you in the cure for the intestines; then treat it with wound care.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you treat the wounds, if they become infected and the wound is healthy, then...
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The treatment is difficult, and it has no appearance in the rupture, but the cauterization moves in this place, and it is closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the hard skin
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the veins becomes softened in no one's body because the substances inside them are mollified, and it is easy to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, to lay the patient on his back and cut the skin that is mollified on the natural skin; then join the two edges with a stitch, and if you see that the excess of softened skin remains, cut it off with three or four stitches firmly; then cure it like other wounds as long as it is healed, and pull out the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You know that castration is forbidden by our law, and for that reason I would not speak of it in this book; however, there are two reasons why it is necessary: one is that he should be able to answer knowledgeably when asked about it, and the cure as well; the other, because we often need castration of certain animals to aid us, such as a goat, sheep, cat, or other creatures.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say, therefore, that castration is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method where we perform castration by attraction, we should keep the animal in hot water until the testicles are softened and relaxed; then, with your hand, press them until they return to their normal state and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the operation of castration: You must tie the animal and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory and cut each one separately when you have well lacerated them; leave no drop of blood or subtle blood that is on the vessels; this method of castration is more effective than the one done by attraction, because in attraction, perhaps something from the testicles remains, causing the animal to desire lust; then treat the wound until it is clean.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	A hermaphrodite is according to two manners in men: one is that between the two testicles opens up also like the figure of a woman's nature, where it has hair, and never cuts short when urinating.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And for women, it is also like this, having on the breastbone as well as a rod and two points.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for hunger and thirst is that you loosen all constricted openings, and treat it like any other wound; in a second way, for men whose urine flows through the skin of their penis, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the goiter
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Goiter is a constricted opening on the natural part, so severe that it is hard to see; no woman can move it as much as a hand, and this is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should hold the excess of the tendon in your hand or fingers and cut it gently; do not cut too deeply, to prevent bloodletting complications, until it is healed; and for another condition that appears at the mouth of a wound, and its use, and perhaps jumps out, and resembles a cow, and for this reason they call it in olden times "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you cut it, as we have said about the tendon, and heal it until it is sane.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erroneous is the diagnosis when one does not fully understand the nature of women, or the wound is small; it arises from nature at birth, or from accidents due to disease that has come upon them; or from an ill-fitting garment, or some subtle or specific cause, and it affects the whole body, in the womb, or on the side, or under the skin, or wherever it may be; and it must be understood for conception, childbirth, and perhaps even the flowers of life; and knowledge of such things is through observation of the body.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the symptoms are immediately apparent, whether it is due to your own actions or by chance.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a soft and delicate substance, close to the veins, act quickly: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then form both hands into fists, until the soft and delicate substance is completely enveloped, and the pressure point is reached; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it over the affected area, having the woman lie down each day so she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the substance is hard and thick, it is necessary that you cut it with a scalpel resembling a sprig of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is from heat, then suspend it with a bandage and a compress; have the medicines that stop blood flow, such as aloe, dragon's blood, incense, together with plenty of egg; then apply a wide plaster so that the wound cannot close; and thus for a long time, apply a dry linen cloth; and then use other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when fever comes from heat, it should be treated in this manner, especially if there are abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For abscesses that are aggravated during fever, they should not be prodded or touched to drain them.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that, without proper treatment, can become chronic. In the previous section, we discussed the signs and symptoms, and I will now describe those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and their complications, when they are completely in the anus, and they do not appear to be felt, can only be cured properly with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the anus can be felt; these are the ones that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then stretch her limbs with pliers and compress them at their roots, then powder medicines to stop blood, such as ginger and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water. And as the blood comes, let it rest in a decoction of sumac and bark from pomegranates and galls and similar things, and then take rye flour, and confit it with honey and wax, and make an emplaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if she is tired, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If this is not done, make the patient breathe with bellows on their back and to the breasts without causing harm; then take cloth, and soak it in juice of plantain or juglans with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has subsided, continue the treatment with medicine as long as it is healthy; and that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles a rough head, so it should be covered as I have said in the previous text; then treat it until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	about abscesses in childbirth
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the body, such as chancres and previous abscesses, herpes, boils, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, in this treatment, we must address the hot abscess that occurs in the body, which is not like other abscesses that cling; and if you are skilled in the work of fire, consider whether the abscesses are aggressive at the beginning of their appearance, filled with heat and fever, and turn red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not rush to pierce, but make the patient suffer as long as the pain is relieved; then place the patient in a reclined position with two small pillows under his legs, supporting him on his back, and bringing his feet towards the head of the bed, away from the affected limb. Spread the patient's hips, put his arms below his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage. Then suck the abscess from the right side, and insert the instrument used to open the abscess; with this, the shape will be revealed. And when you insert this instrument, remember to pierce it first to know the depth of the abscess, so that what enters does not go deeper than necessary, causing injury to the patient; if the instrument is too large, cover the bottom of the abscess with cloth so that the instrument does not hurt the patient. Put the tip of the instrument on top and secure it.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens and they make it with their hands gently, if necessary to cover with a cloth, take a spatule; and when the bowel is empty, it is necessary to put into the wound moist tents of rose oil or dry green oil; and place the tent completely over the wound at the edge of the scar, and then put on top of the scar and over the joint a clean moistened linen cloth with cooked mulberries or alder roots; after this care for two days of treatment coming to it, as long as it is healed; and never raise the scar and the wound by a cleansing of water and honey, and then water or boiled lily roots and alder bark; and then return to dressing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed in the inflammation, it is necessary that you be careful about applying heat, but treat it as we have said in the previous section.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The art of midwifery is first and foremost to know the signs of natural childbirth, and these are when you see a woman struggling downward, and she has an intense desire to push: then the child should be born immediately. At this point, you understand that these children come according to nature, their heads leading the way, and they are followed by the rest of the body; and whenever you observe these signs, it is necessary to gently press on her belly, so that the child is born quickly. For when it descends onto her pelvis, she follows with it, and the birth canal clears itself of excess blood through good cleansing; and this is how natural childbirth occurs, whereas otherwise, it does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes upon his feet no less often, and affects the flesh or the joint, or the hands, or his belly, or his back, and turns by chance onto his neck, and in other evil forms; so it is necessary for the surgeon to be wise and cunning in these matters, and to avoid errors and misfortunes, and I will show you all the forms how he should aid them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the evil comes upon his head by natural cause, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, then she should be placed on a saddle, or held by other women; and take some oil of fennel or fenugreek cooked, and then apply the small spatula in the shape mentioned between her two fingers.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut through the second joint, and saw off the finger as far as the moisture that is inside; and press the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, it is necessary to give the woman a enema with fennel seed musk and oil of sesame; then make her press and sneeze from the condition, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands are stuck, it is necessary to reset them slightly at a time; and if they cannot enter, put the woman on a chair and raise her feet up; then remove the chair from the ground and lay the woman down, so she does not try to stand up; and if the hands still cannot enter and the child is dead, cut off the hand at the joint closest to the body, take out the child, and reset it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the birth of the child on his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child is born on his feet, he needs to be pushed up; then he is turned little by little until he is even; then press on the feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	He can jump up to his ankles if he is commanded to press, and the limb extends completely; if he jumps higher, God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not happen as we have said, he should turn him little by little according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes slightly lighter.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come as we have said, take some musk, and oil of rose petals, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; apply this mixture to the female nature both inside and outside, then let her sit in warm water down to the ribs; when she is moistened, make a collar of myrrh and place it around her, leave it for an hour; then have her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze, press her mouth and nose, gently massage her belly, as the child now moves.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the passage of the child through its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child arrives in this condition, he moves his hands little by little; then lies on his back with his feet hanging down, and lies on his side; then folds his hands little by little, takes hold of his hands on his stomach, removes the cushions from beneath him until he is fully extended downwards; if the child does not move, takes his feet and moves them, then moves his stomach upwards, then pushes his hands away; and thus delivers the child little by little; and tells the woman to press herself down as long as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the birth of the child who comes with a large hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I know how to bring the hand back: if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman rise and walk; if she cannot walk, place her on a bed and straighten her legs; then administer the musk (or ointment) that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on a chair, then try to bring the hand back; deliver the child according to its natural position, make it sneeze, and command it to strain until the baby is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on its chest, with its hands spread and its face turned away from its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I want the patient to hold his hand, then twist it little by little and gently; and when it is even, he should apply a light, muscley compress of wool and oil, as we have said, then instruct him that it moves little by little; and once this is done, place it on a warm seat, and tell him to breathe deeply; and make him sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner, throughout all of this.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it progresses in this manner, if the seconding (unclear term) is between your finger, drain the moisture; and if it sticks to its place on the face or neck, cut it from the edge so that it is not held, and the child will die; then turn the child inside out, as you have placed it appropriately, and instruct the woman to breathe deeply. Then gently pull.
de l’issue des gemelz	From the emergence of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You know that twins are born many times, and never three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Twins are strange things and do not live long, they have no name; I know that they are multiplied, and their destinies are determined by the will of God, who is in control; and they never emerge as naturally as a single child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born deformed, as we have said, the treatment should be subtle and gentle, doing what is necessary immediately and lightly, so that it is guided towards healing.
de plusors enfans	from many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	They are never formed in the womb I, II, III, IV, V, VI, VII, or more up to XV, and they are all shaped like a child according to the measurement of its noble size, and it is necessary that the wise one knows all this, for by chance similar things may happen; so do as is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman who has suffered a stillbirth or abortion and there is no natural delivery, and you are compelled to perform manual extraction; it is necessary that you know if the woman's health is sound and free from any adverse effects due to the death; she should be placed on her back with her knees bent downwards, and her legs elevated. The midwife should apply a mixture of two parts, or have her lie in bed so as not to hinder the descent of the child. Then, moisten the woman's mouth with oils made from almond and fennel seeds, and linseed; then anoint the perineum with these oils and mixtures. Next, gently massage it, then insert the fingers in such a way that they support the descent of the afterbirth, ensuring no entanglement. If the afterbirth is descending normally, secure or pinch it between your thumb and index finger of your right hand, and use your left hand to hold the corbeille (a type of instrument) between your middle and ring fingers, gently applying pressure with your entire hand until the afterbirth is fully expelled and free from any attachments.
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then find another joint, where you need it most, so that the extraction is even; and then extend it equally from one side to the other, to make it move, and be sure the joint is sharp for moving, as this shape shows.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	If a part remains stuck, apply no oil to its joint, but compress it in that part and pull the other part; if nothing comes out, take this joint higher up the limb and do so until it completely moves out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward over the other and it cannot return due to tightness, you should wrap it up with a cloth until it moves completely; then cut at the joint of the plant or at the base, and do the same for the other hand, holding both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's foot is large and twisted at birth, and has a sharp edge, it is necessary to insert the pointed spatula between your fingers and press the toe, extracting the water; or you can use the instrument called 'almidach', from which the form is taken with the tools in this chapter, and thus also treat a child with a large natural toe. Then, pull out the bones with pincers, and if the foot pops out and is locked by force, split it as much as possible until the moisture at the worst point comes out; and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces while you can. And if it is bloated in the stomach or under the ribs, pierce it until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the fever is on its feet, it has a light pull, and the direction to the opening of the wound is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is seized in the belly or the bowels, it is necessary to draw out the drape wrapped around the hand; and make an incision on the belly or the bowels, as long as the moisture within it; and if other members are dislocated, and the excretion remains, then turn the palm towards the wound, and pull until it reaches the mouth of the wound; then incise or cut, and remove it; and if the mouth of the wound is contracted due to heat from the abscess that came, it is not appropriate to work on it, but rather, it is necessary to apply moist and greasy substances; and apply poultices, and soak with mild water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the dislocated joint is on his side, and you can put it back even, as we have said about a living child; and if that's not possible, then cut it off in pieces, leaving nothing of the second joint.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, apply what we have said about the abscesses that come from veins; and if bleeding occurs, place it in strong restraint, and apply other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had been cut open, and I consulted another on that wound, who healed the other wounds.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there comes a abscess in the cheek, it swells until it opens, and begins to cause severe pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called upon to treat it, and I thought for a long time, but I could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong poultice, and an bone came out, and after a few days, others followed.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought this was a bone from a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and found a bone in my hand, as long as the woman's arm was; she cried out for a long time, and then a little blood oozed from her wound; and I have never remembered this chapter to be anything but because, when the masters encounter something strange, they know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the woman back to her place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of the press, with which one binds the books; and at its turn to the shoulder, it handles the two sides of the limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle in their tightening, and made of ebony or box; and the mouth opening should be wide enough, with a margin measuring one palm and a half; and both sides of this same piece of wood should have a firm adjustment, one-and-a-half palms long or slightly longer; and this adjustment is inserted into the mare's mouth to open it when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling pliers; and it should have two adjustments, each one palm long and two fingers wide; and when opening the mare's mouth with the entire instrument, make the woman lie down on her side, with her knees bent and legs spread, then insert both adjustments into the mare's vagina and hold the handle of the instrument between her thighs; then open your hand over the entire instrument, just as you did with the pliers, according to the extent to which the mare's mouth opens, until the stimulus takes effect.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	The surgical instruments are all sorted and have various shapes; and when the skilled surgeon has prepared them, the work is done faster, and to a higher standard for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disregard the instrument if you have not prepared it, for the need for it is not an excuse for negligence.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine (a tool used during childbirth) is attached, it is important that you instruct the patient to hold her breath and then blow from her chest, while holding your hands over her mouth and nose; and if she does so, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this cannot be done, I will take a plug or cover and make an opening in it, and add herbs that can open the mouth of the abscess, such as calament, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or any one of them, should be cooked or boiled in water on the fire. Then place a cane or plug over the opening and put the other end into the abscess, holding it until the vapors enter the abscess; then make the patient sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second treatment does not help.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if after this treatment the abscess remains and is not swollen, instruct the patient to moisten their left hand with sesame oil or almond milk and apply it to the abscess. Then leave it in that state until they feel a pulling sensation, but they must move the limb slightly to the right and left and then extract it. It will come out and depart.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the wound is tightly closed, we have said the cure of sneezing and fumigation of herbs; and if it does not benefit from any of what we have said, be careful not to follow; but it is necessary that whoever is at the mouth of the wound, ties him to the woman's calf, then washes him with a four-ingredient ointment; he will vomit it back and get rid of it, and it will leave. Nevertheless, when she vomits it up, there will be a bad smell in the stomach and head, and the patient becomes worse.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	It is therefore necessary to use suitable fumigations: no one among the ancients has tried fumigation with arugula and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which the woman is cauterized to stop the flow of flowers and bleeding, this is it:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it resembles a tube made of glass, and it is placed with its narrow end in the wound, and its wide opening over the fire; and the fumes are produced from the coals, and the smoke until it is completely consumed, and then another one is started.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have their foundation pierced, but instead have a small lump: therefore it is necessary for the midwife to pierce this lump with a fine, non-sharp instrument, and avoid touching the wound; then apply a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not return, insert or open a plug of cloth, and leave it for several days, and it will be removed when the swelling goes down.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And this sudden stop of a wound or abscess should never be left untreated; it is necessary to cover this stop as we have said about the plug of cloth. And if it is cured, then it can heal like we have mentioned.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from its origin
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that originate from below the fundament are called nodules, and they are larger than those that emerge from the surface of the fundament, or in the space between two parts, if there is a fistula or several; and when this nodule has been present for a long time, it opens up, and still exudes clear or thin pus, and these fistulas do not heal; they are known because there is discharge or flatulence when the patient evacuates, and sometimes they burst open.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if the ulcers puncture through to the bladder, and halfway through the penis; and they reach up to the joint of the thigh, and into the root of the bone.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus, you recognize the fistula that is present in the fundament, but it is not present: and it is then that you insert your index finger into the fundament, and push an extremely thin needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no curvature.

And if it has curvature, if you insert a very thin plunger or horsehair, as long as you feel the resistance of the plunger or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no pain or discharge or wind, as we have said, know that it will not perforate; be hasty in treatment.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists up to the bladder or up to the urine conduit, if it lets go of the urine, and cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is cut close to the hip joint, then it is as if blood veins are coming out of its place; if there is no curvature or change in the pain around it, then it remains bent, and neither medicine nor any kind of dressing helps; and for these persistent fistulas, there is no cure except through hard work and the futile attempts of ignorant people who interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case where it is neither persistent nor old, there is hope for healing by fire, as I have experienced, and the patient lies on their back between your hands; they bend their legs up to their hips, and their hips are inclined towards their belly. Then take a sharp blade, or a smooth one if there is curvature, until you know where the fistula originates.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain in the foundation (of a dislocated joint), it is necessary that you insert your index finger, and then feel if there is any catching; and expose yourself where you feel between your thumb and forefinger the satisfaction or pain, then know that it is present; otherwise do not work further unless it can be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is nevertheless rare that anyone can be completely healed, but this does happen occasionally; and the aid you provide, if it involves gently cauterizing the wound according to its size, as mentioned above, and pouring hot oil into the fistula until it reaches the foundation; repeating this process two or three times, until you are certain that these infected marks have been burned away, which resemble a bird's feather; then apply moist compresses, until the wound is completely healed, and finally dress it with ointment that is soothing and sealing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is in this state, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If, in any other way, he cannot be healed; and if a foreign body is lodged between the bones, and it does not pierce all the way to the bone that forms its base, place a thick covering of wool or similar material between your two fingers and where you feel the fistula through the covering; then cut it from the beginning of the fistula, but do not remove the covering before, and then cauterize after, until it reaches the tip of the tent (presumably referring to the foreign body). The tent will be released and healed. Then beware of these false symptoms that resemble a bird's feather, and do not ignore anything.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pain persists, and a cut appears between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cautery combines two good things: it is the burn of these adjusted parts, and the congestion of blood and the drying of moisture; then treat the wound with moist oils or crushed materials, so that the inflamed parts bow down, and apply the burning cautery to the affected areas; then cure the wound with hot compresses and hard bandages, and use dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	Because once it is restored, it becomes healthy and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way through to the very bottom of the body, and it is distant from the flesh, if you press it into its origin, and feel it there.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the pulsation, and between it is the fabric or the lint or charcoal, or it is about to pierce through, if there is no other way of salvation and hope, through one of the three methods: you cauterize it as we have said, or cut it all the way through, or if you can carefully insert something and treat it as before; but be careful not to go too deep, that you do not cut the tissue holding the origin, and cause complications against your will; then treat it as we have said. Perhaps it will heal, or you remove that cover and clean it after it has been cut away from the origin, either with a knife or another pointed instrument; then cleanse the wound thoroughly, and try to prevent the fistula from reappearing in the area beyond the origin: this is a lighter task for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And they never form fistulas in this manner: and it is when you insert the tent into the fistula, and it is on one side near the base of the skin above, then take a sharp tent according to this shape.
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert the thread crookedly in two places, and push the tent all the way through the fistula until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is persistent at the base inside, then pull out the thread from that hole, and insert your second finger or base; and hold the top of the thread, bring the two ends together, and tie them to each other, and leave it for one or two days; and do not loosen it until the threads break that are between them, and stop pulling; then treat the wound until it is sealed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, try to open it in every way you can, but if it is too closed.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For if it is not properly opened, and then healed as we have said, while it remains healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form is a sharp, spiky one from which the fistula is made, it is both thick and deep; on the other hand, it is neither, because one must not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids exist in two ways: either they are inside the anus, resembling a grain of resin, with small or large veins, and emitting blood, or they protrude from the anus and have a reddish color; but those that protrude have little moisture, sometimes a bit of clear water or blood, and are treated as follows: you command the patient to take room and rest until the anus heals and the threads (presumably referring to the hemorrhoidal veins) become visible. If they are tightly stuck, use pliers or your fingernail to remove them; otherwise, use a cloth, cotton, or a piece of chamoix to grip them and pull them out. Cut them off at their base, then apply hot powders as directed in the cautery chapter, or cauterize them as described there, treating other ailments as necessary until they heal. If the anus cannot be opened, use a strong enema to wash out what is inside so that it can come out easily. When the patient feels better and the threads are no longer embedded, the treatment is complete, avoiding incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary for you to perform the stitch in this manner: take a twisted thread, and wind it into a needle, then draw the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side, and pass both ends of the thread under the needle, and if it is too thick, tighten the forming thread, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do thus with all the others, leaving one for draining the excess blood; then place a moist cloth on the wound, or sealing wax, and cover it, and instruct the patient to rest. And then let it be until the stitches fall out, and when they have fallen out, treat them with care or other remedies, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Carefully consider the sources or foundations.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often, there is a drying up of sources (or causes) in the intestine, due to constraints of nature, and when the illness is old and no medicine avails.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you scrape off the crust with a spatula or your fingernail, ensuring it does not remain moist; then treat it as soon as it is fresh, in the appropriate manner; and if it cannot be made fresh, repeat the scraping more forcefully than before, until it becomes moist and is cut; then treat it as soon as it is healed.
dou fremit	He trembles.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Mice are small, hairy bodies that move quickly; they never stop shivering, and one feels them as if they were dead from cold, spreading throughout the body, especially in the hands.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cane from a goose feather or a strong falcon feather, and place this cane on the shivering until it encircles the shivering entirely; then turn your hand over the entire cane as you wrap around the shivering, and reset it, removing the shivering from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make this of a steel or iron wire according to this form, and be subtle and draw them from below and above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not cut, so as to hold the two together, and press. And if you see, cauterize the wound, as it is in front or at the beginning of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a douching
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never use a clister of silver or gold, or melted iron or wire; and never use these small and large instruments according to those to whom they are entrusted.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	He who is thus entrusted with the care of children, especially those who are weak and in pain, should be small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the bladder should be small and narrow at the top, wide at the bottom; the belly is bound according to this manner.
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and if the belly is distended or tightly bound, as you see, and the feces are contained inside, have one opening on one side and the other on the opposite side; and place in the belly medicine from a bladder of an animal or parchment, making tiny openings all around, with a space between each one, then thread through these openings a strong thread woven tortuously in X shape or similarly, and arrange the belly like a key; and when the medicine is inside, attach it to the instrument with a strong thread, then perform the enema; and this is the form of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and apply the warm compress with oil or egg yolk or similar, then squeeze it gently; then the attendant shall grasp the patient's two legs together until they are completely relaxed, and relieve the pain in their feet against the wall, and allow the medicine to escape as much as possible; and if he sleeps soundly throughout the night, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the enema for a stomach disorder and the medicine quickly escapes, then it should repeat itself until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoid is at the anus or abscess, it should be treated with as delicate a clamp as for a child; and this is the shape of the delicate clamp upon which the skin is held taut.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken of the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments of hands and medicines, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to where they are located, and according to the type of wound, and from what they are caused.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.
