The things by which wounds are made are by the use of stone, and sword and knife, or lance or spear or axe or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the laws of the body, such as a wound that breaks through the neck, or head, or side, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, for the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is caused by stone or similar things, and the skin is nevertheless deeply cut and the wound is large, and you doubt whether an abscess will form: treat it immediately if it comes from fresh blood from the wound, and otherwise from the part that is most affected; and let the patient avoid wine and rich meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to be healed, his flesh should be reduced, and he should not drink wine or eat charred food; and apply a poultice of rose oil alone, or aromatic wine; and if there is a hot abscess, he should apply it to the fresh wound, as long as all its blood has not dried, and do not let air or powder touch it, which I will mention later; and if the burn has touched it, he should apply any clean herbs until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like the size of a sword or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by tenting, they should be sewed shut, as I will explain for abdominal wounds, using stitches.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed and deep, and only temporarily holds pressure, then treat it with medicine and replace the skin with hard wood, and instruct the patient to eat substantial foods such as meat, bread, cooked grain, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrefaction in the wound or leather that has not reached the bone, and it spreads quickly, drain it; then treat it. And if there is an artery in the wound or vein from which blood will not stop, even with medicine, cut the artery, and if this does not help, cauterize the wound.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you place this powder which hardens so that the fire moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The method of the powder is as follows: take one part incense, two parts dragon's blood, and three parts living charcoal, mix them finely, apply it to the wound, and tighten it until it spreads well and joins together with all its blood; then bind it tightly and leave it undisturbed if it does not swell, for the medicine should be removed only when it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never should charcoal be used alone, unless you have incense or dragon's blood, but the fire must move the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, especially if there is no fire or powder applied; but place any kind of ointment, or a paste made from water and honey and rye flour on it, as long as it remains soft; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if there is a fracture of the bone with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with delicate pliers; and I will tell you below about the fractures of the skull.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the collar (or neck).
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is simple, then it has no distinction from that at the top, but if there is damage to the nerves or arteries in the neck.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, then there is no other remedy but to let them heal without applying anything restrictive, as this would harm the nerves and cause them to retract; do not put any sharp objects on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation reaches the brain, which is the highest member. But apply medicine according to custom, such as washing with lukewarm water mixed with rose oil and clean bandages also in lukewarm water, and other herbs according to this method, and moist compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cutting it open and binding it with bands, then heal it until it is cured.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and infected, filled with pus, then pierce them or cut them open deeper; if an artery is severed, and bleeding occurs, ignore it, but apply cauterization as needed; if the pain is in the throat or the heart, do not touch the throat directly but rather keep the flow of blood going by applying pressure on the jugular vein, and then treat the wound with care for several days until it heals; if the wound has pressed into the bone, you can try to remove any protruding pieces of bone, but if that's not possible, let the wound fester until it becomes less severe and easier to treat; for a fresh wound, apply the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones or a fistula in the wound, treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife and deep, pay attention to the symptoms of the patient: if they are weak, know that the wound is deadly. If it is not very deep and still has fresh blood, do not apply any powder in the first hour; do not bind the wound tightly so as not to stop the bleeding until it seeps completely, returns to the body, and calms the patient; but apply an attractive dressing and change it twice a day. If you have no dressing, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture and make the patient sleep on the wound for three, four, or more days; if there is no spasm, no severe shaking of the body, no unusual strain, know that the wound will heal.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the wounds with various remedies and others, as long as they are clean; and if they cannot heal, know that there is a fistula; then treat them accordingly.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is shallow or deep, on the front, back, or side, treat it accordingly; if large, sew it up; if small, use powder; and if it penetrates into the bone, with careful handling take out any pieces, if they are severer; and if they are not severe, let the wound heal; for other wounds in other limbs, judgment should be made as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	disorder of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The disorder of the belly is great, medium, and small; from a large wound no intestines or intestinal nerves protrude, which is why sewing it up is more difficult, and a small wound is never as bad as a large one, unless the intestines are not sewn back together tightly enough; for they tend to swell soon after, causing pain, if they are not sewn back together securely. Therefore, it is important to move the intestines back into their proper place in layers, as with other wounds. And know that the rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: common sutures in the abdominal wall, suturing other wounds on the body, and two other specific sutures suitable for other wounds; yet they are still more beneficial with abdominal wound sutures. I will describe each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing internal is affected, it is a difficult matter to heal, and there are two ways to do so: either because of the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the injury.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth with hot water solely, or cook water with squinant (a type of herb), and cypress, and spice, and raise the intestines until the swelling is gone; and never use wine that constricts, and let it be moved as it cools down.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestine is filled with blood or other fluid, then this is a sign that it is lightened; and if it cannot enter, they make a slight cut in the wound with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and this is the first step: move the bone, for we should not cut without great need; and this is the tool to split it: saw inside the ribcage and divert it, or you will see its shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestine protrudes, return it to its natural position in its proper place, if you are able, for this is movement.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and located on the lower part of the belly, you should make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his head; if it's in the lower part of the belly, put the head and heels higher than the affected area, and pay attention that the healthy side be higher; thus, it is necessary to follow what I have said for both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, prepare what you need and put a piece of cloth over the entire cut; gather and close the edges, and this is the common method of stitching: pierce one or more needles according to the width of the wound, leaving two spaces at the beginning of the wound, and insert a needle with a strong, fine thread. Then, pierce both sides of the skin from inside out until you've pierced that part entirely, and bring together the two parts of the siphac (presumably referring to some anatomical structure); wrap double thread around the needle twice, then gather the two edges of the wound tightly, leaving two spaces, and insert another needle; secure the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue stitching as needed until all the wound is closed. The needles should be medium-sized, not too thin or too thick, because too thin needles penetrate the skin completely, and too thick ones cannot enter properly. It is therefore necessary to use medium-sized ones; do not pull the needles too far from the flesh and skin, otherwise they will open the wound before healing; then cut off the needle ends, place tents or sheets between the stitches to prevent the patient from feeling them while sleeping, and leave them until the wound has healed. This stitching method with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because only one or two stitches are needed, and you bring together both sides of the skin and the siphac with a needle containing a strong, medium-sized thread; when you have brought these parts together, wrap the needle in the manner of sewing clothes; leave a space between each stitch about as wide as a small finger; this stitching is suitable for humans, and I sewed a wound on a man's belly that had been cut with a knife. It was over one palm in width, and it extended two palms from the intestines, and it was a large wound located in the lower part of his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its proper place after it had remained thus for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed completely within fifteen days, and it was cured, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they marveled that he did not die, and this was a miracle; I did not cure him with any treatment, for I was in a place where none could be found, neither any medicines; and I put clean cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and the thread from the opposite side to where you started; when it has pierced through the fabric in a straight line, pull the thread until the stitch is tight, or cut it off, and begin again from the other side, as a tanner does with leather, leaving one part of the stitch on one side and picking it up on the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of sewing, which Galen calls "so as it were," is like nothing so much as when two parts are joined together in a natural way, and one part is applied to the other with something satisfying at their meeting point: take a needle or thread close to the edge, and pierce only this place, leaving the two parts of the seam; then turn the needle and pierce from the opposite side towards that inside, as far as the two parts of the seam are joined; then pierce each one from the opposite side towards that inside, in the other two parts where the thread is on the other side; and this is the most usual way of sewing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen uses these words, and no one testifies to this: the belly should be sewn with two needles, each with a thread; one needle is inserted from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and remember that when the opening is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more difficult than for other openings in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as that of other wounds: and it is that when you open a fresh wound to all its blood, if the flesh has moved, then take care to close the intestines and the cut; then apply the powder made with char, and if the flesh has moved, apply any present dressing, until the wound bows; and stitch it, and make the bandage tight, and the mirach; then treat the wound as other wounds, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, put a piece of old cotton, and move it twice a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you need no other medicine in addition to these remedies for simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound affects principal members, it is necessary that you apply a light cloth moistened with hot seasonal oil or rose oil around the angles and under the armpits; and if there is pain or putrefaction in swells, and this happens often, clisterize them with warm red wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestines. Puncture it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestinal tissue called "jeun" cannot heal when it is weary, and this is due to the condition of the veins, and the subtlety of the entire body, and the nearness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the scab falls from the wound, reset it just as the intestine is fresh; but if it is old and turned black, you must hold the black part still to prevent blood flow, since there are veins and arteries; then cut away the tissue between them, and hang the two edges of the wound outside until the scab comes off completely.
de la routure dou boueil	From the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it cannot be restored in any man, as I have seen one nobleman wounded in his navel or abdomen by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, it became inflamed and fistulated, and there issued forth evacuation and flatulence; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to be subtile until he was healed, and the intestines were made whole.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him healed, I doubted that the patient would not have pain in his stomach; but he felt no pain, only improved conditions, and eating and drinking; and certain experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in this manner: take a large needle, then gather together the lips of the wound, and when the needle has opened the mouth, place it between the two lips, so that it pulls them together; then cut off the head of the needle, and let it stay so that it cannot be untied, then insert another needle in the same manner until the wound is completely closed; and then treat the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That chief is sharp in the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient, and it is possible to bind the intestine with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the chief of this intestinal thread, which is much stripped, and then tie it to the chief of this thin linen thread twisted, then wind the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and arrange it in the rupture; and this method of stitching is only effective according to the path of truth and hope; and if the wound is deep and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no health, except with subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	or whether it is a fistula, wherever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	You know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is generally called a "fistula", especially when it is covered with hair and deeply seated.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula, according to the true nature, is hard and white, causing no pain, and just like the feathers of a bird; it is neither clear nor thick, neither too little nor too much; and I have already spoken about this in the division of wounds: every wound that does not heal, where there is no pus, is due to one of the nine causes. These are: the smallness of blood or pus; its evil nature; the presence of hard matter within it, preventing the formation of pus on the surface; excessive bowing; spoiled flesh and poor quality material; unsuitable medicines; corruption leading to pestilence; late digestion and slow healing due to regional properties; or the presence of veins or bones. I have already explained all these causes, their signs, and the corresponding treatments in detail.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I inform you about the treatment of a fistula which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that affect large veins, arteries, and nerves, or the bladder, intestine, or bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or any joints of the hands or feet, and similarly.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All fistulas of this nature are difficult to heal and require hard work and knowledge. If there is a fistula that does not come to the surface as I have described, but you believe in the cure, and understand it, take a sharp blade of iron or steel; if the fistula is straight, cut it accordingly; and if it is curved, seek a subtile tool to press it into the curve, for the pus will flow and conform to the curvature. Then, thoroughly wash it with one of the openings, as moisture travels from one opening to another, cleansing it. Press your hand firmly on the affected area to determine where the patient feels pain, and mark the location; dig out all foreign bodies and corrupt tissue that are deep within. Cure the fistula as best you can, then apply moist, medicinal herbs around the wound until the medicine dissolves any excess pus at the bottom; subsequently, place hot, clean bandages over it until it heals. If, after these steps, it is not cured, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not affect your principal members, as we have said, and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackening, keep the king until the corruption is entirely removed, then apply remedies to the accompanying issues as long as it remains healthy; and if it is not healthy and bows back as before, know that you are not yet free: expose and cure as much as possible until you reach the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the joint; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot cure it; if there is no other cause but to let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupt bone, and you can pull it with pliers suitable for such, and if there are many bones, break them all, leaving none intact; and if moisture makes things worse and there is doubt or fear, cauterize and dry, and help the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them after an hour, apply something putrid to the wound and let it fester until the bones are soft; then, remove the pus. If it is a large bone, like the leg or thigh, scrape off the pus until all the blackness is gone, then dress the wound; and if there is a great deal of corrupted flesh extending nearly to the bone, cover and protect it entirely until the corruption is healed, then cure it while it is still fresh. I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg so that you can take an example from it and use it in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something that came from inside his body, causing matter to collect in the leg and leading to a large abscess with no apparent way to open it. But because of their foolishness, they prodded the abscess so much that it opened, and many materials were corroded, turning into a fistula, and there were numerous holes through which all the fluids from the body leaked out, making him bow and moan from the pain in his body. Many doctors attempted to cure him for two years without success, as he lacked knowledge of the craft; it was then that I was called, and I examined his leg and the medicines they had used, and what was causing the holes in his flesh due to the corruption. The young man's skin turned red, and it had a citrus-like color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these gaps, and then I examined all the gaps, and I found that some came into contact with each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the gaps until I discovered a part of the bone, which was rotten and pierced, and the corruption extended to the bone inside; I understood what appeared to be the corrupt bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except that which I left; and I began to treat the wound with medications for a long time, but they could not heal; then I re-examined it and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, so I treated it and then set it, and focused on binding the place; but I could only cut around a palm-width of the bone, and pull it to its original position, and then treat it with medications again. It healed and was bound firmly, and did not want to start over again except for the weakness of the patient who could not endure, and the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because for the complete evacuation of blood, it often happens, but it was completely healed, and a hard callous grew in its place on the bone, and it was of good disposition and caused no harm or discomfort at all, neither from going away nor from coming back.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be handled in this way: take a ligature, and pull firmly at the end of the bone that is open, and instruct anyone to extend it upwards; then tie another thicker linen ligature over the first one and secure it to the callous that has formed away from the bone, pulling the callous downwards so you expose the raw bone underneath, where the corruption was; place a piece of charcoal or a table under the bone to protect the raw bone, and be sure to do this as carefully as possible, taking care to observe and feel the corruption, and do it again if necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if a bone is corrupted and will not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then expose all of it; then apply heat from beneath, and move the corruption from one part to another until it stops, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, cut out the corrupt joint and bone from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other way but to cut them; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or ankle of the foot, it is very serious, but nonetheless you must inquire about this corrosion how it opens; and cleanse it in every way that you can, as long as the vein or nerve do not oppose you; and know that there are many tools for cutting and joining these bones, according to the position of the bone and its appearance, thickness and thinness, length and shortness, hardness; and for this reason, it is necessary to adapt each instrument to every work; and know that the operation will show you the instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the ailments; therefore choose the instrument you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joint dislocates either internally or externally; and when you have treated that erosion with remedies but they do not help, then it is necessary to cover that limb until the place where the erosion occurs, so that the patient escapes from death or evil, which is greater, due to the fault of the limb; and the sign of this is that the member turns black, seeming to be burned by fire, and after the blackening, since this corrosion goes from member to member and takes over the whole body, then you must hurry to cover it, and if it is caused by the bite of some venomous animals, such as a scorpion of the sea, a snake, or similar, then if the erosion is at the top of the two limbs, treat it, and do not give it time to come to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, and the bone is stuck in the joint, so that the corruption does not come up to the arm; and if it comes up to the arm, then cut at the shoulder; and if it passes through the shoulder, it's fatal, and there is no cure outside of the quantity of its virtue; and thus it acts when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes in the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut throughout the foot; and if it rises in the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or binding the member is that you tie it above and below, and stretch one assistant with each ligament downwards, and another assistant with each ligament upwards, and remove the flesh that is between the two ligaments with a wide spatula, until the bone is exposed; then cut or bind it, and place a linen drape on each side so that the linen does not touch the healthy part, and cause further damage and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the wound firmly or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, bind the affected limb securely with a suitable tie, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to this man: he suffered from a blackening that seemed like a burn, and that corrosion appeared first on his right lower leg, until it discolored the whole leg. When he saw the corrosion, he covered his leg, and it healed; but long afterward, the corrosion returned on his left hand, and he came to me, and I placed things to repel the corruption after purification of the body, and it could not cease. He asked me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to do so because I had hope of repelling the matter; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, since the strength of the man was weak. He became completely despairing, returned to his land, covered his hand, and it healed; and I have heard nothing more miserable than this, except when one does otherwise, if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No abscess should form in a fleshy part, and linger so long that it causes great swelling; then it ruptures and gushes, leaving the living flesh, just like a vessel, and the skin above is as delicate as fine cloth, not penetrating to the bone or nerve, and this illness is called "sain," not "fistule." But if it extends so far that it penetrates to the bone, it is called a "fistule;" and the skin should be cut all around, especially if it is delicate like fine cloth, and not be allowed to corrupt.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the skin has opened and the corruption has not been completely eradicated, and the flesh is hard like leather, cure it with an enema in this way: examine if the breasts are swollen and have a foul odor; then prepare an enema with Egyptian medicine (made as follows): take equal parts of ash, oil, and lithargirum, put them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and thick like honey. Then, according to your need, mix it with water and honey, and give the enema to the infected breast, closing the fistula; leave the medicine for two hours, then extract it while straining; do this several times until the breast is completely cleansed and the pus has disappeared; and never use an enema of ash water when this medicine is not available; instead, mix ashes from grapevine prunings with water, strain it, and give the enema; continue until you are certain that the breast is thoroughly cleansed. If the patient cannot endure either the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, give him an enema of honey and wine, or a mixture of some other medicine containing a small amount of lithargirum; or use honey and rose oil, as honey has purifying and cleansing properties, and wine causes pus to come to the surface. And when you have done this and are certain that the breast is cleansed, give an enema with whatever creates warmth in the affected part, and use a mixture of plaster of Paris and rose wine; or use any other medicine and ointment as described in the section on treating wounds. If the fistula opening in the breast is small, and the catheter cannot enter it, widen it slightly with a hot iron, then apply a layer of Egyptian ointment (or basilicon) until it is wide enough for the enema; but if the wound is too large, you must cut away part of the skin to make room for the enema, or insert the catheter above or below the fistula opening.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Because when the bowel is perfectly intact, it does not permit any hernias; and if you cannot cover the wound properly as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bowel descends to its lowest position, for when the bowel is perfectly intact, it does not permit any hernias, and if you cannot cover the wound properly as you see fit, arrange it so that the bowel gently flows downwards, leaving no part of the bowel exposed; and take consolidating medicines to place over the wound, and cover it with a linen cloth that covers the entire wound; then close tightly around the opening in the side of the wound, using a wider bandage first, as needed, according to the size of the opening, and place the bandage over the opening of the wound to ease the pressure from the bowel, and do not remove the large outer bandage for several days; and whoever is over the opening of the wound often removes it to ease the bowel, and knows what flows from the bowel, whether it be poison or pus or enough or digested or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when you see the medicine has taken effect in this manner, and you observe the nature that has formed over the opening of the wound, then you know the healing has begun, and bring it closer to health; and then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the bandage, and renew the treatment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast becomes bowed and distended after many days, knowing that it will not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons appear after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people whose conditions worsen when they speak about their wounds, and others who do the opposite; and if the breast becomes bowed and distended after many days, knowing that it will not open; and if the breast is slow to heal, and remains distant, then apply medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, as a final remedy, for there is a great deal of vitriol involved, which is the last medicine; take the final remedy and apply it with rose oil, and mix it with aged wine of equal substance; then preserve it and use it; and the same is done with heated honey, thickening it when it has been taken off the fire; then spread it over the breast, and do not administer alopathy or the roots of celestial lis, which is also like flour of times and centaury; and use simple or compound remedies: crush them and make a powder, and mix it with the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and this cure does not heal it, then know that corruption has taken hold, and is making an impression on the bones, or the hard members, or the ligaments; as we have said before regarding the treatment of fistulas.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Gangrene is an abscess that forms under a nail in the hand or foot, or occasionally elsewhere; and when it becomes old and care is not taken, it can cause a severe gangrenous infection that spreads as far as the root of the nail, and even potentially throughout the entire nail; and it leads to corrosion down to the bone, causing intense foul-smelling pain, and the flesh around the digit becomes large and discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the previous section, and the treatment does not benefit, then you must remove all the dead tissue remaining under the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is great aid if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound; and if the nail grips the flesh deeply, and begins to puncture, and the wound bleeds, it is necessary that you remove the nail from under the flesh, and draw it upwards, and stop the bleeding, and treat the wound with hot and corrosive medicines to remove all traces; then apply remedies for healing until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, scrape it off and pull it out, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see both bones corrupted, remove them immediately as mentioned above, then treat (the wound) until it heals; and if it is burnt and blackened, and causes great pain, it is necessary that you first heal the bone; then cut the nail with a sharp scissor across the top, and ensure the cutting does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, apply something soothing.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain excruciates the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	He who is born without the hands in anyone's care is entirely flesh, and perhaps he has parts where there should be bones, and never an fingernail, and none of them are born at the root of a joint, or birth takes place in no way for any of them.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born without any fingers cannot move them, and he who is born with a joint in the finger might not be able to move it; the size of the one who is fleshly is very light, in this way: cover him at his root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the jointure is hard to cure: if you keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	As for him who is born with or develops a deformity in the last (joint), it is necessary that you first cover the joint properly up to the bone, then dislocate the bone to a suitable position, and then treat it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The deformities that come as one must assemble themselves come either from birth, or from the healing of a wound, or from a burn by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary to close this wound, so that it must be repaired according to its natural shape; then place between two pieces of moistened wool or linen cloth, so that the flesh does not adhere; or you put between two thin pieces of leather, as long as the edges are closed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If adhesion occurs at any of its edges with the palm, close this wound as appropriate.
des vils	The word "des vils" translates to 
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	These veins are thickly wrapped, filled with excessive melancholic fluids, which affect various parts of the body; and they occur more frequently in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry loads, compared to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer purgative remedies no more often than once, and then cleanse the bowel.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of fire is according to two methods: one is with cauterization and extraction of the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and drain it entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done according to this method: first, raise the affected leg with hot water very strongly until the flesh becomes tender, then extract the sick leg from above the knee to the part below the groin; then cut the vein in one, two, or three places with a broad blade, and drain and extract the black blood in your hand from one end to the other, as much as the patient can endure, and then tie it, and command him to turn red with flesh that forms black blood; and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	They should raise the leg of the afflicted patient, if there are many hairs, then immerse it in hot water until it turns red and swells; and if you do not have a bath, heat it over fire, then press the long part of the vein at the top of the knee or on the inside of the ankle; then open the skin at the wound, scrape the vein from each side until it is exposed, and you see it red and black, and when it enters under the skin, it appears like a white string. Then stretch it from the back, until it is raised from the skin, then press it lightly, and then cut it again on another hook; then scrape the skin over the vein until it becomes exposed, then lift it gently, as you have done before, and cut it on another hook; then make a new cut if needed, then lift and cut the leg, and pull and lift it to the second cut; then extract it little by little until it comes out entirely, then cut it; and if you cannot pull it or lift it, insert a very strong needle through all the string, tie it and pull it, and stretch from behind, until it comes out; and be careful that it does not cut, because if it does, you will not be able to pull or lift it, and it will cause harm to the patient; and when you have pulled everything, place a soft cloth moistened in wine and rose oil on the wound and treat it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if it (the joint) is contracted and twisted and wrapped up together, and not in the least straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly but do not cover it; treat it as we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The way to do it is to grip the joint firmly so that it does not slip, and cut only through the vein; it should be done with great force, for if it were delicate, it would pierce the vein, but since it must be thick, as we have said, this is its form:
de la voinne civile	from the vein (in the limb)
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot parts where no plants or trees grow, and on land where there is no moisture; and sometimes it appears elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to putrefaction that comes from beneath the skin, as it winds and twists inside the body.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein appear, it is that there is a very great swelling in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to emerge forcefully, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, it is necessary to wrap a piece of cloth around it from one and a half to two fingers wide, leaving the cloth on the leg, and every time that there is no discharge at the opening, wrap it again around the cloth and the new growth; and if it is too long, cut off a part of it and wrap the remainder, not cutting it at its base, as long as it continues to emerge. For if you cut it, it will return to the flesh and cause abscesses, putrefaction, or other ill health. Therefore, it is necessary that this treatment be done little by little until it has completely emerged from the body; and in no case should there remain any part of the vein when treated with five to ten fingers' length, or even an hour ago, when I saw one that had emerged ten fingers' length, and when cut, it left a hollow or gap through which everything came out. It is necessary to empty the matter inside and immediately apply medicines to prevent putrefaction for as long as the abscess endures.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never touch this vein with your fingers, especially when it opens at the ankle or knee joint, and a lot of blood flows out; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that are born between skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "beef disease" in our land because it often affects cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh. It spreads throughout the body, moving from one member to another, causing great pain as it eats its way through the skin or muscle. It is caused by putrefaction of certain humors, just like worms, snakes, and lice do in the stomach; and one doubts the severity of its malice, for when it moves through the body, it goes up to the head, reaches the eye, and sometimes retracts, destroying the eye; and this happens often.
