Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it heal and subside, it cannot be washed away until it goes completely: therefore, you must lie the limb on its side and above and below with a strong, tight bandage, then cut and drain it thoroughly, so that it does not burst out again; and cauterize it with fire while it still moves; and the greatest damage it causes is when it releases oil, as we have said; and if you see it approaching the eye, tighten the eyebrow from below, then cut and drain it; and it is necessary for the patient to use purification of the body with solutions of medicine to remove bad humors, and take care not to consume foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in no particular member, but can move from one member to another; and I have seen this as I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I discovered a small swelling in the vein of her arm; and after some time, I saw something rise up on her shoulder, as quickly as if it were a live silver coin when it cuts through flesh; the pain left that place and moved to her shoulder, and then, shortly afterwards, spread throughout her body, reaching the other arm; then she told me that she felt it moving around inside her body.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled much at how she moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had observed that many experienced great pain when moving from one limb to another, but I did not understand why, as I saw this in a woman; and I thought it was because she had dry skin and exposed veins, and that this constrained the wind, which did not seem to be the case for those who are healthy, with moist skin and closed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease heal, and the patient feels this pain, opening as we have said, press it from above and below firmly, then close it until this constrained wind in the limb leaves; and cauterize the limb; and if you do not have these at hand, cure it with those who drive out wind, such as foul-smelling pills, or pills of viper, and others like them.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows vary, according to their appearance and according to the parts of the body from which they originate.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Their diversity lies in that they have various tips, some large and others small, some serrated and others smooth; and there are those with two angles, and those with long barbs, and those with segments; and some exit through any member, entering in two ways: either in a principal member, as the head, body, liver, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it breaks in any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterwards, appears: it is necessary that you fight for the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in various dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not extracted completely, pull it out, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow breaks and pierces the bone, and there is pain in the head, and blackness and blinding and turning inwards, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and clouded thinking, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it comes out from the nose or ears; and possibly he loses speech and voice; and also comes out a moist, white discharge resembling pus, and sometimes like blood from a wound; and if these signs appear to you, if you are skilled in healing, extract the arrow, even if it is not fully embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of a broken seat when it cracks or breaks, is that it is close to the left breast, and feels as if it were wedged into something hard, not empty; and sometimes the seat becomes silent like the pulse, and there is black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: therefore be certain without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that the pulse never moves is that there is no foam coming from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns pale, and he breathes heavily and stops moving.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow breaks in the covering of the pit, it is a sign of broken ribs; and it causes great pain and heavy breathing and sobbing, and all the movements of the shoulder blades are affected.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow pierces through the stomach, perhaps something from the wound disturbs the indigestible flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces through the belly, and there is no trace of good fate through the intestines, then there is little hope for a cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces through the bladder, and the urine flows out in spurts, and the patient feels intense pain, know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs—as it feels and appears—the fingers, hands, arms, shoulders, aid (possibly referring to a specific medical term or condition), the lower back, knees, feet, and legs, all exhibit various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	There once happened to me at home a wound that hit the ear or the jaw: I attempted to extract it, and pushed from another side beneath the ear's fat, and it was completely healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And also, through a trick, he removed an arrow that was lodged in the fat beneath the skin, and the arrowhead was only visible towards the wood, and it was an arrow of great length with a blue arc, without causing any pain; the wound healed, and no further accidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And pull a arrow from the throat of a Christian, which was an Arabic arrow with ears; I opened the mouth, and extracted it carefully as I pulled it out, and healed the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I pulled an arrow from a man, which was embedded in his belly, and thought he was dying; but after thirty days had passed, there was no change in his condition; then I cut the arrow, dug it out, and pulled it out without any ill effect.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to help a man whose arrow is embedded in his back, and there is an abscess at the wound; and the arrow remains inside him, and he does not change his natural condition, or find any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man to whom an arrow has penetrated his face, and the wound is deep; he suffers greatly without relief; and many others like him.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated a prince, the king himself, who had an arrow in his neck that was slightly tilted to the right side, and it had been there for three days when I was called to cure it.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I carefully probed it, and I felt nothing; but he experienced sharp pain and discomfort beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I placed a soothing poultice on the shoulder, because the muscles did not tense up; and I saw the arrow's muscles.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice for several days, and thus healed the wound, holding back the patient's pain for a long time until he felt the arrow inside his body; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it healed and I felt the tip of the arrow sticking to the flesh; then I adjusted the opening of the wound using that medicine until I could clearly see the shaft of the arrow; it took about four months for the wound to heal, and then I used pliers to remove it from both sides, but it would not come out. So I continued to try subtle and ingenious tools, until I finally managed to extract it using well-made pliers, as described at the end of this chapter, while I pulled on it and dressed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they consider that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I then restored it, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have also told you the quality of extracting certain arrows; so put your trust in what I say, for books cannot encompass everything; but wise masters compare and discern well enough between a small thing and a great one, and at the very moment when strange things occur in this art, they find new works and new instruments.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of the members where they are embedded unless in two ways: either through the vein from which they entered or from another part; and those that came out from the side where they entered, it is an arrow entering into their flesh, and never comes out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, let it stay as long as the swelling around it is soft and light; and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for several days, and every day move it slightly; then it will come out, and if it does not, pierce through the entire wound with a fine needle until the swelling around the bone is widened, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone so deeply that it reaches one of the cavities in the brain and none of the events I mentioned earlier affect the patient, do not pull it out, but let it stay as long as it remains even after several days, for if the arrow reaches such a place, it brings death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not driven completely into the bone, and does not heal properly, and the patient suffers no ill effect for some time, the skill of extraction must be applied.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be extracted outward, then apply poultices around it as I have told you; then treat the bone while it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone deep within and cannot be seen, one must try with all their strength; and if you feel it, use any suitable instrument; and if you cannot reach it due to the depth of the arrow or because there are no muscles, bones, or nerves nearby, leave it until the wound has healed; and extract the arrow if possible, and if it has roots by which it is attached, break off the part that is embedded in the bone as much as you can, and then twist or bend the arrowhead so that you can pull it out, taking care not to break the arrow.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, so that the limb around it is completely relaxed, then pull it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding from the wound makes it contraindicated, then administer what we have said about treatment in that chapter; and be careful with the incision on the nerve and vein, and use any means you can to extract the arrow without danger, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position it was in when the arrow entered, for that is the greatest help, and if you cannot, then do as the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	He knows that the arrow comes from another direction, where it opens something within, and the flesh is inflated at that point, as one can see or feel: then cut through, as far as the pincers can reach, and then extract: if it comes out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be extracted, leave it for now, and then try to extract it again until it comes out; and if the arrow is deeply embedded, keep pressing down on it, so that when the arrowhead enters the end of the instrument, you push the instrument further out, easing the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you clear all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow comes out in the side or abdomen or near the bladder or ribcage, and you can reach it, take care to remove it; avoid touching the vein and nerve, then extract it, and then dress the wound carefully, as is necessary, and cure it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to extract arrows resembles an eagle's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape [for the arrowhead] when it is like a feather is also like the quill of a bird, to push to the tip of the arrow, as this shape is:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of pliers for pushing and pulling, if it is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins from which one can draw blood, of which there are 16 main ones: 2 beating veins behind the ears, called "herbech"; and the 2 arteries that are visible in the temples; and 2 veins in each arm, called "aspires"; and the vein across the forehead; and the vein at the crown of the head; and the 2 veins at the nape of the neck; and the 2 veins on the lips above the mouth, which are called "augeherich"; and 2 veins beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which blood is commonly drawn are 5 in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, located on the left side and called by the common people "vein of the head"; and the median is called "fast" and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and called by the common people "vein of the body"; and the basilic is on the right side and called by the common people "vein of the stomach", and it is located above the flexor and is the one from which blood is drawn, clearly visible on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saving vein is the one between the little and ring fingers, and if it rains; and in the leg, there are three veins: one below the knee on the left side, and the second is the shin bone vein on the right side; and the third vein is called 'nesse', located in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg, there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The veins behind the ears aid in the discharge of old catarrhs and migraines; and the quality of the vein, as I have said, is to raise the patient's head and rub the affected area with a rough cloth; then tighten the bandage around the patient's neck until the two veins behind the ears relax downward from the head: hold them there, and where you feel the pulse beneath your hand, it signifies life; then take the lancet, and pierce through the vein down to the bone, and lift your hand along the entire vein upstream, cut and sever the skin and the vein well above its course, and allow blood to flow until you see; then drain and tie it, as long as it remains healthy; and I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	He heals the two arteries that are in the temples, which is a powerful and old remedy, and accustomed to stop the flow of tears at the eyes; and the quality of the healer is as I say: and it is that the patient pulls his collar tightly, until the two veins open widely; and feels the pulse under his right index finger, and then signs with a pin; then lightly touches the vein on top with your left hand index finger, and withdraws the lancet from below, and gently opens the vein on top, and the clot, as you did with the other veins, and allow the blood to flow according to need; then release the patient, and place your right hand on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton; and then form a bandage and leave it until it is healed; and we have often spoken of their healing and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The surgeon of the vein on the forehead is as valuable as the surgeon of the skull for facial diseases old and new, and for migraine and redness; and his quality is that the patient squeezes their head tightly until the vein appears. Then take the instrument called "discherter," which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, allowing blood to flow out according to the amount you see; then loosen the patient's head, and tie the vein as long as it remains healthy without opening a wide cut.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too strong; and the healthy wood must be crossed, for the bone is close, and perhaps breaks the flames when they are too thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The health of the two veins located in the arms is beneficial for these conditions: abscesses, inflammation, redness, and facial diseases. The quality of their health is such that the patient feels no pain or discomfort, as if there were no injury; then the healthy vein, and it should be slightly across, neither too thin nor too thick, because there is no middle ground.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the fire is subtle, it may burn; then apply pressure to the wound, as much as needed, and then wrap it in cotton and secure it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The health of the vein near the nose is very valuable for cold, sudden fever, and facial illnesses, such as migraines and redness that appear on the face, especially when it is chronic. The quality of the health is such that the patient tightens their jaw, strains their nose with their left hand, and inserts the subtle long flame between the two nostrils, since the vein does not open well enough, and the blood will begin to flow. Do not poke too deep, and apply pressure with the flame according to your need, then bind it for a night, as it is quickly restored; this is the form of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The holy water from two springs helps in the tightening of the eyelid, and at the onset of illness, and much sickness, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and oedema; and the quality of the water is such that the patient pulls his eyelid away from both sides, as we have said; and the skilled one standing over the head of the ill person, and the patient seated in a certain place, then cleanse the vein with warm blood, as much as necessary; then repeat the same in the other vein, then unbind the ligature, and tighten the veins gently so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound may heal.
de la sainie des leivres	from the cleansing of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cleansing of the veins above the lips helps to improve oral health, and it aids in the healing of gum disease, lip splits, and pain and swelling around them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the cleansing involves having the patient sit before you, holding their chin as mentioned; then turn the lip, and examine both veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by their black color and the small veins around them: therefore, cut both, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, cut the thicker ones from each part, and do the same for the two veins above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The health of the veins beneath the tongue is of great importance after treating the health of the head, and it aids in the constriction of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and conditions of the mouth; and the quality of the healing is such that the patient should bite between their fingers under the light of the sun, gently moving the tongue, and examining each side for a dark vein: then both are healthy, and do not press too hard, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck, which are commonly healed, are treated in two ways: either by gently pressing with a hot flame or a fine knife, known as an "aneis," and they are wide or narrow according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	It forms a bright red mark, very renowned, and is broad as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it requires skill to open veins with thick, clotted blood, that contain much blood and pus; and this is the form of an olive-colored flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more delicately pointed, and is for cleansing the delicate veins, where there is delicate, yellow-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The cleansing of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, is very helpful for illnesses that are beneath the throat, and the collarbone, and the chest, and the stomach; and it is important for the healer to cleanse it thoroughly and to wash out the artery below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it touches the artery, and blood comes, as it should be stopped, as I have said; and the flame must not be squeezed, but cut like a serpent.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the vein does not open clearly, it is necessary that you extract it and choose another, or take any rain from it, or heal the vein next to it in the arm: it opens clearly; and cut it with the serpent flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you come to know the place of the vein, it is necessary that you extract the arm, touch the vein as long as you feel the pulse; then mark the place with a sign, and bind the arm, and cut the vein with the serpent flame; and be careful not to injure the artery when you see it inflated, for that is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it bubbling up from above like a child's urine, and the veins are red and delicate, know that this is a sign of an artery: then hurry, and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger so that the vein does not burst, which often happens; let the arm be still, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; be afraid, and do not move until it heals.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the vein does not stop bleeding and it seems to be life-threatening, and no medicine is at hand, if the artery opens up, as often happens with the retarding of death; stop the bleeding from the vein.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of fig bark, and cut it, and take one half and bind it tightly to the other side; if the pain subsides, that's good; if not, cure it as we have said, with powders that stop blood; the stopping is not too grievous in various dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	If a vein is infected, help by cleansing blood from the top of it and from inside, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the healer should wash for the nerve that is inside, and if he does not reach it thoroughly, and finds the nerve, it swells and the health is harmed, and perhaps it cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, then it is necessary that you cleanse it with an instrument; and avoid touching the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if a vein is between the two bones, cut it from above.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The treatment for cephalics (head pains) consists in drawing blood from the head, which helps; and it is beneficial to apply a flame of olive or myrtle oil, as this is the safest of all veins, as it does not damage any nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is advisable to seek the lightest vein, and do not be concerned if it hurts the first time, just try again; sometimes, due to the peculiarity of each person, the veins might swell up even if they are pierced for the first time, but this is not cause for alarm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood depends on your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it should only be practiced to preserve health and prevent future illnesses; and bloodletting should be performed in one of the three veins: the cephalic, femoral, or basilic vein. One should bleed at the beginning of prayers, during autumn and winter after meals, when the sign of satiety appears; and one should bleed on the first day, or third day, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bloodletting to treat illnesses does not have a specific time frame, but it should be done as needed for the day or diet, at any hour and in all seasons; and children under twelve years old, and pregnant women after only four months until the seventh month, should not be bled.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should not consider the old who have passed sixty years as healed.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to heal themselves in any way, it is necessary that they clean the intestines with a light enema, if they have a lot of feces retained, so that the veins do not draw out the superfluous, harmful waste from the primary members; nor should one consider as healed someone who is too salty with meat, or drunken, as long as it persists, or those who are water-retained, or after colic, vomiting, abdominal pain, frequent sexual intercourse, heavy labor, wakefulness, and fasting; then carefully remove the humors, if they are excessively swollen, from meat, beverages, and medications, if you have good cause; then enter a bath, if nothing prohibits it, to purify the blood, and heal the vein from the inside on the third day, as we have said; and guard yourself that day against work, strain, luxury, and similar things; and be calm and joyful, and consider yourself healthier than those you are healing, and rub the limb two or three times, then gradually tighten the bandage, for if it is too tight or loose, it cannot heal properly; and then rub it with your hands until the veins swell and you feel them. Moisten the wound with a little bit of old oil, then place your left-hand finger on the vein under the limb where you want to heal, so that the vein does not move and is not injured.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow like cords in the body, and if they are blocked by wind or other obstructions, when fire is applied, it retracts from the flame, and cannot open the vein, thus becoming one of these cases; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, so it is necessary for the healers to be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, it should be tried again a little lower, or with greater care, for if the veins are not inflated.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the vein is inflated and the patient fears, let it be for one or two days without binding the arm: perhaps an abscess will form later; do not enter a bath, but continue the treatment as she judges appropriate; and if the opening is small, cut through gently and carefully, so as not to release too much blood, for this very act itself can cause a great deal of bleeding. This happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the vein enfolded, don't immediately continue with the cure, but apply a little oil, for it lightens the body of blood, and the oil moves in this vein the substance that is attached; and thus administer the oil in each vein you open to stop the flow of blood; and it also acts as a triacle and bow, when it is placed on the vein; it subtlety loosens the clot and spreads it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess forms, which often happens, especially when the vein is not opened properly or the incision is small, hurry and apply a moist sponge with hot water and some silk, holding it for an hour; after the blood flow from the vein stops, and if it remains in place without any blackening or turning green for several days, then do not harm it. And if you see, apply aloe or myrrh mixed into calament juice, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and swelling appear on the holy basil: then place your hand there, and if you feel the soft joint under the pressure of your hand, it is this appearance that is harmful.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put anything we have said to use unless by chance it lacks an artery; but apply a dry plaster to harden the joint, then treat with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each one of the pains according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the pain.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because if the wound is infected, let it drain as much as possible while it remains red; and if you see it swelling, let it drain until it becomes less swollen; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is strong and robust, and has the skill to extract blood, to make a wider wound, and have broader flames; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and cauterize him more gently and frequently, and use a diagonal cut, not a sharp puncture; and this method of cauterization is safe from infection and nerve damage, and it is better than long or broad cauterization.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him whose body goes to the sickbed, it is necessary to give a moist drink of pomegranate juice; if he is overheated, he should draw blood three or four times, and if he has a cold complexion, he should take before the sickness a moist drink of syrup made from mused grapes, or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a very fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints at the sickbed, after drawing much blood, it is necessary that he inhale a brew of charcoal and subtle fragrant syrup, and use other things as we have mentioned in the section or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to extend his arm and heal it later, as necessary, when it is weakened by much healing, he should pull and release it little by little, according to the amount of its continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to extend his arm after the first healing, and he has strong stiffness, he should heal it seven hours after the first healing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to heal from another side, he should heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood in the body, which has already been heated and causes fever; so it needs to be drawn out in large quantity, and the wound widened as much as possible until it is filled with pus; then you must consider all the conditions of health, and place your hand on his pulse when he is healthy, that death does not come in its place, and this happens often when the healers are negligent; and it is not right when you release the arm and make blood flow out again, and the wound closes, pressing hard on it; nor should it be if it is bent, that he extends his arm reluctantly, for that would be bad; but leave it until it heals a second time; or you pierce its tip with a flame, until the blood frozen in the vein comes out, and put a little string dipped in water, pressing lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not squeeze it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it becomes necessary to drain the blood again due to the abscess, either in the same place or in another vein or arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthier in place of the vein in the head because it is composed differently.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the vein is that the patient holds his hand in hot water until the veins are red; then tie it moderately so that the vein appears well, and now go through it from side to side, not too wide or too long; and make the incisions large, and drain close to the joint of the hand, and if the blood does not stop, put the hand back into hot water and let the blood flow in the water until you have enough; and if this is the case, do not remove the hand from the hot water because it is put under more heat than necessary; and this vein is healthier than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The healer of the salvation of the right hand is worth against all soft illnesses: tighten the hand and immerse it in hot water until the vein is engorged if you see it; then cross the healthy across, and press it with all might throughout, without causing pain; nor should you be too forceful, for the nerve is completely bare of flesh, and then return the hand to hot water, so that if it is frozen in the wound, it cannot escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as best you can, then place oil and silk on the vein to bind it tightly, and so do for each person.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healthy person holds the mouse with their left hand if it has a disease of the eye, and does everything as I have told you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sage of the soul holds sway over all illnesses affecting the body, such as illnesses of the eyes, and retention of flowers (possibly referring to a condition related to plant or petal-like growths), and diseases of the kidneys, feet, and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of his health is such that the patient should immerse themselves in hot water, rub the vein until it ruptures, and bind over the joint with a bandage; the vein should be at the ankle, and above the foot they apply much pressure; thus, if there is a large or small wound, or at the ankle, that is where treatment should begin.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you place the splint on the foot, be careful of the nails that are underneath, and the splint should also pass through as if it were cutting; and the fire will become lessened.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the splint cannot be removed, place the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the splints need to be replaced the first time, then do so again slightly above, because the joints are stiff; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same thing for the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein's lion is at the ankle's fire, and its healing brings pain to the lower back when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its healing is such that the patient should bathe and stretch it three times from the ankle, otherwise the vein will not open; and if it does open, then heal it in all ways you can, gently and thoroughly, for the lion (presumably a metaphor for the injury) is safe, and it is much relieved by manual treatment.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you cannot stretch it, let the healing blood flow from the opening on the back of the foot towards the little toe, and be careful not to squeeze it; make sure the blood flows freely, then loosen the bandage, place cotton on it, and re-bind it; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	From the medical treatments of the vacuum (sauce/suction).
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Vacuum devices are made of horns, iron, or glass; and suction is performed in two ways: either by pricking and attracting blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	This suction, performed without pricking, is also done in two ways: either with heat or without heat; and the suction performed by pricking and drawing blood is done in twelve parts of the body, one over the forehead, others between the collarbone, on both sides of the collarbone, under the chin, on both shoulders, on both legs, on both ankles, and on both feet. Suction does not treat blood clots, only small veins scattered throughout the skin, and should not be performed with heat or without heat in any condition caused by excess, until all parts of the body are drained.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if, through necessity or habit, it is necessary to vomit, we should do so each hour at the beginning and end of the month, and at every time in between; for there are those who, when they need to vomit, have a heavy head; and others who experience fullness and redness in their face, and on their head and neck, and darkness as well. And there are those who spit blood in their mouths, and have a swollen tongue, and feel pain; and some see or think they see blood and become nauseous, die, or experience similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we order vomiting after three hours during the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The physician of the muscle finds aid in the great heat of the head ... which comes from the dislocation, and it does not suit that this be after the evacuation of all the body; and this treatment is for the muscle of the skull, and it does not suit those of cold complexion or who have scabs, for they do much harm to them; and therefore the elderly should not use it, nor those whose heads are subject to cold illnesses.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who recovers from it often becomes oblivious, and for this reason, the cup should be placed a little lower down in doubt of its oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation of the chest should be in favor of health, with an open nose and mouth, and for this reason it is beneficial to constrict the breath deeply, and to clear the passageway of the windpipe, and often, and completely; but one must not force it too strongly, as it may cause discomfort or even harm to the stomach and body.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilation through the ribs of the chest, if not properly managed, can cause neck pain, eye strain, headaches, constriction, and pain in the roots of the teeth, obstructing the health of the sinuses; therefore, it is necessary for you to instruct the patient to gently press his hand against his nose without blocking the artery, preventing complications with blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The breathing through the nose is beneficial for mouth illnesses, and the corruption of gums, and similar ailments in the mouth, and it is suitable for the healing of both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Breathing through the shoulders is beneficial for illnesses that arise from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Breathing through the sides is as beneficial as three veins in the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to breathe too strongly, for the lungs are empty of blood, and know how to drain and control the arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The vacuum that is on the back is as effective as bloodletting from the depths, and for diseases below, and it is necessary that the vacuum be large, and of iron, so that it has to draw well; and by chance, if it is too delicate, it will break; and it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg vacuums should be applied tightly as they draw blood from the entire body, and they are as effective as ancient pains in the kidneys, and in inflammation, and in the bladder, and they disperse the humors; and they are located in the two shoulders, and in the two ankles, but after long use, they weaken the body and cause various ailments.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying a vacuum is such that you apply it first while empty, sucking temperately, pressing firmly and moving it equally, ceasing only when you see the skin turn red and swollen, opening the pores of the blood; then place the cups again, taking care in the positioning of the skin, for there are some with thick, others with thin skin: it is enough to strike once, making wide cuts and rather deep ones; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is deep, it needs to be struck twice: first to open the way for the thick blood flow.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the pain is very sharp, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw out blood little by little, we suffice with only one blow.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we must often apply pressure; and if the pain is sharp, the striking must be deep and sudden, especially for those with thick and hard skin, and who have scaly wounds, one should use leeches with oil that stimulates and dissolves: such as violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and for ivy wounds, watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or other similar ones.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amaranth oil, or balm oil, or hemp oil, or similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one has a strong and wide wound, it is not necessary to put oil on it, but rather after cleansing with rosewater, or cold water, or myrtle water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or any similar liquid.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with much moisture should rise from it using myrtle water, sumac water, and similar substances.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excess fluid should rise from old wine, or lemon water, or decoction of nettle or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not advisable to use a cupping glass before a bath or after a bath, but an hour or two afterward; and they must not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary for them to bathe when they should be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And let those who have a fever be careful not to overheat or inflame themselves; it is advisable for them to apply cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, lettuce and similar foods; and eat little, and drink chestnut juice, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, should sip syrup of honey, and half-sweet wine, which is neither too old nor too new, and eat little, and small flies and birds; and on the day that he takes a bath, he must drink more than he eats; and it is right to give any man, at times, triacle or mace before or after bathing, to strengthen the principal members; but it is unwise for those who are hot to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.
