The cups that are applied without causing harm are those placed on the liver, and the spleen, and podagra, and the belly and bowels and joints and spine, for these members do not tolerate being hurt under any circumstances, and they are only done so to draw blood from one member to another, as we apply them to the mammary glands when nursing; to remove the adhesiveness in a member, as we do with cups on the stomach and bowels to reduce the member; and to alleviate pain, when there is oppression or a stone, it may perhaps draw away the oppression or leave the stone in its place; and thus it acts when applied to the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these cups are left empty to suck up only; and they should never be heated with fire, nor filled with cold water as in cases of painful tears; rather, one should fill the cup with hot water infused with suitable herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cup (ventose) administered by fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It should have two parts as wide as a half palm, and on one side, near the center, it should have a small hole, large enough to fit an needle, and be made of metal, gently curved so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the body; and in its center there should be a crossbar made of metal, either iron or steel, for holding a cloth with which to apply pressure, and their sizes should vary according to age and health of those who use them; for the cups for children are different from those for adults, and for thin people they are smaller than for fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus, one should place this suction cup over the affected member: take the wax or linen cloth and place it inside the cup across the stick that is in the cup, ensuring the clarity at the bottom of the cup so it does not burn the patient; then place it on the member, and your fingers should be on the openings we have mentioned, so when you wish to, the vapor goes away, and you remove the cup; and take up the linen cloth as before, and repeat often, if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the case of the suction cup used for treating pleurisy, a condition of severe pain and fluid accumulation, it has no stick or opening, and is only effective when completely filled with water, and should be placed on the affected member only briefly. This is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without wounds that are not amenable to cupping for their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and in cases where the skin is stripped of hair, like on the face, or neck, or other similar places; and if the quality of the wound is such that when you discover wounds that are in fresh, clean water without putrefaction, take them and place them in fresh water until they become calloused and have nothing in their bellies; then cleanse with vein and cupping, then rub the member until it turns red, and apply the cups; and when they are painful and chafed, if it is a wound that can be cupped, then apply the cups, for this is beneficial afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If he cannot raise the lion from its resting place, and then with water, it improves, and you expect; but if the bones are too soon healed after the body of the wound, and a cloth dipped in cold water is placed on them, and left until they are dried; and if the wounds multiply, vitriol or gall, and similar things, are applied until they are dried; or you place half dried peeled beans on it, and leave them until they adhere to the lion, it will be dry now; and if you need more, take other wounds.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not want to be taken, rub the lion with fresh blood, or insert an needle into the wound until it bleeds, then apply them, and soon as they smell the blood, they will adhere; and when you see that they are pulling, sprinkle a little aloe and silk powder, or ash, and they will stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	We begin the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear reader, that the curious minds of this chapter are such that they have never been seen in any of the ancient books, nor have their letters ever been read; and for this reason, the science is strange to our land, because I never found a single good one, and I know nothing about it, except through the knowledge of ancient books, on which I have studied so much that I have mastered the science; and through experience, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and abridged it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in this prologue of this book the principles of speech and the chapters where the wise ones apply their understanding, staying on the truth, so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, or twist, or any similar injury occurs, it is necessary to hurry to heal the patient on both sides. If nothing helps, such as weakness of the body, illness, or old age; or if the condition is very severe, or too cold, and you use cold things like ice, and do not consume wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill the veins with excessive meat, until there is no doubt about abscess formation or material expansion in the member; then the patient returns to his previous state as he used to be.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that we alleviate the patient from foods that cause excessive belching, or have a viscous consistency, such as cooked flour in water, and rice, and peas, and veal, and offal, and fish, and fresh meat, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For excessive belching prevents the bone from healing properly, as it re-opens the fracture more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that bones broken in the elderly and decrepit cannot heal or fuse well according to their nature because of the stiffness of the members, nor can those that are too soft, such as the bones of small children; but take no heed, hold fast to the broken bone with large pliers, so that it reattaches and joins the member together, as much as it did before; and do not remove it entirely from its work, for this reason it is necessary to consume large quantities of rich foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manners of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	Because there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another when sharpening, just like the blade of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and the fracture is at a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each type of dislocation has its own mechanism and specific means of restoration, according to the memory that is in its place; and the fracture of a bone is known because its joint is twisted, widely opened by pressure from outside, and sounds when pressed with the hand; but when there is no twisting or pain or sensation for the patient, there is no fracture, but it can have curvature, or a crack, or a small dislocation.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it with the hand, but apply remedies that will come hereafter, and then gently tighten it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes up in the air, and the two parts are disjointed, it is now necessary to put them back together evenly so that abscesses form below; and if hot abscesses come, let them remain there for a while until they calm down; then place them back evenly, so that you can gently and skillfully move them, and know that the restoration of the bone is easier than the restoration of that which has been broken in two; then hold it tight as needed.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if a bone is broken into two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or one of the small members, or at the tendons, or at a tendon and your hand, put the member back according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are in place, you can use all the tools to adjust them until they are firmly set; and be careful not to cause the patient any injury or pain with your work, and adjust the two halves of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And it feels good in the hand if it seems not to be well: if it is dressed nicely, and not pulled too much, nor pressed as those who cause hot abscesses and contractions in the member with their own work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is at its limit, gently reassure the patient so that they do not move it, neither awake nor asleep, nor turn it in any way; and be sure that the member is well-supported so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, and is not yet at its limit, it is necessary to put it in the right position so that it does not feel any pain; and be careful that it is correctly aligned, so that any twist does not return as it heals; and the quality of the damaged member will depend on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that broken members are diverse in size and shape and strength.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones; these should be wrapped in soft and thin linen cloth; and those that are large, like the thigh or leg: these should be wrapped in a wide and firm bandage, which embraces the whole member and tightens it equally from all sides, so that there is no movement; then gently tighten lighter bandages, three or four turns according to the member, and hold your hand slightly on the bandage; then go above the fracture and tighten less, allowing the fracture to move a little; and gradually soften the bandage bit by bit, until you press greatly upon the healthy part below; then take another bandage and wrap it around again from the top of the broken member; then return to the lower part of the fracture and tighten moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first chapter above; then place soft linen or cloth between the bandages, until they are all even, then tie everything above with a good strap, and put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is a swelling or abscess, apply a cold compress to the hot abscess that removes the swelling, and leave it for several days; then strain your veins, and make them half the width of a thin cane, sharp, or of wood used to make blades, or of palm leaves, according to this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the thread placed on the rupture be a little thicker and wider than the others; and also as long as it should be for the member, whether small or large; then strain the threads just as you did in the first layer on the rupture; tighter now, less later. And it is necessary that the thread be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; because if the thread is thick, like those people who make their bindings from twisted linen threads do, this is a great error, for the binding cannot be even if it is too delicate, and it does not suit that there be less space between each thread.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is troubled by the seeds of stars (possibly referring to splinters or foreign bodies) after dislocating their joints, he should place soft cloth or other bandages over them to prevent bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by breakage (of bones or tissue) and the heart is broken, I will describe its treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to extract all the stars (bones or splinters) from a member that is broken on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the member is large, it is not appropriate to put stars (bones or splinters) inside for more than 5 or 7 days, or according to your judgment of hot abscess coming; and here you see the ancient method of emplasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that clings to the walls of the mill, mix it with plenty of egg, and make this mixture neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of an emplaster restoring fractures in many positions, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too hard nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for repairing fractures, dislocations, and twists: take bear's fat, dani (resin), gum Arabic, myrrh, aloes, and mugat, each in equal parts; add an amount equivalent to X; add mirror and aloe in equal parts, and aubepine in an amount equal to V; mix with egg albumen; if the patient's body heat is high, use this plaster, as it is of good composition, and it will restore broken bones severely damaged, and it helps many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster for twists: take mugat and rhubarb, each in an amount equivalent to X; add myrrh and aloes, each in an amount equivalent to 9X; add akes (a type of herb) in a quantity of 6X; add Armenian bole in an amount of X, and grind well, mixing with vinegar or egg albumen, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of splinting joints and realigning bones out of their sockets, soothing the pain that comes with it, and using the bone for healing, as well as mending: take a new cloth, soak it in hot water and oil, and place it over the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cyst splints do not restore, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of splinting that restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves and terrestrial pawpaw leaves, grind them together, and make a paste.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plastering to restore the broken bone and thus lessen the remaining pain of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of wormwood, chamomile, violet flowers, and meal, each in equal parts; grind them and mix with wine, and apply to the affected members, which should be heated beforehand. Alternatively, mix with fresh coriander water or water alone and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of plastering when the abscess hardens during the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of chamomile, and seeds of linseed, fennel, melilot, and marshmallow, and violets and chamomile flowers, from all in equal parts; grind them and prepare a poultice with strong salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the warmth of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that one should not apply a hot compress to a broken member, but rather a certain type of compress made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be neither too hot nor too cold.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen states that one should apply warm, dry things to a broken member to restore it, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plastering that is effective for injury and pain: take moss and horse hair from shorn sheep, or feathers from an eye, or cloth, and cut them equally, and crush them, and make a paste and bind it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, afterwards, untie it a little and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor does the bone move from its place; if, however, pain comes instead or itching, restlessness, or swelling, hurry up and untie it, and remove the plaster immediately. Take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, dip it in water, and lift the skin until the itching stops and the pain is soothed; then let the limb rest for an hour, then place a dry cloth, dampened with water or rose oil, and bandage it tightly while you are certain of the heat. Rest the inflamed limb, and alleviate the pain, then begin again with a delicate application of plaster, a little at a time, and do not squeeze it too hard as before; apply it gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is closed, red, painful, and swollen, then you need to apply plaster and bind it again; just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if the limb does not recover after what we have said, do not release it before three or four or five or seven days; and never leave a fracture to heal for twenty days, as you see fit, until the joint is set correctly; then restrict it more than before and thicken the tissue as I mentioned previously. And if you see that the limb is drying out more than necessary, know that healing cannot take place. Then apply hot water compresses, every time you release it, once every three days, and loosen the bandage a little; by this means, you cut short the recovery of the limb, and do much harm, for what the ignorant do, they twist the member out of its natural position; it is harmful and very dangerous, and I see nothing else but to leave it alone and correct it.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of fracture, each with distinct forms and causes; for some fractures are caused by the impact of a sword, and the point pierces through the bone entirely, severing it as if cut with a hatchet or axe; this type of fracture is therefore called "hatchet-like.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or, the sword may cut through the bone without piercing it, and this is called "absolute" fracture; and the wound from these two types of fractures can be either large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a pounding, or a fracture, or a cut from a stone, or a blow against a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent fracture, which approaches the bone tissue that is beneath or on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is healed in the bone is as subtle as a hair, and the fracture is small, it is called a "capillary" fracture; and if the wound is caused by striking with a stone or a blow from a tool or similar things, and the piece of bone enters inside, and the edges are jagged like a blacksmith's work on a furnace, then between the bone and the object.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often with those who have moist heads, such as an infant's head; and it occurs in all these ways of breaking that smaller fragments are dislocated as if they were. And I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the ways of breaking through withdrawal from them, and inquiry at close range, and by corrupt flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is perceived when the bone is discovered and rubbed further, opening the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be cautious of accidents with the patient, and if you notice any ill effects such as vomiting, loss of consciousness, extension or bending of the limb, paleness, fever, sudden warmth, redness, or other similar symptoms in various combinations, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any dangerous accidents and hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fever comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon's cycle while it is still fresh.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this happens, if you hurry to remove the bone on the seventh day, when the tissue surrounding the bone is decomposed, then come the complications that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone breaks down to the tissue covering the brain, it is necessary that you split the broken part in this way: press the patient's head with great pain, and expose the bone in all ways possible, and carefully uncover the wound before the pus has formed, or an abscess at the base of the bone, and if there is any doubt about treatment, or infection appears upon exposing the bone, then you should fill the cavity with moist oil-soaked rags, and keep the wound at rest until the abscesses are calmed down, and be assured of the absence of infection. Then, begin to remove the bone according to two methods: one is by making a very narrow cut in front, and this is its form...
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then take another treatment even more powerful than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have many different sizes of tools, some with pointed and others with wide ends, all made of hard iron; and use them gently so as not to damage the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, it is necessary that you drill around it, using tools with carefully measured gaps, so that they do not penetrate beyond the soft part of the bone; each tool should have a margin or curve at its tip to prevent it from going through the bone. You will need several types of tools, so that each one reaches the appropriate depth for the thickness of the bone, making them useful for all parts; and this is the form of the three types of tools:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to understand around the broken bone is that you apply pressure on it and let it rest in your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then move the pressure elsewhere a little later, doing this all around, then cut with incisions the space between the cracks of the bone, and do so as delicately as possible, gently while still holding the bone in your hand or using any instrument like pliers or tweezers; be careful not to touch the brain or the soft tissue.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And once you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you observe the remaining tightness of the bone compared to any other cutting instrument, but it should be more tenuous and delicate than the others; if it holds onto smaller bones or scales, gently remove them with the appropriate instruments; then dress the wound with bandages and remedies as we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that which Galen describes, which is safer; it involves applying a poultice very strongly, and this is what he says.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you expose a part of the bone, either where it is broken open or clearly visible, and when you have exposed this part, place the flat edge of this lens-shaped scalpel beneath it. This is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, but expose the sharp edge on the other side, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then gently tap with a small mallet all around the bone, taking care to protect the soft tissue beneath; if it is detached from the bone, gently pull it away, for it can be done without much harm or pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not reach down to the flesh, and the bone is only broken on top, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to smooth out these asperities and shave off the scales with a fine rasp, of which you should have various quantities, to soften each part according to the severity and form of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you encounter great difficulties and then even more subtle ones, do not cease from this task until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and subtle breaks, it is necessary to soften according to their location; and this is something that cannot be fully explained to someone who has dedicated their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the wound is exposed and needs to be bandaged, it is necessary that you cover it with a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three layers, moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; do this as lightly as possible so as not to burden the wound. Then administer another bandage, without tightening it too much until the wound is only covered; leave it like that for a day or two, until the abscess has calmed down, then unbind it, and apply medicines such as licorice roots, flour of times (a type of grain), incense powder, aromatic herbs, and similar things. Make a powder from these substances and sprinkle it on the wound, and administer foreign remedies without any bite; and ensure that the wound remains clean, do not leave behind any dressing or allow the bandages to become too tight, because when bowing gathers around the skin of the head, it will corrode and break, causing great harm to the patient, for when a mordant substance is placed on the syph (wound), it becomes infected.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness comes not from the medicine applied, and its virtue is in question, it is then necessary that you mix a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and add a cloth, and place it on the wound; then cure it in the manner of cures suitable until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that the two parts of the bone above are never broken, either entirely or partially, for they are two bones; and the inner one is cartilage, which does not break, but only bends or twists, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should insert your little finger or a thin tool between the joints, and put the break back in place gently, until the joint returns to its natural position; do this carefully, so that the patient does not feel pain from your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the joint and the fingers cannot be moved to reset it, you should put a slightly thick stick at the top of the joint to realign it.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in both parts, repeat the same process, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if possible; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, then insert thin linen strips at the top of the joint, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or turn to another part, if it is broken; and make the bandages so thick that they fill the openings in the wound.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that no healing occurs when the bandages are not moistened with butter, and they must be changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think this is good, but it is necessary that they be moistened with a mixture of egg and mill powder; then leave the bandages, until the bones are healed and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never should one insert new feathers from an goose into a wound other than in places suitable, and if it irritates the suffering patient, holds the break, and blows air among them; or do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses form in the wound while you are treating it, apply a plaster or wet cotton wool soaked in rose oil or a poultice of dill seed.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no abscess forms, apply an external plaster of flour of millet, and incense powder, confited with egg albumen, then place light poultices without binding the wound; and if the rupture in the wound is small, and it is broken into tiny pieces, extract them with suitable instruments, then clean the opening with hot things, and treat it as a wound with appropriate bandages and applications of oil, and if there is no injury inside the wound, cure it externally with moist compresses until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the dislocation of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is dislocated and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only slightly out of place, and it is not broken into two pieces, but only displaced inward, then if you gently recognize it, it can be set back in place.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right side, you should insert your index finger of the left hand into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left mandible, insert your index finger of the right hand, gently pushing the fracture inward, and pull it outward with the other hand, making it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is severe in two parts, it is necessary that you administer an extension of the second part, as long as it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth occurs, or rupture, by applying strain with a gold or silver thread or silk, then place cerate on the broken jaw and cover it with a double cloth; and place the cloth on the tooth an iron well-made star or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and bind it firmly to the teeth, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes on the third day, then re-adjust what has changed and apply plaster to it; use fine powder ground with egg or flour of sesame after removing the cerate; place a thin layer of plaster, and if the plaster hardens and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it is healed; often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess appears, then administer what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both a fracture and a wound together, do not remove any part of the bone that is broken; it is necessary to use suitable instruments for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is tight, stretch it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and it does not delay, close the wound if it is wide, and apply suitable plugs to it, to draw out pus, as long as it is healthy.
de la forcele	from the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break many times, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways: it is broken and separated into two parts, with fragments, and is easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with an accompanying wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And for the tasks when the fracture is without a wound, you will need two assistants: one to hold the aid that is broken; and the other to stretch the collar towards the affected part; then place the fracture evenly in both hands, so that the shape is as it should be, with no appearance of movement or shift.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch it further, place a round spear of cloth, or wool, beneath the shoulder of the patient, as thick as needed; then gently pull, holding the spear with your hand, until the dislocation is even, as required.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the dislocation away from the bone because it is stuck completely, then the patient should lie on their side with their shoulder supported, and have a helper press the shoulder downwards until the bone in the dislocation is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then grasp the dislocation with your fingers, and if it feels loose, gently pull; but if the bone cannot be moved, despite using one of the incisions you made, place a supporting tool under the dislocation to prevent further damage.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it should look like a spoon, and is not too narrow, and is as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and it has two parts, as you see, one broader and the other thinner, just like the wound's rupture that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of the hot abscess, if you cut the wound too deeply, then doubt the hot abscess, and use cloth and bandages to cover the wound according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses appear, then moisten the cloth with rose oil and silk and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The splinting of the bone, when it is sensitive to touch or has been broken, consists of placing a paste made from fine powder and egg albumen on the bone, covering it with light bandages, and inserting a stick under the joint if necessary; then take a very wide bandage, place a double cloth over the bandage and splint, and wrap the narrow, long strip around it so that the end of the bandage hangs down; place the narrow strip across the fracture, and reapply the bandage to the healthy shoulder and the injured one, adjusting each part carefully. And when you see that the splint holds firmly on the broken bone, and clearly see that the narrow strip does not move over the broken bone, tighten it each day and, as the ligaments loosen, secure it with a small pillow under the arm; do this for up to 20 days. Then restart the splinting if needed, tighten it, and leave it in place until healing is complete; it usually takes around 28 days for healing, or less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder is dislocated far from its place and does not stay put except through touch; if, according to the shape of the dislocation, it is reset in its natural position in every way possible, then sprinkle a little fine powder over it, apply light bandages, and cover with a double cloth. Then place a wide and thin stele (plate) just larger than the shoulder, so that the edges of the stele rest against different parts of the shoulder; if you use strips of linen for this, make sure the stele is cut evenly. And then tighten it firmly with a great bandage so that the stele does not move from its place, and check it every day. Whenever it loosens, tighten it again, and put the stele back in place if it has moved out of its spot; lay the patient on their side. The shoulder is usually restored within 20 or 25 days, and when this number of days is reached, take off the bandage with caution, for it is not a bone that can be easily reset.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out and is not removed from the inside, it causes inflammation and pain in the abscess, so do as we have said to calm the heat of the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from the break of the worst abscess
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is never broken in the middle, but that happens rarely; it often breaks at the extreme end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken at the end, it retracts inside and causes the patient great pain, and there is no strength left, and sometimes it bleeds, and opens up the wound in the broken bone, and feels better.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their side, and places a cushion between their shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and aligns the ribs of the two sides with their hands, and adjusts it delicately in all ways so that the bone figure is as it should be; then apply plasters and bandages over the gentle salt or other light splint, and wrap it in a cloth, securing it to the broken bone so that it does not move; and return the ligament to its natural position on the back, and tighten it properly, checking the freedom every hour, and if it becomes soft, tighten it; and if it needs to be loosened, due to decay or itching that occurs in the place, or pain or abscess, do not delay, and loosen it, remove the plaster, and address what has come of the curative ways; then apply the plaster again, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	from the breakage of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You know that the breakage of ribs occurs only in the upper part of the back, and at the top, and they do not bend except because they are brittle; and anyone can feel it through inquiry as needed.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you put it back in place as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, gripping it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs leans inward, the patient feels great pain and piercing, as if from crying out, because the bone pierces through the flesh; it weakens the hands, and sometimes causes the patient to cough, vomit, and experience severe bleeding, which is a great illness, and old physicians have put much effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And for those who say that it is appropriate to administer foods that cause bloating in the stomach to push the fracture out.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not claim that incisions in hot wounds will not come, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes back, then the patient is healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that none of you should place suction cups on the body to draw out fluids, as it seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the suction cup might attract excess fluids to the joint due to weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that none of you should cover the joint with moist wool in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to evenly distribute the heat around it, then treat the cure for pleurisy, flesh, and with medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear through the bone where the wound is, then doubt comes to the patient, and it is necessary to make an incision above the broken rib, and put a instrument inside to achieve relief; and then one must break the bone, pull gently, and stitch the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses appear, place moistened oil-soaked rags on them and apply heat; treat the affected area while it is hot, keeping the patient lying down on their side where the abscess is, until they heal.
de la brisure dou col	From the rupture of the collarbone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Ruptures of the collarbone bone do not occur alone, and it often happens when it rains; also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover, pay attention if you see their hands becoming soft, swollen, and numb, and they cannot move or stretch them, and if you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Knowing that it is deadly in many ways, and if they are mute and feel well when squeezed and not at all, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and the patient will be cured, if proper treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens in the back, you must know if it is healthy or not, by observing if the muscles are relaxed, and if there are any signs of illness, and on the back, sudden excretion and evacuation without will; and when it is remembered lying on the belly, it suddenly evacuates without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is remembered lying on its back and wants to move, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Knowing that it is fatal: therefore, do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not occur, then the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is as follows: if there is a hot abscess, apply rose or egg oil to it until it is soothed; then put on a comforting and drying plaster and bandage it, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is separated, it should be covered; then the bone is removed, and the two edges of the wound, if large, are sewed together with a stitch, then dressed with healing ointment in a warm compress, until it is healed; and if the piece of bone that is broken off, called the "fragment of the cow," is still in your hand, you place it equally in your other hand, then apply the plaster and bandage as needed; then tighten it, and if there are any more bones out of place, do as before, remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	from the fracture of the bone in the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the bone in the hip is fractured, and there is no slight reduction in size at the site, it causes the patient great pain, swelling, and inflammation at the place of the fracture.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as long as you are above the fracture; and know what the fracture is and its form; and if the fracture is only at the top, then equalize this fracture, as long as it retains its natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, it inclines inward, then make the patient lie on his stomach until the restoration of this fracture appears.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And once you have made it even, place a splint on it, then put a wooden or iron rod across it and tighten the fracture so that it does not move, and apply heat to the affected area until the bones are aligned.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess appears and is not touched, until the abscess is calm, apply what we have said before; then return to the restoration, gripping it as necessary, unless there is some adverse event; this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	dislocation of the joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The joint (ajutoire) is that which is between the shoulder blade and the top of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, one must restore it according to one of the two methods: one is to take a thick, medium-sized stick, following this form...
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And he should hold the two feet, and bend them upward, and watch the patient on one side; then he throws his broken arm over the leg until it becomes relaxed, and places in it a splint of wood, and bends it to any heavy object that the healer holds beneath; then he adjusts the binding equally to both hands together, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is that one should place the patient on his back, and bind his hands to his neck, then command the assistants that one holds what is above the break in the hand, and the other holds below at every joint, and extends each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then tighten it slightly from around the fracture, and on the fracture, and stretch each of the assistants to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the top of the shoulder, it is necessary to put a medium tie from under the acromion and another towards the neck, under the fracture; and if the fracture is on the side of the neck, it is necessary to put a light tie without effort, as long as the fracture remains level on the bone, then set the fracture correctly and tighten it, without complications.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess forms again after it has been extracted, do not put any pressure on it for seven days; then apply a warm, moist cloth and olive oil to soothe the abscess; later, pull it out, and the manner of pulling is such that you place a splint over the dislocation, then reassemble the limb above the joint, and place your hand on the shoulder or breast; then cover with a bandage and pull again on the limb and the arm, so that the arm remains still, unless something prevents it or the bone does not move.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.
