If you doubt whether the bone moves, use splints and place a wider and stronger splint over the dislocation, maintaining two spaces between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it extends three times beyond the break on both sides; then pull on the splints as I have said at the beginning of this chapter about pulling on the dislocation, with increasing force and gradually widening them.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the stars, and the dislocation, as we have said, when you return the broken member, and you doubt the heat of the abscess, leave it attached for up to seven days, as we have said; then examine the wound every three days to ensure there is no swelling or pain, so that healing can come to the limb.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident occurs, do not release it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; place a soft cushion under the dislocated limb, equal in thickness, and check every hour during the day or night to ensure the limb does not move or the ligament becomes loose. If it heals by the power of medicine and the diet we have previously described, in such a way that the food is first made subtle, then when it begins to improve, it will be great.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the joint and the leg should be re-taken every forty days; and then one must loosen and administer baths and remedies with ointments to correct the position.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the contraction is severe and swollen, it may take longer to loosen, sometimes days or even months.
de la brisure du bras	of the dislocation of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, called the "fosse" (cavity), of which one is smaller and supports the wrist; and the other is larger, situated below the smaller bone, towards the hand. Sometimes only the larger bone breaks, or sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration and healing is light; but when the large ones are broken, the healing is poor and more difficult than when they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bones are broken, it is sufficient to extend them slightly and make them even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, it is necessary to pull harder; place the patient on his side with a pillow under the armpit, and the small bones should be lower than the others, and the patient should be crossed over himself, and a pillow placed in front of him higher than the pain allows. Then extend the assistants' arms to the part below their hand, or to the joint, and another assistant above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set it even with the eyes, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture each piece is set in its place, and if there is none that holds the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then doing as we have said above, on both sides of the bone.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is an open wound, I have spoken of it in the specific chapter; then take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of restoration there are abscesses, then I apply a bandage made of oil-soaked lint and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and I wrap it gently over the abscess until it is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the poultice, and apply the plaster of the softest powder with plenty of egg, then place the needles, making the needle from the break even stronger, and a little wider than the others; know that there should be six needles or more on the arm in different positions: whether the break is in one bone or two; tighten above the break more than elsewhere, and always less distant, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and make the cloth covering the break soft and moist, and not too hard or rough; and let the thread, from which it is bound, be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after no days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if no adverse event comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you should soak the limb in hot water until the itching is soothed; and allow the limb to rest without compression.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then repeat the exercise, and if the ligaments become slack and the bones lose their alignment, or any similar thing, address it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the tightness prevents any movement in the limb, because it is too tight, then you should loosen it a little and leave it for some days until the stiffness improves, and then tighten it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then he should be released in twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If uncertain, tie the patient's hands to his chest, ensuring his collars are even, and guard against movement and digitation, and have him sleep on his back. Know that this dislocation is restored in thirty days or forty-five, or perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the dislocation of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that on the back of the hand and at the joints there are often small breaks, and it brings only pain many times over.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient cuts across the wound, and holds it straight in front of him equally; then he places his hand on a flat surface and extends the broken bones with his fingers, aligning them properly, as well as possible; and applies a plaster and compresses if an abscess does not form, then he wraps it with a piece of linen cloth according to the size.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is near the edge around the belly of the hand, he makes a small cloth cutout and instructs the patient to pull it towards his broken hand; then pulls with a long cloth, making the plug as large as the palm of the hand, and tightens it appropriately.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the edge, then you must place a stick across it and another underneath in the sole, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly all around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the bones.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs in neither of the bones of the hand, and it is dislocated, then place it evenly, as appropriate; tighten it with the sole, and if you see that it needs a small, straight stick to keep it from moving, do so, and if the fracture is in other fingers, like the index or any other, place it evenly and tie it to the healthy finger next to it; you can either hold them all at once, making sure they are aligned, or put a stick on it, as with the dislocated one; be careful in the restoration and positioning of the abscess high up, and support what comes near it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	from the broken hipbone
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The hipbone is often broken, and one can clearly see it when it turns to the front or back; its restoration is achieved by binding it tightly over the break, from above and below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their face, then each limb extends equally to both sides; this is when the break is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the hipbone, one should bind it towards the wrist, and the others below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, then the ligatures around the knee should be loosened, and the extension below; then place the splints, with both hands, equally according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and bind, so that no further damage occurs.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside, then return to your work and treatment; the binding should be done in the same way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap over the fracture a hard bandage doubled in two or three, and remove any excess, then turn the leg until the heel reaches the root of the toe, and thread a long thread between the shin and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end up above; then turn again on the leg and the shin the bandage, then put on the splint, and place a star on the bone of the leg; then use the eighth part of a soft cloth between the leg and the shin to achieve equal compression, then begin to tie three or four turns around the fracture; and as you go higher on the fracture, it becomes less tight; then take the two threads that you had threaded between the leg and the shin, and tie them with three stars that are above, then return to the bottom with the thread, until you reach below the foot; and tighten it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, so that nothing comes, no abscess or swelling, or any other thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, and the dislocation occurs, and you address what comes next, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that stick, if possible, one should pull them out; and if they cannot be pulled out, then it is necessary to break the joint, and draw it out forcibly; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never should the foot be broken in this way with a cast, as is done for the arm; nevertheless, the restoration thus made does not benefit the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the foot is restored in 7 to 10 days, or perhaps a little less or a little more, depending on the variety of complexes.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the alley of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	You know that in the alley of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, even if it is only a crack or a hole, it affects every wound, and without a wound, and everyone feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when you put each part back in its place as much as possible, and then apply a plaster, and attach a round stick if necessary, and tighten it appropriately, then follow all the arrangements that we have mentioned for other breaks, such as a hot poultice or anything similar; and apply to each case what is appropriate, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	from the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	You know that in the leg there are two bones, which are called "tibula" and "fibula"; and any fracture in the leg occurs as it does in the arm, and the treatment is identical to that of the arm; and all the challenges are the same. If both bones are broken together, the leg can move in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, they return to their original position.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain, and one can see it well; and the joint turns away.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension, but make it even, and tie the stars equally; however, it is necessary that the broken bone be ugly, and there are more pieces, so that the extension is smaller and lighter; and align according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of broad cloth that cover the leg from one side to the other, and extend them down the length of the leg from the knee to the ankle; then wrap two bands around it above and below, and tie them in the middle as well, and at this binding, the leg cannot lean to the right or left, and so it is good. And no one should administer anything along the length of the leg, and this should be of strong cloth, and they place the leg to prevent movement, and properly treat the fracture where there is an abscess or any other accident; and each day they move the leg to see if there is a pus or other complication, and cure it as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones of the foot can be fractured and the two small bones, and there is no treatment that applies in all cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If the bones of the foot are fractured and you see them pushed against each other, the patient will cry out in great pain on the affected foot as if they wanted to walk, so place your foot on their leg, raising the broken bones, then press until they return to their proper position; then apply a splint and bandages from above, and under the belly of the foot, a small wooden wedge with two holes, then fasten it to the foot properly, wrapped in cloth and other things as needed.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three or four days have passed, if you loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones even, either broken or discolored.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are no bones broken, but they are discolored, restore them as we said for the hand; then place a thin piece of wood along the length of the bone, a little wider, and put the table beneath it, with firm pressure; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, place a piece of wood over each one according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and tighten the table beneath the foot; and make sure the top edge of the table extends beyond the abdomen of the foot so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other injuries, as we have mentioned; and treat each case as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Regarding the fracture of the bone in the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If a woman's bone in her hand is fractured and the swelling subsides, then she should lean forward with her back supported. Next, fill the palm of the hand with cotton and pack it tightly; then raise the woman's arm and gently tap the back of the hand from time to time until the cotton reaches the joint. Once this happens, the bone will be healed. If she needs to urinate, remove the cotton, and after urinating, replace it. Do this for seven days or so. The fracture will then be restored. If necessary, use a bladder from a goat (berbis) and tie one end of a tube (cainne) to the opening of the bladder, then fill the bladder completely with the tube still attached. Blow into the tube until the bladder is inflated inside the hand; this will help heal the fracture. Then pack it again with cotton and leave it that way for several days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the arm or of the woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the hip bone; and these breaks are not hidden from one who puts his study and skill into it, and heeds my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For these breaks mean various dispositions for the right way of restoration: understand this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the staff is broken, take a goose throat and blow the staff; then wrap it with cloth around, and leave it for three days or longer, and it will be healed naturally.
de brisure avec plaie	from fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is important for someone with a fracture and a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone in the shin or shoulder or similar, to be treated immediately, so that the healing process, as we have described, can begin.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but there is still hardness from the bruise, if you have no other remedy, then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour or on the same day that the abscess appears.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscess opens on its own, let it heal undisturbed for a new day or two, until the abscess is calm, and do not touch it even on the third or fourth day, or you would bring about a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible beneath the skin, you must gently place your hands on it, with small extensions.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions do not appear even when placing your hands, take this instrument made of iron, with seven or eight fingers, or as long as necessary, and adjust its width according to the size of the wound; it is best to press gently, about three or four times, depending on what is needed for each break; and it should be rounded and slightly thicker at your discretion, so that it does not bend under pressure when working on the member, and wider in front, thicker in the middle towards the front.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", therefore the dislocated bone should be placed back on the visible head of the joint; and press it once, until it returns, and becomes equal one to another.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, you must hold the head of the bone until the instrument has a firm grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, with an appropriate instrument such as a chisel or a saw, within your power, then remove what is stuck in the bone from roughness and small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterward, knowing that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do your best to put it back in its natural place, then moisten the drape with astringent black wine, and arrange it properly; do not put any wax or other substance on the wound that could cause putrefaction and corruption. Then administer stars (medicinal herbs) when you have restored the bone, leaving the wound uncovered, and clean the covering around it according to the size of the wound, and be very careful that the wound is not constricted by the bandage; many times the foolish ones have done this, bringing death or corrosion to the patient. The tightness (of the bandage) should be gentler and more gentle than with other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is deep or great, and you doubt that a bad accident may come, as we have said, and you feel pain in place instead of finding relief when applying heat, then wrap it tightly with hard cloths, and secure them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is bowing or sinking, then remove what you have applied to it, and apply a healing dressing for wounds, such as a four-part ointment or similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it remains swollen and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be separated in such a way that the bow of the joint gently moves downwards.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if this persists for a long time, it cannot heal but repeatedly returns to the bowed state, knowing that there are small fragments of bone, so it is necessary that you clean the wound thoroughly and remove all these misplaced fragments causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula forms in its place or any other type of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it according to what is said in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when a bone is broken and open on the member, such as the bone of the leg or the shoulder, or other similar bones in large members, do not pull it, for often death results, but let it rot until it heals; perhaps after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; if not, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	burns that come from the solder
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of the burn, especially when it is near the joint, and the sight of the misalignment of the limb is a bad thing; and by chance, the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then, if we must administer astringent medicines such as aloe, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, so that you press any of these things, or all together, and preserve them with astringent wine or with abundant honey or with ash; and place them on the wound in bandages, tighten it well, and do not loosen it for many days; then loosen it and begin another one until the swellings are removed; or press a piece of well-made plasters, for the property of plaster is to remove all swelling from the limbs; and if the nodulation has already hardened like stone, it must be removed, cutting off the top, and making the surplusage apparent; or you can use a razor until it is removed, and cure it as long as it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the weak member after treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and the weak and delicate members remain, this can happen for many reasons: one is because it was bound too tightly and not properly secured as it should be; or because there are too many bindings and it cannot assume the normal movement of the member; or due to excessive swelling; or because of too great movements, not at the right time; or because it has little blood in its body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and tighten the body, until the blood flow multiplies within it; then administer a bath, give joy and comfort; then apply powder to the member, so that the powder draws out great movement, and often moisten the affected area with warm water, until the flow of blood reaches the member, and it returns to its natural state.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The twisted member after health.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When a member is twisted after healing, and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those who say one must break the limb all over again, and many foolish people have done this in our land; such actions are blameworthy, and cause great harm, and perhaps even death. However, if the contusions and tortures are fresh, then they should be treated with hot water or softened herbs, such as fennel leaves, roots, melilot, and similar things; and make a soothing application with something like dragon's blood well-prepared, or take the mucilaginous part of fennel and confit it with goose fat or oil of sesame, and apply as an ointment. Alternatively, you can use fig fats, crushed with colon powder and similar medications that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never should the dislocation be rubbed continuously and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow the limb to move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the stiffness becomes inflamed and hardened, like stone, it is necessary to dislocate with iron, if needed, covering up to the bone, with a delicate incisor lightly; and apply compression and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur from a joint moving out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs due to no apparent cause, it is necessary to attempt to bring the limb back to its normal position immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Because if treatment is delayed, the limb may swell, and upon resetting it, one might cause pain; therefore, it is inappropriate to move it at that hour when it is swollen: in many cases, it brings about spasms and other pains. However, once this has occurred, make the patient better, then leave it until the abscesses are calmed down; then apply hot water and oil, and gently reset the limb, treating each member as it comes to be cured in its own way.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder joint all the way to the foot.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It is often the case that the jaws become dislocated, and there are two types of dislocation: either they are slightly out of place, a bit bent, or entirely dislocated, hanging towards the chin, preventing the patient from holding their mouth shut, closing it, and even involving the tongue when speaking.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is minor, it often returns to its proper position through various dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is intact and complete, then you should reset it urgently, without delay; and in such a way that the practitioner places his thumb on the patient's chin, just below the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, so the dislocation is from two parts; and the other two fingers should be extended, to equalize; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he should equalize the pressure, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns to its place, especially if both jaws are involved, then apply hot water and oil, gently resetting it; do not delay in resetting it, as we have said before.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back even, and the patient's mouth is closed well without molesting it, place moistened bandages made of rose oil and wax on them, then gently bind them with soft cords; and let the patient sleep on his back, with his limbs between two pillows, so that he does not move to either side, nor makes any effort to open his jaw wider. But eat light food and drink until the pain is gone and the jaws are healed; and then begin eating as usual, without opening the mouth too widely when eating or drinking, until the jaw is completely healed and strong.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be brought back to their proper position within an hour and are not aligned properly, then fever and severe pain may occur, as well as abdominal distension, and possibly pure bile vomiting.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know it is a misfortune; and many die from it in nine days.
de la forcelle	De la forcelle" translates directly to "of the
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot stay in place from either side within the continuation of it and is dislocated neither outside nor inside, and it causes great pain.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And its restoration is that the patient lies on their back and extends their arms; then press the joint into your palm, and it will return; then apply the plaster and bind it tightly; and the limb that is dislocated towards the shoulder cannot stay in place; if not, and if it does not stay in place, then put it back in its place as we have said; then apply the plaster and bind it tightly, and command the patient to rest until they are healed; and thus the same happens with the shoulder dislocation when it is returned to its proper position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one when it is dislocated at the acromion end; and the second when it is dislocated at the soft part; and occasionally dislocated upwards, which happens rarely, and does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves; and most often dislocates downwards towards the acromion, especially in those with little muscle, because it easily dislocates there; to those with enough muscle, it slightly dislocates and returns slightly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And occasionally, no matter the person, they might experience a bruise or fracture, and an abscess of heat forms in the shoulder, and they think it is dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary that you test it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And dislocations are known when they tilt towards the joint, and it is necessary to distinguish between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their differences manifest; and you will find a hollow in the top of the shoulder when touched, as if it were one with it, and the patient cannot bring his hand back to its place, nor make any movement; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, unless it is hidden, because you will find it manifestly by touch; and this type of dislocation is not easily remedied when it is new or if the disease is in the shoulder.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the healer places his hand on top of the patient's sore spot, then places his palms below the joint, and pulls the joint firmly upwards towards the bone; and the healer releases his hand, extends it upwards, and puts it below; this will bring relief.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said above, then the patient must be bathed in hot water; and administer a soothing and softening ointment, such as an infusion of althae, fennel, and melilot in water, and apply it; then attend to the patient lying on his back, and place a piece of equal wool below the joint, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the heel of the foot on the wool and gently pull the top of the shoulder, while pulling the hand of the sore spot; and another healer should hold the head of the sore spot so that it does not move. This shoulder will return immediately, and you will see that it is reset in this way: and it is important that you have a man who is stronger than the patient; and he should be straight towards the side, and pull the shoulder away from below the joint of the sore spot, and pull the joint upwards so that the patient's arm hangs down; and another healer pulls the hand of the sore spot downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, and any heavy object causes no discomfort, then the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is also arranged in another way: take a long stick and insert it into the ground so that the end is as bright as a pistol, but not too thick or too thin; then place it from beneath the patient, ensuring that there are soft rags above, and the patient's limb is extended longitudinally; then extend the hand on the opposite side towards the ground, and the joint will return to its original place. If this does not make it come back for all the reasons we have mentioned, then perform this cure: take a stick of considerable length and width, which has a bright end so that it can enter fully beneath the skin along this form.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then place a heavy cloth over the affected area, so the pain does not afflict the patient, and lay the afflicted limb on a hard surface; extend the arm above the affected area, and tie the aid to the wrist, then put the arm on the edge of a wide knife, and let the hand hang down below, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will now be realigned.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is dislocated, in any way, it is necessary that you place under the limb a spear of equal wool, then apply the plaster made from powdered chalk, with incense and eagle's egg, over the entire shoulder area, then stretch the limb away from the body, and secure the bandage on the plaster, and press the hand to the collarbone, so that the hands remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he press lightly, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; and then press again after a few days or seven, and move it; and if it remains closed and is not softened, it will be healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is stuck due to moisture or any other cause, it is necessary that you apply heat at three points, as described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and after seven days the joint loosens and cannot raise its arm, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is either compressed, stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place again.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the worst, and the joints, or behind, if it occurs through a blow, and the extension of the hands, and is treated by another means; and heal as long as it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing comes cracking in the limb, and delayed movement; if the patient uses it often enough, as long as that cracking is relieved, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation cost
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	You know that the jointure that is dislocated is relieved at times, and it returns; but if it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not resolved, because one can see and feel it well; and it heals according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick part with the healthy, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is dislocated, and the arm cannot bend, nor can it touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you should reset it in such a way that the abscess closes and goes away, because if the abscess closes but does not go away, it will be difficult to reset it; especially when it is at the back, it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and may even lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be brought back, that you extend his hand with both of yours; and his arms are spread out, and the hands turned to the sides according to the cost around, from above and below, and bend the joint to his fingers together, or at the base of his palm, until he returns to his place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his palm, and turns the root of the palm side that is misaligned.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, apply a strong extension; and have the assistant extend the arm, and tie the two ends together, so that it does not move with the extension; then turn each part of the arm, after you have wrapped a double long and wide bandage around it; and when you see the joint at the hand, seal it with no oil to soften the joint, then bend the joint firmly, until it returns; and once it is in place, apply dry plaster with egg white, make it firm, stretch the arm towards the patient's chest, and leave it for several days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, repeat the plastering and binding, and leave it for several days until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if the patient feels stiffness after resetting the joint, and it becomes mute, bathe and gently rub it, pressing until it is relieved; or place a piece of fat sheep's wool on the joint, leave it for a day and night, then remove it, and give the patient a bath. And when he has sweat, massage the joint temperately, then put back the wool, and repeat this process twice or three times, until it is healed; and if you notice, use fine moist warm wax with butter, and strain it over the joint; it will return to its normal position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand joint moves slightly and its return to position is lighter than the other joints. Nevertheless, it needs to be carefully reduced immediately after dislocation so that the muscles do not swell or an abscess does not form near it.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the reduction is such that you place the patient's hand on a table, extend their fingers, and look to ensure they are straightened, so that the palm is facing upwards over the joint, and press until it returns. However, you should check if it is in its proper position; then, place the patient's hand with the back of their hand on a table for extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, let the patient lay his sick hand on a table, and look carefully at the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it comes back now, it is good; otherwise, if the strain of healing abscesses causes new ones, it leaves them so as not to recommence.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after any number of days, then the joint remains twisted; and neither hurts the patient more than the hand is bent, nor can anything be extracted: then know that a nerve or an artery is cut; otherwise, there is no other cause but to extract it carefully with cautery, and perhaps there is nothing else worth trying.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, if you put on the plaster as we have said, then pull it and leave it for a day, then loosen it and leave it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no fracture, then apply warm water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	on the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Under no circumstances should the fingers of the hand be dislocated at any joint, neither at the back of the palm nor on the palm itself; then pull the finger, and straighten the dislocation as much as possible, holding the tip with the other finger, and bend it towards the side where it is separated. Leave it for a day, and then repeat this process each day until it heals. Do not bind it, but rather loosen it each day, and make it move, and re-straighten it if necessary; and do this often, as much as needed, until it becomes tight, and follow the same procedure if it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	dislocation of the shoulder blade
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade or collarbone is dislocated and there is no cure, the patient faces a greater risk of death due to haste.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the limbs jump without volition, and the patient cannot hold them still; often, the joints become soft, especially in the hips, or both arms, or both legs, or sometimes even the shoulder blade moves to one side—this is called 'gypsie' (a term for a deformity). The cure, if there is any, is that if the gypsie has been present since birth, it may heal on its own; otherwise, there is no treatment or recovery.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from a fall or shocks or similar events, the ancient ways of treatment speak in great words, but they do not bring much benefit to all; but I have abridged it according to my understanding and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the stiffness that comes to the penis in front, no one has any health; and also that which comes directly in two sides, and it is only the cure outside of that which properly comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient should be extended on his face equally in the first position, and hold them tight from below so they do not bend; then I stick a stick into the head in the earth in a curved shape, and another at the stone, and tie a band around the affected parts of the patient, and another on the hips, and on the knees, and on the ankles; and these servants know the bands, one on the head and others on the feet, among the two sticks; and they should be well fastened, the stick as we have said, and the expert places his palms on the curved spine until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a table three feet long, cut a hole in the wall from behind, place the patient on their side, and turn the head of the table away from the wall; then place the middle part of the table over the spine, and put mirrors under both ends of the table, pressing firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see it moving, do it with a turn that turns towards your hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And take two long splints, one for the patient's head on the affected arm, and two others for their feet, with a space of about three finger lengths between each; and make in each splint a hole, or turn it correctly, and let them be firmly fixed so they do not move; and between these two splints, place one more turning splint, so that it turns, and attach to it two small splints one palm length long, for the purpose of turning; then tie the string which is among the bound parts of the turning splint towards the head, and the other string towards the feet to the other turning splint, and let each assistant turn their respective splint with all the strings; and the master should make the spine straight as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a drying plaster with plenty of heat, then the compresses, and then the end of a tablet three fingers long, which should adhere to the area of the stiffness and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and use remedies that soothe and soften for as long as it is healed; and if any thing happens at the end of healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, as we have mentioned above; and never should one apply a piece of cloth, nor does any appearance show up in the rear spine, making them believe it is dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, for which one must not be presumptuous; perhaps death would come.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the spine
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	You know that the joints of the neck and the joints of the shoulder only cause dislocations, unlike the other joints; and the joint of the neck is misaligned according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more inside, less misaligned in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is such that when you join the affected leg with the healthy one, the diseased knee extends further and opens wider than the healthy ones, and the patient cannot bend their kneecap; it is the muscles around the abscessed joint that are affected, because the bone in the thigh comes close.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who experiences this at death is that this event is contrary to what has been said before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who experiences this beforehand, are that his leg is weak according to its strength; nevertheless, do not bend the knee without pain, and if he wants to walk, he cannot do so before, and he retains urine, and the angre swells, and when he looks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who experiences this afterward, are that he cannot spread or bend his knee, and one leg is more twisted than the other, and the angre is softened, and the limb of the thigh is raised on the side of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	They reset this appearance of dislocation if it is such that you reward the dislocation being ancient, and it lingers according to its position, as there is no cure; nor should he have any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for those whose dislocation is fresh, and it's of the four types of dislocation, you must act quickly to reset the joint, both inside and outside, and align it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other cure is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	If it does not return in this way, you must then use a strong appliance, extending the leg firmly to two hands, or binding it above the knee; other ministers should extend their hands from above in such a way that they press his hands down onto his buttocks, then pull strongly on a tight ligature placed on the calf; others should hold the head with a ligature; and all should stretch up and down at once, until the patient is completely raised from the ground and remains still.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all three cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
