Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If the dislocation is recent, it is necessary to treat this condition. When the dislocated joint is hidden, it is advisable for the patient to lie on their healthy side, then tie the leg at the ankle, and the joint above the wound; then extend the ligament upwards towards the wound and downwards towards the strong part. Then ask another assistant to hold the patient's arms, and hug the large joint of the affected leg, extending it beyond its normal range; it should return to its place now; this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in the manner we have said, then you must bind both feet of the patient together with a strong, soft ligature on both heels and both knees; then let the affected leg be extended two fingers more than the other; then hang it from the top of a post, and let it be suspended above the ground by two long arms; then command the assistant to embrace the head of the thigh, and let another assistant be hanging with the patient, who embraces the thigh, for the joint now returns healthily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is outside, if the patient lies as we have said in the case of the stiff joint, then tighten the ligature properly on the affected leg and also on the other; then place two hot coals, one at the top and one at the bottom, and insert a hot coal between the cuisses near the dislocated joint; and surround it with moist cloths to prevent the patient from being hurt, then stretch each assistant towards him, and have them equally apply pressure to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it does not return, place it on a table and press it as we have said in the previous section, and lay the patient on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is on the front side, it is necessary to extend the affected leg forcibly, as I have said; and alleviate their pain of being on the sore joint, then press with the other hand, and stretch it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is on the back side, it is not necessary to stretch the affected leg downwards, but rather keep it as calm as possible, just like when the hip was dislocated in a previous section; and place it on its face, and extend the leg as we have said before, and press on the joint against the table; and it will be done when the patient extends their legs and they are even. Then tighten the bindings and apply a poultice, and tie up with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then remove the bindings and apply a poultice again; and gently move the leg until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The patient is dislocated in three ways: internally, externally, and behind; but not in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not give way at the knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place his face on your hand, and place his foot on yours. Then take the kneecap in your palms and pull between your fingers, then bend both sides of the kneecap forming a curve; and another assistant extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it gives way slightly at the knee. And apply the plaster, and raise the leg with the knee towards the chest, and tie it together firmly for three or four days, then release it; and do not let the patient move about, until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, apply firm extension as we have said in the treatment of the shoulder, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are neither completely dislocated nor fully aligned, and they are distorted both inwardly and outwardly.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tender to the touch in the area where it is dislocated; the reduction is gentle, and one should gently extend their hand towards their body when it is slightly dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when the dislocation is released from all its sources, it is necessary that you make the patient lie straight, and hold the leg with both hands above the ankle; then take the foot in your right hand, and twice in your left hand, then stretch it upward, and neatly bring the foot back up; and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, recommence the procedure, for it will return; and if it cannot be returned in such a way, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and insert a firm stick into the ground between his thighs, and wrap the blankets around him so he does not hurt himself; then have each minister hold the thigh, and others stretch the foot to its place or fasten it there, that it may be held when stretched; then put both hands equally over the dislocation, and another minister hold the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return more easily.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when the wound is at the right length, apply a poultice and compress it, and stretch the bandage around the leg, and secure the stirrups behind the ankle, ensuring the ligatures are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandages are loosened, remove them on the third day or the fourth.  And the patient must walk within three or four days; otherwise, the wound may still worsen.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses form, it is necessary to soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, while they are clean.
des dois	Of the two (parts/sides)
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both (sides) are dislocated, if they need to be realigned without effort, it is a light task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any new pain in the back or leg, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his side or on a table completely straight, and place your foot on what opens these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it returns; and when it is even and nothing opens, place a small table under the sole of the foot, then pull firmly, and release after three days, and make him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	From wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound occurs with dislocation and you wish to restore it, often the patient dies: if you are not cautious in its treatment, since you lack knowledge of this art and have not practiced it for long, nor are you compassionate and merciful and slow, do not be hasty; instead, at the beginning, use hot compresses on the abscess, and leave the patient in God's care, if you see no hope of recovery.  And when you see hope, now realign the limb to its proper position, so that the abscess heats it; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing hot applications to the abscess and treat the wound as appropriate, using dried herbs; and if, with dislocation, there are broken bones or small pieces of bone, reduce them and do what we have said about simple diseases; and be careful not to enter a path of fear, according to what I have said, for this will serve you well according to your Creator, and through the knowledge of your arms and body.
